another ete nor drink for dread of the dome that is com^n^. The sixth day all
great byldynges / castelles / towers steples and houses shall fall down and
brennetyl the sonnense again. The seventh day all stones and rockys shall bet^
to gyder that each shall break other with one horrible noise, the which shall
be herd into heven / The eight doye the earth shall quake so that there may no
man stand thereon but shall fall down / The ninth day ye* people shall goo
out of they re denmys / and goo as they were myndeles and nonespake to other /
The tenth day ^yles and earth shall be even and plain / The eleventh day / all
graves and tombs shall again and the bodies shall stond upon them / The twelfth
day / s^erres shall fall fro heven shetyng out brennyng bemes a dreadful sight
to see / The thuteenth day they shall deye that be^en by ^ / The fourteenth day
heven and earth shall brenne the fifteenth day heven and earth shall be made
new and all people shall rise in y^. age of thyrty winter / and come to the
dome. (Dominus venie^ adjudicium cummulti^^dine angel orum) Thenneshall come to
the dome our lord Jesue rystvery god and very man with his angellys and show
his wounds fresshe bledynge / as yt. day he deyed on ye. cross. with allye
instruments of his passion. The sper crown / seourges / nails / hamer
pyn^sons / and the garlande of thorns / to show what he suffrede in his
passion for mankind Then may they besory and ferde that have sworn by his
passion or wounds. or by o^^ membre of his body / that shall be a great
repress to them but they a mend them in this world / or they deye. Then will
our lord gretely thank them that have do mercy in this world for hyssake to
they reve^crysten / and will say thus to them (Venite benedicti patris mei
pe^cipite regnum^^^) Come ye my faders blessed children and recey^^ye the
kingdom of heven, that is ordained to you and someher^e so them the seven
wekes of mercy when I was hungry ye gaaf me mete (Sihvi^t ded is tismihi
bibere) when I was thursty ye gave me drink / and when I was herberles / ye
herbered me / and so for the all the works of mercy / For when ye gass any
thing in my name / it was to me / Then shalour lord rebuke the rych people /
that would not do for his love / nor sorgyve nootresspasse for his sake / And
said to them / ^iscedite a mem^ledieti in ignem eternum) Goo ye cursed people
into everlastyng peyn of hell / For when I was a hungered ye gave me no mete
etc / Than may they befull sorry and woo that ever our lord Jesue ryst shall
thus rebuke them. For there shall be no man of law to plete nor for gold nor
for sylver nor other yeftes to help. For than shall another master nor lord
ship help but all be set be side / butt right as a man has done so shall
he have.

And there shall be dyvers accusers both above him and byneth him And on
everyside above him shall be our lord Jesu Christ his domys man / (^rahisest
fur or domini in populo suo) without mercy to them that deed no mercy / and
so accuse them of the least thought that ever was amys. On the right side his
angel tellyng redely where when and how oste he did amys / On that other side
fendes challengyng him they res as by right for his wicked dedis. Under him
hell ready if he be found in sin that day they shall be peyned and in pain
wythoutenend that day poor people* shall sylle with eryst at the dome / and
deem the rich people for the great wrounges that they did to them. and they
might get none a men des tylle the day of dome then they shall have their
will of the rich people for when the rich done the poor wrong: they can
do no more but pray to god to quyte them at the day of dome. And so he will
for god says thus (Michi vindi clametego ^etrib^am) Put all to me / and^ yield
every man after his deservynge / therefore while yeben here make ye amends for
your wyckednes / And make them y^* friends that shall be your domys men at the
day of dome and trust not to them that shall come after you / lest ye be
begyled And dread the pain of of hell / that never shall have end.



Saint Bid tells how there was an housbonde man in England that fill syke /
and ley dedefram the evyn till on the morrow. Then ne he rose and departed his
gods in four parties and all his own part he gave to pour men / and went
and was a monk ^n an abbey that was nygh the water side. Into the which water
he went every night / were it never so cold and stood therein long / and
suffered great penance. And when he was asked why he did so to suffer that
great penance / He said to esche we a greter peyn that he had seen. And he
would ete but barley bread and drynk water all his life after. And told two
religyous men the peynes that he had seen and they were so great that they
cowde not tell them openly. He said that an angel ^ad him to a place there
yt* one side was so cold that no tongue might tell the pain thereof. And ye.
other side was so hot that no man might tell the pain thereof and souls were
cast out of that one into that other and that was a great pain to them. And
the angel showed him ye. fire that came out of hell that was sooho^ / And so
far as him thought he might see it / he thou ghtal bren^ him* and in the ^eme
thereof / hesawe souls boil up and down cryeng and waylyng for woo / Also he
herd fendes cry / cast out hole led and brymstone to make herpeynes gretter
/ and so they tormented the souls in pey^e

Now lord god for thy great mercy have mercy on us / and keep us ^ro thoo
peynes / and bring us to the bliss of heven / that never shall have endyng

Amen.
Dominica in septuagessima.
Good men and wymmen this day is called in holy church / ye sunday in
septuagesme / Forcause^^* holy church is mother of allerysten people / she
takes good head to the children as a good mode^ owes to do and ^orasmo^he as
she sees hem full sore syke in sin / and many of them wounded to ye. with
the swe^d of sin / the which synne^ has caught all this ye^^ to fore / And
namely this cr^stmas time yt. was ordained in holy dryrch for great solemn
p^^yte / for every man should be besy to serve god with all his power / because
that cr^ste himself she wed that day swetnes of love to all christian people /
For man he was borne yt. time / And in the same flessh and blood as one ^f us /
and laid in a cradell more pourly than any of us / and was crystened in water
as any of us. And also he come to a weddyng for to dense it from sin / and to
make us holy and bredern to him and heirs to ye. kingdom of heven. For this
causes all christian people owen to be full glad in their souls as my^. time
making solempnyte and myrthe and making hem both clean in body and soul from
all manner of sins And groundyng them in great sadness of love to god and to
all cryssten people doing great alms to them that have need: But now the more
harm is for that high and solemn pnefes^e is turned into f^llye. sin and
great sykenes to ye soul / as in pride by dyverse wise in clothing / and in
many dyverse gyle usyng / into great covetyse / and into ^echery* that sueth
always gloten ^^ In slewth in god is servyce / as ^apys and vanyte syngyngery
baudry spekyng For vanite causes much slow the for among such people / he is
most worthy yt most charlatry can speak. thus these solemn and high festes
yt. were ordained to great worship of god and of our lady and all the saints
in heven now ben turned into great offense to god / wherefore our mother holy
chircheseying her children in such dyspayre / as a mother full of compass
yons^r^ in her heart for them / this day leyeth down all^luia and other songs
of m^^the and melodye / and takes ^raclus / that been songs of morning / Also
for this holy sacrament of weddyng is much de^oyled by vanyte of sin /
therefore it is leyed do^n this days and in advente. For many that been now
wedded yeveth them all lust and liking of the bodies of fleshely lusle of
this world And thinks full little of the death yt. is full grevous that comes
too soon after. But as it is red by great clerks / it is more spefull to
monnes soul to god / to an house there as is a corpse and weeping / than to go
to an house / there as is a great revel and much myrthe for such things make a
man to foryete his god and himself both / but theras is a sight of a corse
makes a man to think on his death / that is ye specyal thing to put away
sin and vanyte of this world. For Solomon says thus to his son / ^ili
memorare novissima tua and ineternum non pec^^bis / Sone have in thy mind that
thou shall deye^^ thou shall never sin dedely / thus holy church havyng great
compassyon of her children ordeyneth three manner of salves to help and to hele
her children that been to think on death inwardly to labor besely and to
chastyse ye. body resonably the first as to think on death in wardly / holy
chircheyeveth en sample this day in ye office of ye mass Circumdederunt me The
sekenes of death has b^^typped me / this says he techyng every good child to
have in mind how hard he is bestad with death on each side in so much that he
man not seape no way. but eve^ death sueth him with abow drawn and and an
arrow eye^ therein ready to shote him he wot never what time / This is a
pryncypall salve to every man yt. takes it to her t^ to putt away all manner
ofvamyte and vain myrthe / But for to understand this the better I show this
by ensample.



I read of a king yt. ever was in hevy sorrow and he would never laughe ne make
merry ^here / but ever was in morning and in hevyness / therefore his mayny and
all other men were greved / there with they yede ^o ye. kings brode^ / prayng
him to speak to the king / ^ said he greved all thoo yt were about him with
his hevy chere / and counseled him to leve it and make ^yght chere in time
coming / Then was this king wise and thought to chastyse his brother by a
while / and wrothly bad him goo home and do that he had to do Then was the
manner of ye. country that when a man should be done to death / should come
trompetts and trompe before his gate. Then said the king byddyng them goo
trompe before his broders gate. and men goo with them to arreste him / and
bring him before the king / And in the mean while / the king called unto
him seven men that he tru^ on / and bad them that when his brother was come /
to draw her swerdes and set them at his breast before his heart.

So when his brother was come they did as the king bad hem. than the king
commanded all men to dance and to make revell all that they could and so they
dyden then said ye* king to his brother / why art thou so hevy of chere / heve
up thy head and be merry for all this myrthe is made for the / Then answered he
and said How should I be merry of chere and see here seven swerdes set to my
heart / and wot not who shall be my death first / Then said the king put up
your swerdis / and spoke to his brother thus. It fares by me yt seven dedly
sins be everredy to reve me of my soul to the heart / and this makes me
that I may never be merry and make glad chere / but ever am aferde of death for
my soul yt is the ^yf of my body. Then said ye. brother / lerye thee mercy /
for I knew never this till now and shall be wyser ever after / This I will say
boldly he yt will take this to heart he shall have better will to loure than to
laugh to sygh than to be glad / to weep than to sing so yt he shall find the
mind of death the pryncy pal salve of all manner of sin also princypally we
must have in ne mind ye* peynful death of our savyour yt he suffered for us all
/ of ye which is made me^cyon in ye. first chapter of trenys / Attendite and
videte siest dolor similis sicut dolor meus / That other salve is to labor
besely in this world / of us* labor speaks St. Poull in the pystle of this
day and says / Sic currite ut comprehendatis Renneye so yt. ye may have the
game / by this rennyng ye shall understonde yt. he that run for ye. game
enforsyth himself with all his might to run fast and so must every servant
of god enforce him to labor besely in the degree god has set him in and men
of holy church must labor in studying and prayeng and to teache ye. people the
law of god. Lord is and rentelmen must labor to keep holy church in rest and
peace and other common people must labourlogele lyvyng t^ these other degrees and
fsorhymself both to soul and body And for no man should excuse him from this
labor Christ in the gospel yeveth an ensample sayng thus Primomane conducere
operarios / An husbound man went into his gardeyn or vyneyard at pryme and a
yen at undren or myddaye / and sat even song time. And he hired people to
labor by all ye tides of the day / This is to understonde all ye-grees of ye*
world / For as Job says / A man is borne to labor and traveyle in this world
as a byrd to flee / And saint Bernard says He that will not labor here in this
world / He shall labor with the fendis of hell. For yt, is the testament of
Adam that he left to all his of spring / labor and traveylle / To this
labor he geveth ensample and reherseth how god made Adam and Eve ^o labor to
keep paradyse and bad they mete of all the fruits that was in paradyse / except
one tree that he keep for himself so as ^fte as they saw that tree / they
should think ^n him that made them and know him for their god / And for they
should notete there of inpeyne of dampnacyon Then the fendesawe them in so
much Joye that they were in and himself in so much pain / And woo that he
had great envye to them / and went to Eve: and asked why they ete not of the
fruit of that tree / And she said god has forbede us that tree in peyn of
death Then said the fend / he woteful well that and yeete thereof / ye
should be like god knowing both good and evyll / And if yewyl prove that I say
so the / ete thereof and assaye. Then took Eve of the fruit and gaafadam and bad
him ete thereof and for Adam loved her well / and would not wrath her / took an
apple and ete. And an another with ^yher of them saw others shape and were
asshamed. And took leaves afafygge tree and so ^evered her members. Than come
our lord to adam ^^ayd *Quarefeci^ti hoc* why have thou do so* and he said
(Mulier quamdedisti mich isociam) The woman bad me / Then said our lord to
eve / why did thou this (Serpens decepit me.) The serpent begyld me Then for
they might not deye in paradyse nesuffre no penance / therefore he drafe hem
naked out into this world that is full of wretched weeping and waylyngefull sore
syghynge to goo and gate her mete with great labor and travaylle and deye at
the last. Than prayed Adam our lard weeping / he should not take great
vengeance upon them* but have mercy on them / and pity for they were begyled
byenvy and malice of the fend / and by innocensye of them self that they wist
not what they did.

Then had our lord ruthe on them / and for they were both naked he clothed
them in pylches, and badde them goo labor and traveyle for the^r lyvyng /
And said to Eve (In dolor paries filios) In sorrow and woo shall thou bear thy
children / and took adaminsrumentes to labor with and lest them there. By
this yeshall understond and take ensample to labor b^seley. For and adam and
eve had labored besely / the fend had never overcome them. For the fend
desires no more when he would tempt a man but for to find him idle And
therefore know ye well that it is a rich salv^ against sin for to labor
besdy. The third is to chastyse the body dis^retely. (Unde Paulus. Castigoco^
pus meum etin servi^^te ^edigo) I shall chastysen^y body / and dress it to
service of my soul for man m^^ flesh is so wild and so lusty to sin that
it will not* in no wayeleve his lust to serve god / but if it be chastised
with penance. For it must be chastysed sometime with pain / Thus did adam and
eve in ensample that all other that shall come after hem should do the same for
many years before her death either of them stood in water a nyghtes up to the
^hy^ one serve from another to suffer penance till her fless he was as grene
as grass for cold. Then come y^*fende to eve also bright as an angel / and
said y^* god ha^ sent him from heven* and bad her goo to Adam and say to him
/ that god bad him leve his penance for her hespasse was forgyve. And Eve did
so / but adam wist well yt* it come forth from ye. fend and not from god. He
said to Eve when god drove us out of paradyse for our sin and had compassyon
on us / for we wept sore on him. and prayed him mekely of mercy he setted us
here to penance to ourlyves end. And therefore go again* for the more
penance yt we do ye more shall be our mede. And therefore go again and do thy
penance in god is name* yet the fend come again y^ second lyme and said to
Eve* god of his grace has take reward to your penance yt* ye suffer and has
forgyve you Then went Eve to Adam and told him so. Then said adam / I wot
well yt* he yt* has said so to the is our enemy / for our penance greveth
more him than us and he would have us to leve of and so to lose our mede / but
dowe fourth our penance to our lyves end For god takes none head to ye*
beginning of a thing but to ye* endyng* Yet ye* fend came again ye* third time
to Eve and said / goo thou to adam and say to him yt* he began foul and well
foul will end for first he trespassed by innocence and ^is^eyte of ye* fend
/ and now he synneth by good deliber^cyon and will not do as god byddeth him
wherefore your trespass is worthly dampnacyon. Then was Eve aferd and told adam
so Th^^ adam syked sore and wep^ and sai^ to her on auysyd woman god made the
of one of my rybbys for to help me and comfort me. and now be tysyng of the
fend thou art to combre me again but think how our first sin stancke in
the sight of god that all our ospryng shall be enfecte and have repreue there
of in to the world is end. where for though we might do also much penance
as all our ospryng might do yet hit were to little to quite our lord god
for our tres^asse but god of his special grace a lowythe a good will Than
went eve ayene to her penance as adam bad and than said adam god woll send
us the oil of mercy when time of mercy is. And so adam and eve deed her
penance to her lives end and when adam had leued. ix. hundred year and.
xxx. and had.xxx. ^ones. and. xxx. doughteris they deyde and were both beried
to gedyr Adam and Eve.

Thus ye may se well that adam and eve were full holy or they dyed and
thought one death full inwardely and labored full besely and chastised her
flesche full resonably and so must we do that comythe of hem yt wolle come to
the joy of paradyse in tokenyng here of this sunday is called the sunday in
septuages^me a nombre of.lxx. The which nombre be gynnyth this day and en dyth
on estyr euyne so holy church is morning from this day till Escyr euyne than
she takyth comfort again in party of on alleluya with a tracte for hit is not
yet in full might till saturday in Estyr weke the which is callid Dominica in
albis. Than she leythe down the tracte and syngithe doubell alleluya alleluy^
techyng all christian men to labor and do penaun ce treuly till the saturday
that is to a man's lyuys end that is till the soul go to rest yet is not
the soul in full rest till the saturday in albis that is till the day of dome
when the body and the soul shall come to gedyr and be clothyd in albis that is
in whithe seven times whyter than the son and than they shall sing doubyll
alleluya that is to sey lord make us save in ever lastyng bliss to the which
bring us he that for us all did on the wode tree Amen.

Dominica.lx.
GOod men and wymmen this day is called the ^onday in sexagesime that is the
nombre of.lx. the which no^bre holy church techith every man and woman to
think how short once lyffe is now in our days for sum time people
leuyd.ix. ^ year and more and now three score or fore score is a long lyffe But
yet the grace of god and his mercy and goodness is so much that if we will do
our besynes and diligence to serve god and plese him he will give ^s as much
joy and bliss in heaven as he gaffe to ada^ and eve that leuyd so long but he
y^ will have that joy and bliss must do iij. things. One is he must hate
sin namely and suffer tribulacion mekely and do alms deed wylfully Than for
our days be short we must the more tribulacion suffer mekely and with
pacient heart and not grocchyng and dissese comyth of special grace for hit is
remedy for sins here in this world for penance or else for great encresyng
to his joy in a nothir world where for goddys apostell poul woll that all
christian people shall take ensample of him for he suffered much tribulacion
patiently that he rehersith in the pistell of this day And said thus. In
laborihus plurimia Poule seith I have be in many great trauelles and oftyn
times in prison sore bou^dyn with cheynes of yren Quinq virgis cesue.v. times
betyn with roddys and stourgis on my bare body with paynemes Semel lapida tus
And ones betyn with stones and three times in ship brekyng Nocte ac die in
profundum maria fui. And I was in the ground of the sea a night and a day Sepe
in periculis fluuium. many times in parell of flodes. Periculis latronu^ in
parell of theuys and in parell of false brethe re^ that showed true love to me
and were false and conseyled other to do me dissese and troubell. In fame et
siti. in hungre and thirst In ieiuniis multis. in much fasting In multis
vigiliis. in long wakyng In frigore. in cold and in many other myscheuys and
parell that were to long to tell and all he suffered with good will and ever
thankyd god of his sweet sonde for well he wyste that all these tribulacionus
and dissese was for sin that he had done to fore And to encresse his merit
and joy that should come after where for all christian people that woll plese
god what manner dissese or tribulacion that come to hem be hit sykenesse loss
of catell or other goodys or death of frendys take hit patiently and mekely and
thyn kyth hit comyth for sin that thou haste do to fore or else for great
encresse of joy and bliss that thou shalt have after for hit comyth of
special grace there as god visitith and comyth there as god sendith but there as
he sufferyth all her will is no good syne that he louythe. And there fore
thank god ever of his visitacion and beseke him ever of his mercy god knowithe
our entente. and there for he for yeuith sone to all that askyth mercy with a
meke heart Thus must a man suffer tribulacione patiently he must also do
alms discretly which be figured be these.lx. days for.lx. is sexesythis x.
so that by.vi. ye shull understand the vij. werkis of mercy that comen out of
the.x. comaundementes the why the be these to give mete and drink clothe her
borow visit p^soners conforte the sike blind lame and to berie hem that be
deed these be the. vij werkys of mercy the which all christian people must do
that woll be saved and have mercy of god wherefore sexagesime be gynnyth this
day and endith the wenesday in esterwe^ke the which holy church spekyth of
thus Denite benedicti pr^ia mei ^^. Come ye my fadres blessed children and take
the kingdom of heaven that is ordained for you These same wordys god shall sey
to you at the day of dome And to all that has done alms dedys diseretly and
full filled the werkys of mercy and they where of pore and tho that be not of
pore must do her good will and that shall fullfille the deed this must be do
discretly and how god techith this day i the gospel be ensample and seyth thus
Exiit qui semiuat seminare seme^ suu^ A man went to sow his sedis and as he
sewe sum fill by the wey and fowlys come and ete hem and sum fill among
thornys and was lost and su^me fill in good earth and brought forth an C. fold
encrese to this criste seythe thus him self Ego su^ via veritas et vita. I am
the verray right true lyffe and wey to heaven Thanne fallyth his sede be sydys
the wey that yeuith not his alms for cristis sake discretly but for pride
pomp and vain glory of the world and so lesith his mede And that I preue be
ensample.



There was in yrlond a wondyr rich man and deed much alms in his live in so
much that the people went he had be a saint But when he was deed he aperyd
to on that he loved well in his live as black as any pyche with an horrible
stynke and said ye wene that be a seynte but now y am soche as thou seiste.
than said he where be thy alms dedis and he said the wind of vain glory
has blowym hem a wey for he that does his alms for vain glory of the
world lesithe his mede and the ^endys of the air destroyit hit Also he
lesithe his mede that yeueth his alms to soche that knowith that bethe in
dedly sin and so to maynten hem in her syn his sede fallyth among stones and
wexyt dry and so lesithe his mede his sede fallith among thorns that yeuith
his good to rich people that have no need there to and so les^ her mede. But
his sede fallith in good earth that yeuith his alms to good true people for
they be goddis earth and that sede shall give an hundrid fold encrese in ever
lastyng joy and bliss and shall be ever lastyng fode to hem that does thus
her alms discretly. ye must also hate sin namely and fle hit in all that
ye may for he that hatythe and fleith sin loved god and god loved him for god
hatith sin in so much that he took vengeau^ ce one all the world for sin
of lechery and in special for the synn again kind for when god saw this sin
regnyng in all the world so vnwordely he feyd thus me forthyn kyth that ever I
made man and said to noye Fac tibi archam. make the a ship of planed bo^dys
as I shall teache the and make chambres there in and take of all clean bestis the
coupull be hem self and mete and drink with hem Than made Noye this ship
as god taught him square in the bottym and. iij. C. cubytus of length and.l.
cubytus in bread and.xxx. cubytus of heythe and this ship was in making an. C
winter to schewe how mercyable god is in taryyng to look if the people would a
mende hem. and how loathe he was to do vengaunce but the people was ever lengyr
the wors than be help of angellis all manner byr dys and bestys were browghte
to Noye and when all where brought to the ship our lord badde Noye and his
wyffe and his.iij. sons go in to the ship by hem self and Noyes wyffe and
her sons wyffes by hem self. for the men should not common with the wymen so
when they where all ynne god closyd the door to hem with out forth
Quodraginta diebus and quadragin ta noctibus aperti sunt celi Thanne hit reymd.
xl. days and. xl. nyghtes that the water bare the ship heyer tha^ any hill
be.xl. cubytus and stood still a.C. days and.xl. and drowned all the world
both people and best save those that were in the ship. yet Josephus said in
armany there is an hill and that is called Sarus that was heygher thanne the
water was And there for diverse people have opinione there was much people
saved so noye was in the ship all a year and then he put out a rauyn for
to bring word for to know if the water was cessyd or no and he come not ayene
Thanne he sent out a dove and sho come ayene and brought a branch of olyue
in her bylle and there by noye know well that the watyr was cesid in sum place
Thanne as god bad him Noye went out and took the unclean bestys from the
clean and burnt the unclean bestys in sacrifice to god And that plesyd god so
well that he yaffe hem and all that come of hem after leave to et^ flesche of
all clean bestys and for to drink wine there as be fore the flode the people
ete and drancke no think but watyr for the earth was so batyll in hit self to
fore that the people nedyd none other fode but soche as come of the earth Thus
may ye see and understand how great vengeance god took on all the world for
sin and now there is as much sin as ever there was in those days and much
more in many degrees where I dread left god will take vengeance on us And
would or this time where not the preyers of holy church and good seyntes And
in especial by the preyours of our lady and that ye shall here be ensample og
seint Do mymke as he was in his preyoures he saw our lord ihesu criste
holdyng three sperys in his hand ready to schete hem in to this world for
vengeance and all for sin Tha^ come our lady knelynge be fore our lord and
said my dear sone what woll ye done. And he said my dear modyr the world is so
full of sin of pride couetyse lechery and other sins that Iwoll schete
these.iij. sperys of vengeance on the people Thanne seyde our lady my dear
sone have mercy of hem and bide a while for I have sum true seruau^tis the
which shall preche and teache people to turn hem from sin And thus be preyour
of our lady god spared to take vengeance But now the world is so full of
sin and cursed leuyng of false extorcione and oppression of the pore people
that they cry to god for socour and help wherefore hit is full like that we
shall be smetyn full sone with some grievous vengeance other with derthe or
with skarnesse of pestilence wherefore hit is needful for us to prey besely to
our lady that she may prey for us to her dear sone our lord ihesu criste to
spare us in our days that we ^ow have grace and mercy now and ever Amen

Dominica.l.
GOod men and wymmen this day is called the sunday in quinquagesime this word
qumquagesime is a nombre of.l. the which nombre be tokenyth remissione and joy
for in the old law every l. winter all manner of people that where over set
with service of bondage. when they come to that age they were made free in
great joy and mirth to hem wherefore this no^bre begynnythe this day and endyth
on estyr day schewyng that all christian people that be oppressyd with any
tribulacion or dissese here in this world shall be made fre and have remission
at the day of dome and be made air in the kingdom of heuene And yet in
comfort of all christian people every.l. winter the pope of rome grau^tith full
remission of all sins to all christian people that comith to rome that year And
for all that may not come thedyr to have this pardon The pope of heuene ihesu
criste of his special grace grauntyth to all christian people full pardon of all
sins in her last end so that they woll keep three things here in this
world Confession contricion and satisfaction Holy shryfte of mowthe with
contricion of heart and satisfaction indede doing Also he must have charity
with out faynyng and stabyll faith with out flateryng and with out these there
may no man have pardon at rome nor else where and there fore he that woll be a
soylyd of the pope of heuene and have clean re^^ssyone he must be contrite
sorry for his sins and shryue him clean and be in full purpose never to sin
more And they that do thus god will for gyffe hem all their sins for a man
may have so great and soche contricion that hit may quench all the pains that
ever where ordained for him Take ensample by petyr y^ for soke crist thryes
with great othys but he was after contrite and sorry Et flenit amare. And wept
full bitterly and god that is full of mercy for yaue him his trespass and made
better chere to him after than he deed to fore for he should be in no dyspeyr
and dread.



we find of a great rich man that was so wicked in his live that much people
demyd him dampened to hell so he fille sike and felyd him self that be should
be deed. and he be thought him how wicked he had be in his leuyng and took
soche a contricion to him and so great sorrow that he wept night and day ever
wha^ his sin come to his mind and so lay.vij. days and.vij. nyghtes and
shroue him clean and took great repentance to him and ever cried god mercy so
that all people had great pite on him and than dyed Than hit happid that there
was a monk in an abbay that dyed the same time and was ma de by his abbothe to
come ayene to tell him how that he ferde and so he deed and said to the abbot
when he was come. Sir I am come to hepe my promysse I prey you give me leave to
go a gain for I go to joy Thanne said the abbot was there any moo that dyed
when thou dydyste that went to joy but you And he said ye for sothe on and no
mo and that was the soul of soche a man and told his na ne Thanne said the
abbot now y know well thou art not my monk but sum fend is come to te^pe
me for we know well if any soul be in pain he is one of tho. Than said the
monk full unworthy is any man to know the preuites of goddys dome. For that
man had so great contricion and repentance and wept so bitterly for his
synnys that the watyr of his eyes perysched through all his clothys to the
ground where for go thou the dyr to morrow and when thou fyndyste hit true that
I sey than leave me And I go to ever lastyng joy and bliss. Than went the
abbot the dyr and found that hit was true as the monk had said. and there
knelid the abbot down and thankyd god and badde all the people to be glad that
god is so merciful and that he had that knowleche. Here ye may se that great
contricion that this man had quenchyd the great pain that was ordained for
him. Thus ye may se how great help is to a mannys soul to be contrite and
sorry for his sins and to draw a man to the more contricion those.l. days
these psalm in the sauter Miserere mei dena Be more rehersyd these days than
any other time of the year the which is thus much to sey. God for thy great
mercy have mercy on me and when a man is sorry for his sins and seyth thus
with a sorrowful heart god he ryth his preyour and for yeuith him his trespase
so that he be in full purpose never to sin more but to a mende him and be in
parfeyte love and charity with out any faynyng and but he have chari^e with
out faynyng all this preualyth naught and be this ensamp^le.



There was a man that had.v. sons and had found hem long to scole and
cost him much good So on a day he called his.v. sons be fore him and said
children I have found you long to scole and have spend much good up on you
and I se no great profit there of. where fore but yewoll a monge you all a soil
me a question I woll do no more cost on you ne find you no lengyr to scole and
they asked of her fadyr what the question was and hit should be a soyled And he
said I am old and febyll and may not live long and there fore I would wete of
you what thing would bring a man's soul sonnest to heaven and anon the
eldyste son answered and said for sothe fadyr prechyng and techyng woll bring
a soul sonneste to heaven of any thing. well said quoth the fadyr what seiste thou
to the second sone And he answered and said faith and true be leave bryngithe
a soul as sone to heaven. what seyste thou to the question my thryde sone and
he said good preyours and alms deed bryngith a soul sone to heaven what
seyste thou to the matter fowrith sone and he seyde pylgyymage going and great
penance sufferyng bryngith a soul sonner to heuene than any of all these what
seyste thou my fyuith sone and he said for sothe fadir there is anothir thing
that bryngith a soul sonner to heaven than all these what is that seyde the
fadyr for sothe fadir said he charity for what virtue that ever a man have and
he lack charity it vaylith not to heaven wardys for though a man prey and do
alms dedis goo a pilgrimage have full faith and be leave teache and p^che fast
and suffer penance never so much cry and wype never so loud and he be out
of charity god herith him not And here to acordyth seint poule in his pistel
and seythe thus Si linguia hominu^ loquar ^^. Though y were so eloquente as
any man or any angel. Et si babuero propheciam et omne scienciam And though y
had all the co^nyng in the world and know the propheci and the preuite of god
Omnem fidem vt montea tra^sferam And though y had so much faith that y
might meue hills. Et si distribuero in cibos pauperu^ And though y delyd all
my good to pore people for goddis sake Corpua meum vt ardea^ And my body to
brenne in hot fire. Caritatem autem non habe^m nichil michi prodest. if y have
not charity all this prefetith not to heuene wardys where fore hit is needful
and most necessary to every creareis soul that woll be saved to have charity
but though a man seyth that he loves god and loves not his even christian he
is disceyued For he that loved god loves his neighbor in good entente.

Thus must a man have full charity that will be saved Caritas cooperit
multitudine^ peccatorum. For charity coueryth the multitudo of sins. For he
that dies in dedely sin and out of charity shall be dampened And therefore of
all virtues charity is most vertuus and most necessary to a man's soul. yet
we must have a stable feythe with out flateryng and to believe saddely as
holy church techith. and to believe feythfully in the fadyr sone and holy ghost. the fadyr full god the sone full god and the holy ghost full and these
three persons be but one god that made all thing of naught. This faith was
first shewde in the holy patryarche in the vale of mambre there he saw three
fair men coming toward him but he worshipped but one yeuyng ensample to all
christian people to se in spirit the fadir the sone and the holy ghost three
persons in one god head and worshipped hem as on god Also ye must believe in
the carnacion of our lord ihesu criste that our lady conceived in the holy ghost with outewemme of her body in flesche and blood as one of us and verry
god and man and was deed and beried Tercia die resurrex it a mortuia And one
the thryde day he rose from death to lyffe Ascendit ad celos. And styed up to

^iguryd by isaac the sone of abraham that he get one his wyffe Sara thourgh

There was a bishop in england that hyghte croste head and was bishop of
lyncoll and was holdyn the grettyst clerk in england or in the world and when
he lay in his death bed there come to him a great multitude of fendes and
disputedr with him of the feythe in so much that they had de nyghe turned him
out of the believe and put in to despair.

Thanne was our lady ready and said to him my servant be leuyste thou not in
holy church as it techith And anon he cried and said yis gracious lady I be
leave as holy church techith me. and anon the fend is went her wey and gafe
up the ghost to ever lastyng bliss to the which god bring us all Amen.

Thanne angelis come and brought him fode for the fend is most besy these xl.

feign glory of the world ye must put a way all soche thoughtys of pride and

borne febyll sike and full pore and how he gothe every day a journey toward his
death while he leuythe in this world and at the last comythe death and cast
him down in to his bed and lie there Sykyng and grownyng and chaundid both
hyde and hew Thanne stynkyth his brethe and his lyppys wexit black his face
pale and his eyes yelowe his tongue eugleymed and his nose black his tothe
fallyn a wey his flesche wederith and tournythe to earth And thanne at the
last with great sighyng yeuith up the ghost and thanne lythe there as earth
and put in to the earth Cito obliuisceris And so shall be s^ne for gotyn.
There for take this sadly in your mind and I hope ye shall put awey pride.
Thanne a yense couetyse ye must have Abstynaunce that is for to sey ye must
absteyne your self from wordely couetyse and vanytees and they that have be
hard in keeping of goodys. and ever have gaderithe to gedyr to and fast have
in keep But now shul de ye be as ready to pay and content that ye be in debt
un to both to god and to the world And also to restore again that he has
takyn wrongfully. and give to pore people mete and drink and clothys and other
things such as is needful and to hem. And the fete that have all this this

et da bitur ^obi^. give ye and god will give you for the hondys that woll not

a great shame in heart so that he dare not tell hit out. Thanne must he
weastell with the find and the flesche and over come and tell out his sin
opynly with all the circumstaunce of his syn Thanne woll his flesch be a ferde
and a shamed there of but than he must wrastell with his flesche strongely and
make hit to tell his sins and to do penance aftyr the counsel of his
goos^ely fadyr taking the ensampell of the woman of ^er country that come to
criste as the gospel seith Ecce mulier cananea a finibua illis egressa
clamauit dicens How the woman of cananee come to crist to get hele for her
daughter that was trobbled with a fend And said Ihesu fili david mi serere mei
ihesu the sone of david have mercy on me Thanne our lord answered No^ est
^o^^m sumere panem filinrum and dare canib^^ Hit is not good to take bread of
children and give hit hundys Nam et catelli ^^e ^t de mensa di^ro rum suorum
yis lord for why when l^es eten of the c^ommys that fallyn from her lordys
board. Thanne said our lord Mulier magna est fides tua fiat tibi sicut via. O
woman thou haste a great feythe where for as thou wolte thy daughter be saved
and so was her daughter hole. This woman and her daughter be tokenythe a man
that his concience trauelythe with a fyude of dedely sin that may not be
helped but he go to god and there shryne him to the priste sparyng for no
rebuke nor shame ne for dread but me kely suffer all that the co^fessor seythe
to him and take his penance mekely with a contrite heart and do hit with good
devotion and so he shall be de lyueryd of the fend that has trouelyd his
concience. For a man that has done an horribell sin and shall be saved he
shall never have rest in his concience till he be shryuen there of for right ^^
an hounde gnawith a bone that is hard right so his sin gnawith his concience
showing be experience how houndys of hell shall gnawe his soul ever more with
out rest that dies wetingly in dedely sin that he might have be shryue^ of
and would not Ensample of a woman.



There was a woman that had done an horrible sin and would feign have be
shreuyn there of and durst not. Tha^ come our lord to her bodily and said my
daughter why shryuest thou the not of thy sin lord y may not for shame.

Thanne seyde onre lord take me thyn hand and put her hand in to his side
even to his heart and seyde woman what felis^ thou and she quakyd for fere and
said lord y feel thine heart. thanne seyde our lord be thou no more a shamed
to show me thyn heart tha^y to let the feel mine than this woman rose and
with light saw her hand all blody and would have waschyd hit of bnt it would
not till on the moxow that she was shrenen and than was her hand clean as hit
was be fore and she clean of all her sins and thus she was made clean both
body and so ule.

Om^ca tercia ^n^ dragesime
GOod men and wymmen this is the thridde sunday in clean sent on where fore were
de in the gospel of this day* and seythe thus Erat ^^esu^ ^i ciena demonin^
How our lord cafte out a fend of a dome man. and when the fend was out
^ocutna e^ mut^^ Thanne the dome man spoke be this dome man ye shall
understand all tho that have no might to shryue hem with her tongues to tell
her sins but ta^y as long as they may for there is much people and hit where
not for shame of the world in lenton nor out lenton would never come to
shryfte and that makyth the fend for he is in that man or woman whethyr* hit
be that is so disposyd. There for ye that be behind come and shryue you and
make you clean and have this dome man out of your mind ande^ cast a wey the
fend but there be many that bythe not yet shreue^ what shall I do there wolle
they sey they can not shryue hem they wot not where of. But I may sey to you
of many an evil word and many an evil thought and many a cursed deed many
great othys many an evil word that ye have spoke I wot ye can not tell all
for ye have been so long fro confession But I sey to you that vnknowyngnesse
shall not excuse yodo at the day of dome for as soon as ye have offendyd god in
many trespacis that hurtith the soul anon ye should make you clean and will
it never in your mind but ye woll not come till hit be for gotyn And so yet
wha^ ye come to shryf te ye be dome for the fend is withyn you for ye wene
many times that hit be no sin to speak an ydyll word to make the people to
laughe nor to swear a great oath it does no harm but seint poule in his
pistell forbedith every man to speak any idyll wordis and seithe thus. Dico
autem vobis quod omne verbum ociosum quod locuti fuerint omnea reddent rationea
in die iudicii For sothe. I sey to you that ye shall give a rekenyng for every
idyll word that ye speak and non shall pass un punyshid at the day of dome.
and there for late all idyll wordis be harlatry and rybawdiy And if ye so do
that is worship to god and profit to the speker for there as harlatry is
much spokyn it is much in mind For the tongue shewde the habundau^ce of the
heart so first in thought after in his spekyng hit causith much people to
fall in sin of deed doing. Dnus quisque temptatur concupiscencia. Furste
every man is temtid to sin be lust of thought there one. Concupisce^cia
generat pccm^. And the lust gaderith sin. Peccatnm cu^ consummatum fuerit
generat morte^. And when the sin is done hit causithe dam pnacione ever
lastyng death that is in spekyng rebawdry and harlatry for the lust that a man
has in spekyng is great sin.



we find of an abbas that was a clean woman as for any deed of sin but she
had great lust to speak there of So when she was deed and beried in the
church the night after come fendys and took up the body and all to beat hit
with brennyng scourges fro the nauyll upward that it was as black as any
piche But fro nauyll downward it shone as bryghte as any son and the fendes
might do it no harm and ever as the fendes beat her she cried pitously that
ij. of her sustres that where sextens were sore a ferde there of but either
comfortid other so that they went nere till they wist how it was Than spoke
the sperite to her suste ren and seyde ye know well that I was a clean meyden
as for any deed. but I had great lust to speak of synn that party has
great pain as ye may se where for i prey you susteren prey for me for by your
preyouresy may be helped. and be ware by me in time coming here by ye may se
what parell it is to speak idyll wordis and harlatry speech. where for this
same pistell seythe thus Abstinetis vos a fornicatione. Absteyne you from
fornicacion and all sins and walkithe with criste in love and pees as criste
deed that suffered for us many scorns rebukes and dispites and all he took
mekely patiently and in charity yeuyng ensample to all christian people to do the
same* but he that woll leave in rest and pees shall have great persecucion of
evil people but and he suffer hit mekely he is a martyr be fore god and in
confermyng of this holy church makythe mind and mention as thus.

we read of an holy man that was callid Joseph that suffered great persecucion
but he suffered ^it mekely there for god brost ghte him to great worshipp^ and
prosperity. and how ye shall here but for this story is long there for we shall
take that is most needful at this time. This Joseph had a fadir that highte
jacob and had xij. sons brothe ren to joseph but his fadir louid him most
specially of all that other and there for his brethren hatid him the more And
in especial for a dreme y^ he dremyd where by they supposid all that he shul
de be lord of hem all. and all they should do him worshipp^ and a non they
took her counsel to gedyr and seyde Venite itamque occidamus illum Let us go
there for and sle him but yet they durst not for dread of god and a non
Vendiderunt eum in egipto they sold him in to egipte to a man for.xxx. pennys
as god was sold and there for god was with him So a man that was steward to
the king bought him that hight po^tifer but the fend had great envy to Joseph
^ temptid the lady sore on him. Post multos itaque dies iniecit domina oculos
in joseph et ait veni dormi mecum So on a day the lady lokid on joseph and took
him by the mantill and seide come and sleep with me and as soon as Joseph under
stood her menyng anon he yode and flede his wey and left his mantill there Than
this woman cryde and told her husbonde how Joseph would have leyne by her and
for he should not sey nay she kept his mantill. There for the lord made to
cast joseph in prison there as pharao had put his boteler and his baker and as
they fell a sleep they dremed the which dremes they told Joseph and he seide
that the king would restore his boteler to his office ayene with in three days
and the Baker should be hanged with in three days and as he seyde hit was than
happyd so that the king dremed him self but there could no men tell what
should fall there of but be counsel of the boteler the king sent after joseph
And when the king had told him his dreme Joseph seyde that god hade sent him
a fair warnyng to puruey him to fore that should come aftyr And he said there
should come vij. plenteuous yeris of corn and of all manner fruits and vitayles
and aftyr hem should come vij. yeris in the which people should spend all
that was go tyn to fore. Thanne the king seyde I know no man that cowde puruey
so well for soche a thing as thou coudist wherfo^ I make the gretttest under me
of all my ^eame and ^ shall do to the as to me at thy commandment Thanne a
none io seph let make the gretest bernes that ever was seyne and gaderid corn
fast vij. yeris And sone after come vij. yeris that all things was scarche
and dear. Than jacob Joseph fadyr herd that there was corn to selle in
egipte. And he sent the their his x. sons for to bey corn and when they come
thethir and saw Joseph all fill down on her knees and did him worship like
as his dreme was for they know not him but went that he had belord of the
country. But he know hem well y now. Thanne he spoke to hem in lateyne. Surge
And said they where spies that where come to know of the lon de. and they
seyde nay they where all brethren and all oue man's sons and a nothir
brother they had that was at home with her fa^yr and there was a nothyr and
they woste not where y^ he were a live or no and that they mente by Joseph and
for to preue the trowthe he made to bind on of hem that highte Symeon and
seyde that he should a bide with him tili they hade fette him at home. and so
let fill her sackys with corn and preuely put her money in to her sackys
vnwetyng to hem. And so when they come home to her fadyr and put out her corn
there they for de her money and they told her fadyr but than was he sorry for
symeon his sone that was left be hynde in prison And more over for that he
must ^edys send fore him which he loved most and that was beni^min Joseph
hole brothir for these other where but half brethren to Joseph But when jacob
faylyd corn he must nedys send for more and he sent forth Benjamin And
when Joseph saw his brothyr benjamin he might not for bear weping and anon
delivered him his brothyr symeon and set hem all to mete and fillyd her
sackys with corn and preuely put the cup that they drank of in beniamyns
sack and he ^ad hem go her wey But anon aftyr joseph seute aftyr hem and
seyde they where to blame while they had so good chere to bear a wey the
cup that they drank of Thanne they were heavy and sad and said hit was not
so and he ran sakyd hem by and by and than they fond hit in Beniamyns sack
tha^ come they ayene to joseph sore weeping and when joseph saw hem all weep
and his own brothyr Benjamin made most sorrow for it was found with Thanne
^oseph badde hem all be of good chere for I am joseph your brothyr and be no
thing a dread for god has sent you hedyr for your profit and a none sent
aftyr his fayir and so dwelled all to gedir a great while in that land with
much prosperity This story is rad de this weke in holy church for goddys
childeren should take ensample of old fadres to suffer tribulacion and
persecncion mekely in parfyte charity for goddys sake as he suffered for us.
for who that gro^hith a yense tribulacion and persecucion that god sendith
must shryue him and take his penance. for there is sum people will sey why
does god thus by me what have I trespa sid a gain him tho be in great parell
for her patience for truly wordys may let much grace.



we find in miracles de wynfryde the virgyne that a man come to her on a

So at night he went to his bed in good hele and on the morrow his sikenesse
took a yene sarrur than hit deed be fort and so lay cryyng that hit was great
pi^e to here

Thanne come a monk to him and asked him what he hade done that his sikenesse
was come a yene and he said no thing Thann seyde the monk were thou shreuyn
sethe thou were hole and he seyde nay I had no need for I stale nethyr ox
nor cow nor did no grievous sin than the monk thought though a ^a^ do no
dedly synue he may do so many vema^^ that they may make a dedely sin for
right as a man may with many small cornys charge a scronge horse so may he let
his soul with so many small sins that he may fall in to the pit of hell
Thanne a none this man went to a priste and shwue and so was hole both in body
and soul ever aftyr be confession and preyoures of this holy virgin Amen

GOod men and wym men this is the fourth sunday in lenton the which holy church makythe mention of an holy prophet that was callid moyse the which
was a figure of our lord jhesu criste many yeris or our lord was borne Tha^
as we read in holy church as moses was in the deserte of synay god spoke to
him and said Didi afflicto^n^ populi mei qui est in egipto clamorem eius ^^dini
etc^. Pharao the king of egipte oppressithe so the people of israhel with
bondage and unreasonable werkys and they for woo cryde to me for socour and
help where for go thou thethir and bring hem out of her bondage and I shall be
with the then bring hem and offer hem to mey woll bring hem into a land of
plenteuousnes of all goodys So wha^ he had taught moses how he should do
moses went thedyr and gederid all she old people to gedir that know the
prophecy how they should be ladde out of that land and said to hem as god bad
him tha^ were they full glad and went with him old and young till they come to
the reed see and god was ever before hem in the day in a pilar as a cloud to
refresche hem from the hets of the son and in the night in a pilar snyur to
light fro harm of venym bestis. But when that pharao herd that moses had
forth this people he took.iij. C. chariotis of his own and iij. C. of the
land and lx. M. horsemen and iij. C. M. fotemen and went aftyr

And when moses saw this people come he preyde to god for help and god him
self smyght the sea with his yerde. Et percussit mari rubro And when he had
smetyn the sea he had wey for him and his people the sea clefe a ij. parties
so that the watyr stood still on every side as an hill and the ground was dry
sonde. Than moses yede forth and all the people aftyr him

Than wend pharao to have passyd also and sewyd aftyr with all his oste but
when he had his oste with in the se the watyr went to gedyr and drowned him
and all his oste and when moses saw that he and his people were thus peryshyd
he thankyd god and was there vij. days aftyr and every day they yede to the sea thankyng god of her passage making great melody that our lord hade do so
to hem. And yet mind here of all Estyr weke we make solemn procession to the
font y^ is the reed see Thanne went moses forth with his people in to
deserte till he come to the hill of Synay and there he left the people be
nethe Stabat moisea super montem and moses stood up on the hill there as god
was And there he was fourthy days and fourthy nyghtis with out mete or drink
Thanne god gafe him ij. tabeles of stone in the which god wrote with his own
fynheris the x. commaundementis and took them moses and bad him teache hem ^o
his people And when moses come down to the people his face was all bryghte
as the son and ij spyris stondyng on his head like ij horns so that the
people might not speak with him for clerenesse Abscondit moisea faciem s^am.

Thanne moses hid his face with a kerchoffe Thanne in that on leffe were
wreton the three co^maundementis that langithe to god. and that be these. The
first is thou shalt worship thy god and love him a boue all thing for thou
shall te direct all mauer thing to goddys will be ^^^ thy ne own and shwe his
will and not thy own will The secounde commandment is this.

Thou shalt not take his name in vein. that is for to sey thou shalt not be
callid goddis child as a christian man and serve the send fore than that name
is to the but vain. Also thou shalt not swear by god nor by no part of his
body no^ by no thing that he made but in foetheryng of the truth And yet but
when thou art constreyned there to. The thrydde commandment is thou shalt
keep thy holy day that is for to sey thou shalt be erly up and late down to
serve god on the holy day as thou art on the work day to thy own work as
besy shalt thou be on the holy day to serve god The fourth commandment is
thou shalt worship thy fadyr and thy modyr that brought the in to this would
Also thy godfadyr and thy godmodyr that made the a christian man and thy fadyr
vndyr god that has cure and charge of thy soul The v. is thou shalt sle no
man no this with thy tongue nor with thy hand nor with evil ensample The vi.
thou shalt not stele no man's god (...)

fere of the common people for they hylde him a prophet But this day they knette

Thus our lord this day began his passione where for holy church redithe
this weke in the book of jeromie the prophet that first prophesied of cristus
passione and told how and in what manner the jews should done him to death
Tha^ye shall understand well that in the same wise as the jews pursued criste
to the death in the same wise I fere greatly left there be much false people
that been christian that pursewith criste in heaven now. Saint Austeyn seyth that
they sin more grievously that pursew him in heaven than the jews did that
pursewid him here in earth to death. Than if ye woll wete which these be. take heed how criste markyd hem and seyde thus.

Qui ex deo est verba dei audit He that is of god herith the word of god for
he herith not the word of god that swery the many great othis full falsely these
ben tho that pursewid him in henen that been glad in her hertys when they have
a foul deed do and be groundid in foul cursid leuyng of syn and woll not a
mende hem for prechyng nor techyng but ever do foul dedys and a none be ready
to fight and to chyde with hem that tell ithe hem her defawtis as hit is
shewde by criste For the mo har me is. the conditions of the people is such
now a days that he shall have many enemies that will sey truth and that I
may preue by ensample



There was sum time a mawment in a cite that would tell where anythyng was
that was stole or myssyd and how had hit. So hit happid on a time that a young
man had stole a thing and was a ferde of this mawmetis and a none he went to
this mawme^t and seyde thus well I wot thou may do me a great shame and
vyllony but be god that y believe upon and thou discover me I woll break thy
head and so went for the his wey Thanne so ne aftyr come they that myssyd this
good preyng the mawment to tell hem how had hit and when they had long
preyde at the last the maument spoke and said times be ^hau^gid the people be
worse thanne they were who seythe the troughte his head shall be broken. So he
that woll sey truth he shall be shente and so the true man shall be so huntyd
and so pluc hyd that he shall not we te to whom he shall speak nor to whom he
may tell his council in trust for he that woll sonest disceyue him wolle
speak sum time most fay rest so that may be p^uyd Hit is wreton in the book
of kings how there were ij. knyghtis great enmyes on to that othyr y^ one
highte Jacob and that other amasa and this jacob seyde to Amasa as they met
hayle brothyr and kyssid him and with his other houde be hynde he slew him
with his knyfe and smote him to the heart. Thus hit farithe now a days be mo
the people they speak full fair be fore the people and be hynde him they woll
^le him with a shrowde knyffe that is with the cursid tongue these be they that
pursewed him in heaven and set naught by goddys word for if though they
heren hit with her erys hit synkith naught in her hertis.

where god pleynith him grievously be his prophet Ieremye. and seyde thus what

Thus be her hertis herder than any stone and thus we be worcester than jews thus we

ou^tyn end so that all the fawte shall be found in the and not in me Thus

^^yndes in richesse and this worldis prosperity in this present lyffe and take
