We read in seynte Gregorius time there was a woman that highte laciua and she
made bread for the pope and othyr prestys to singe with and for to hosell with
the people Also when the pope come to this woman to give her hosell and seyde
take here goddis body than this woman smylid and laughed thanne the pope with
drew his ho^de and leyde the oste upon the auter and turned to this woman
laciua and seyde to her whismylest thou when thou shuldeste resceyue cristus
body and she seyde why call^ste thou that cristus body that I made with mine
own hondis Tha^ was Gregor the pope sorry for her mys^e believe and badde all
the people prey to god to show sum miracle for this womannes help and when
they had preyde long Gregor went to the auter a yene and found the oste
turned in to reed flesch and blood bledyng and he shewde hit to this woman
Than she cried and seyde lord now I cry the mercy I believe that thou art
verray god and man and goddis sone of heaven in form of bread. Thanne badde
Gregor the people prey a yen that hit should turn a yene to bredis likeness
and so hit deed and with the same oste he hoselid this woman lacina and therefore
late us do all the worshipp^ that we may to the sacrament that we can or may
and be in no mysbeleue



Also we find that in deuynchere be side exbrigge was a woman lay sike and was
nigh deed and sent aftyr a holy person abowte mydnyghte to have her rightis
than this man in all the haste that he might he a rose and went to church
and took goddis body in A box of yuery and put hit in to his bosom and went
forth toward this woman. And as he went thourghe a foreste in a fair mede
that was his next wey it happid that his box fill out of his bosom to the
ground and he went forth and woste hit not and come to this woman and herd
her confession And than he askid her if she would be hoselid and she seyde y^
sere. than he put his hand in his bosom and sought the box and when he
found hit naught he was full sorry and sad and seyde dame in woll go aftyr
goddys body and come a none a yene to you and so went forth sore weeping for
his simpulnesse and so as he come to a ^elow tree he made there of a rod and
strypyd himself all nakyd and to beat himself that the blood ra^ne down by
his sydys and seyde thus to himself O thou simple man why haste thou lost thy
lord god thy maker thy former and thy creator And when he had thus beat
himself he deed on his clothis and went forth. And than he was ware of
pilour of fire that last from earth to heaven and he was all asto yned thereof
yithe blessed and went there to and there lay the sacrament fallyn out of the
bore into the grass and the pilour schon as bryghte as any son and la styd
from goddis body to heuyn and all the be stys of the foreste were come about
goddis body and stood in compass round about hit and all knelid on four knees
save on blake horse that knelyd but on that on knee Than seyde he if thou be
any best that may speak I charge the in goddis name here present in form
bread tell me why thou kneliste but on thy one knee. Thanne seyde he I am a
fend of hell and wolle not knele and y my ghte but I am made a yense my will
for hit is wreton that every knelyng of heaven and of earth shall be to the
worship to the lord god. why art thou like a horse and he seyde to make the
people ^o stele me and at soche a town was one hougid for me and at soche a
town anothir Tha^ seyde this holy person y commau^ de the by goddis flesche
and his blood that thou goo in to wilderness and be there as thou shalt never
dissese christian people more And a none he went his wey he might no le^ ger a
bide And thanne this man went forth to(...)

De festo sancti andree apostoli.


GOod men and wymme^ ^och a day ye sha^ have seint Andrewis day and ye shall
fast the euene and come to god and to holy church and worship this holy
seynte that day for three special vertous One is for his great holiness in his
ded doing. The secounde for his good leuyng. The threde for his great
compassion sufferyng. He was a man of holy leuyng for when he understood and
herd of seint Johan the baptist that he was prechyng in deserte anon he left
all his wordely occupacion and went to him and was his disciple. And so after
on a day as crist come walkyng by the way and seint Johan baptiste saw him
walkyng he seyde to his diseiples. Ecce agnus dei qui tollit peccata mu^di See
the lombe of god that shall do a way the sin of all the world. And when
seint Andrew he^de that anon he left seint Johan baptiste and sewid forth
criste

And when he herd criste preche hit plesid him so well that a none he went
and fette Petyr his brother to here criste preche than they cast great love to
god and sone after as they where in the sea of galyle fischyng crist come and
called hem and a none they left fischyng ship and net and all that they
had and sewid crist ever after and where with him till he styed up to heuene.



Thanne after that seint Andrew prechid a mong the people than on a day as he
prechid it happened so there was a man among the people that was called Nicoll
that had leuyd many wynters in lechery but yet by the g^^ce of god he
thought to amend his lyffe and when he herd that the word of god was of so
great virtue that hit should put a way all temptacions of sin he let write
a gospel and bare hit with him where some ever he went and with the virtue
there of he absteyned him self from sin. But yet on a day by temptacione of
the fend he for gate him self and went ayene to a brothellus house as he was
used to do be fore and when he come thedyr and when the wymen lokyd up on him
they cried out on him and said o thou old sely man what doste thou here go
home ayene for we see so many marvelous on the that we may not have to do with
the. Thanne this Nicoll be thought him that he had the gospel upon him and a
none he went to seint andrew and told him all the cause and preyde seint
andrew to prey for him that his soul might be sauyd. Thanne seint andrew
would never etene drink till he wyste whethir Nicoll should be sauyd or no
Thanne seint andrew fastyd.v. days bread and watyr and preyde besely night and
day. Thanne come a voice and said as thou haste fast and preyde make Nicoll to
do the same and thanne he shall be saved. Than seint andrew bad Nicoll fast.v.
days bread and water and prey besely unto god and so he deed and thanne come a
voice to seint andrew ayene and said thy preyours and thy fasting has made
Nicoll that was lost found ayene and he shall be sau^d.



Also anothir miracle that anothir young man come to seint andrew in a time and
said preuely to him sire my modyr has be long about me that I should lie
with her and for I would not do her will she has acused me to the bishope and
said that I would have done that sinful ded with her where for I wotte well
that I shall be deed and yet I had lever dye than sclandyr my modyr so soul
There for I beseech you prey for me that y may take my death patiently to the
salvation of my soul Thanne said seint Andrew goo forth to thy dome and I
shall goo with. and so there with the people come and set him be fore the
bishop And when his modyr accufid him he said no thing but held his pese
Than said seint Andrew.

Innocena sangnia eiua sine causa dam nabit. This cursed woman for lust of her
body wrongfully is about to dampne her own child to death vengeance woll
come to the. Thanne said she lo sire justice ever sethe he might not have his
will he has drawyn unto this man for counsel and socour Thanne the justice
comaundid to cast this youg man in to the watyr to drown him and to put
seint andrew in prison till he where a vysid what death he should dye. Thanne
seint andrew preyde besely unto god for help and socour and thanne a none come
a great thoundyr and made all the people so a ferde that they where feign to
set seint Andrew out of the prison. And even there with come a lyghtnyng of
fure and brennyd the modyr of the young man in sight of all the people. And thus
was this man sauyd and the justice by this great miracle turned to christian
feyth and much other people with him and ever after believed in god and seint
Andrew there by ye may see that he was holy in leuyng.

Also he was great in miracles worchyng for on a day as he went by the sea
side he saw a drowned man cast out of the watyr than andrew preyde to god to
rere him ayene to lyffe and anon this man rose Than andrew asked him where
that he was drowned. and he seyde we where.x. men to gedyr and herd of an
holy man that hight Andrew And we where coming to here his prechyng and as we
where in the sea there come a great tempest and drowned us all to gedyr but
would god that we had be cast to land to gedyr that we might have been
raised to lyffe to gedyr ayene. Thanne anon seint androwe preyde to god that
all the bodies might come to gedyr and so they deed. and where raste up in
diverse countres Than seint andrew made and ordained to gedere hem all to
gedyr. Than he knelyd down and preyed god long for them till they where
raised all to lyffe. Than seint andrew made hem all to knele down and thank
god and preached hem and taught hem christian feythe and cristened hem all and
when they where stedefaste in the feythe he sent hem home to their own
country with much joy to hem and many other miracles he ded that where to
long to tell thus ye may se that he was mighty in miracles worchyng that
raised so many men to lyffe Also he suffered great passione for criste sa^ke
for when he was in the cite of pateas there he turned to the feyth the wife of
Egeas. And this Egeas was a great man and made much people to do sacrifice and
ofringes to maumentys but for seint andrew repreuyd him there of anon he made
to take him and would have made him to do sacrifice but he would not and
stedefastly ayenstode him and preuyd be many ensamples be cause that he and all
the people should worshipe god and not the fendis of hell Thanne was egeas wode
for wroth and made men to take andrew and stripe him nakyd and beat him with
storges that all his body ran on blood and thanne made to bind him hand and
foot and made do him on a cross for he should pain there on long or he died
but when andrewe come to the place there the cross was he knelid down and
said thus. Salve cr^x que in corpore christi dedicata e^. Holy be thou xrosse
that art hallowed and made holy by the precious body of our lord ihesu
christ I desire to clippe the to me where for take me to the for I yield me
unto my mastyr ihesu criste that dyed on the cross And than andrew stood up
and ded of his clothis and yaue hem to the tourmentoures and bad hem do as they
where chargid to do of the justice Thanne they bound him to the cross hand
and foot and his head downewardes and streyued him so that the blood barste
out at every knotte of the ropes and so he honge there.iij. days a live
prechyng the people and so there come to the prechyng many thowsandes of people
and for pite that they had of him they bad Egeas take him down or they would
sle him. Thanne for fere of the people egeas come to take him down Than seint
Andrew ayenstode him and said Quid tu venisti adme egeas what comist thou to me
Egeas wete thou well thou shalt have no might to take me down for on this
cross woll I dye And even there with. Hiis enim dicti^ splendour nimis circuiens
eum quasi per media^ horam. a great light come a boute him that there no man
might se him in space of half an our and more Thanne said seint Andrew.
Obsecro tedn^e miserere mei. I be seche the lord have mercy on me and so in
that light he yafe up the ghost. And thanne when egeas saw and know this that
he was deed he went homeward than after that day he waxyd wode and sone after
he dyed among all people And when maximilla his wyffe herd there of a none she
took andrewys body and buried it in a tomb. and out of the tomb wellyd manna
and oil to gedyr and by that people of the Country know when hit should be
dear and when great plente For when it shall be cheppre hit wellyth plentyfully
and when it shall be derthe sharsely.



Hit fell so there was a bishop that louyd well seint andrew and for the find
might in no wise bring him out of his purpose he come to the bishop in
likeness of a feyr woman preyng him that she myt speak with him in counsel of
confession And he granted there to Sire said she y am a knights daughter and
have be much cherished and norishid in great tenderness and for I see this
world is but a vanite to trust upon y have avowed chastity and now my fadyr
would mary me to a worthy prince and for I would not brecke my vow y am come
preuely a wey in pore array and thus y herd of your great holiness and am come
to have your council and socour and help of you. wherefore I pray you that ye
ordeyn for me that the fend have no power to let me of my porpose Thanne the
bishop comforted her and bad that she should thancke god that had set her
in such porpose and that he would send her grace there with to co^tynue And
seyde to her Esto secura filia. Be thou sekyr daughter this day thou shalt
dyne with me and thanne we shall by good auyse when we have dyned ordeyn so for
you that ye shall do right well Nay sir said she left the people would have any
suspessione of badde reule ye said the bishop there of no charge Plurima erimus
and non soli. For there shall be so many in company that there shell be none
suspessione Thanne sho thankyd him feyre and scho was set to for the bishop
in a chayr at mete And ever when the bishop lokyd on her he semyd her so
fair that he was greatly temptyd on her so that he had all most foryete him
self. And thanne anon there come a pilgryme to the gate and beat fast on the
gate that all that were in the halle were sore a stonyd of the noise so he
cried let in let in Thanne seyde the bishop shall this man come ynne.
Tha^ne said sho late him answer to sum questione first whethir he be worthy
or no to comesonye in presence. Thanne seyde the bishop I pray you makeye the
question for I am not a vysid at this time Thanne said sho to the massenger In
terroga quod e^ magis miraculu^ quod deus vmqua^ in parua re fecit Ask him
what was the grettyste miracle that ever god made in a foot of earth. Thanne
when the pilgreme was asked this he answered and said a mannys face the which
is but foot and but a mannys own face For thou all the me^ and wymmen that
ever where borne stood a fore me ytte should y know one from a nothir be some
degree. when he yafe this answer he was greatly co^mendid therefore Than said she
I se that he is wise. bid him yefe a nothir answer to anothir question Ask
him whethir earth is he yer or heuyn Than he answered and said thus There as
cristys body is there is earth for cristys body is of our kind and our kind is
earth. there fore there as cristis body is earth is heyer than heuyn. when he had
yeuyn that answer he was well a lowed and was beden come in Nay said she late
him a soil the third question Ask him how far it is fro heuyn to hell than
when he was oposid of this he answerde the messengere Goo again to her that
sets in the chair be fore the bishop and bydde her give this answer for
she can better than I. Quando de celo in abissum ^ecidit For she is a fend and
has metyn hit and so did I never She fill down with lucifer And when the
messengere herd this he was all heavy but he yafe this answer that all men
might here. Than this fend vanished away with an horrible stink Than the
bishop bethout him of his temptacion and was sorry in his heart and anon he made
to send after this pilgryme but be that the messenger come ayene to the gate he
was gone. Than the bishope made all men to pray to god to send wetyng what the
pilgryme was y^ so goodly halpe him at his need Than come there a voice to him
and said hit was seint andrewe that come and to socour him for the good love
and service that he did to him and bad him preche this miracle to the people to
se and know how graciously he helpith all that well pray to him And there fore
late us worship and pray to him to be our socour and help ayenste the find
now and ever.

AMEN.
Festum sancti nicolai.


GOod men and wymmen soch a day ye shall have seint nicolas day the which is
much preysed in holy church and specially for three causis. the furste for
his meke leuyng The secounde for his heavenly techi^^ The third for his great
compassion having Furste he was made lowly Pater eius epiphanus matter eius
iohana dicta est. Hit is said that his ^adyr highte epiphanus and his modyr
ione the which in their thought goto seint nicolas And when he was borne they
made her ^owes both to keep and to leave in chastity and no more come to gedyr
but hold hem plesid of this one child that god had sent hem the which they
made him christian and called him Nicolas that is a maunes name but he kepith the
name of the child for he chose to keep virtuous meekness and simpleness and
with out malice. Also we read while he lay in his cradyll he fastyd we^^nysday
and freyday these days he would soke but ones of the day and therewith held him
plesid Thus he leuyd all his live in virtuous with this child is name And there
fore children done him worship be fore all othyr feintys for he was ever
meke with out any malice so that all people preysed him for his meke leuyng
here. Also he was bishop of the cite of mirre by the which that come from
heuyn. For when the bishop was deed all the bishops of the country come to
gedyr to chese anothir than ne come a voice to on of hem and bad him rise erly
in the morrow and go to the church door and make him bishop that ye find
there that is callid Nicolas And so on the morrow he come to the church door
and there he found Nicolas And than he said thus to him Quale nome^ habeatu
what is thy name. Inclito capite And lowtyng with his head answered mekely and
said Nicolas thanne said the bishop Fili ^eni mecum. Sone come with me for I
have to specke with the in counsel and so ladde him to the other bishops and
said lo seris here is he that god has ordained to be. And so they made him
bishop of mirre by heavenly chesyng. He had also a great compassione of tho
that where in dissese and parell for when his fadyr and his modir dyed they
left him wordely good y now the which that he spente on the^ that where pore
and nedy.



Hit fell so that there was a rich man that had iij. fair daughters young
wymmen but by mishefe he fell in to pourte so that for great need he ordained
his eldyste daughter for to be a common woman. And so after the tothir to
daughters for he might not find hem And so by this mean got his leuyng and
heris both for he woste not how to leave for the great pouerte that he stood
ynne And when Nicolas herd there of he had great compassione of hem all and
come preuely in a night to this man's house and at a wyndow he cast a b^gge
of gold in to this man's chanbre. and on the morrow when this man ^ose and
found this gold a none there with he married his eldeste daughter Thanne come
nicolas and brought anothir sone after and there with he married the secounde
daughter Thanne this man had great marvel how this gold come the their and
wakyd preuely to know there of a^^ the thridde time Nicolas come and this man
herd the gold fall anon he went out and ouertoke Nicolas and when he know
that hit was he that had helped him so in his need he knelid down and would
have kyssid his fete but he would not suffer hit but prayed him to keep
counsel while he leuyd.



Also anothir time men where in the sea like to be drowned in a great tempest
they cried to god and seint nicolas seeing thus Domine rex eterne succurre nobis
misery. Lord king ever lastyng socour us wrechis and anon nicolas come and
said. Docasti^ me ecce assum presena ^o I am present at your calling and so
brought hem forth save and sound to land.



Also there was in the count^^ in a time great derthe of corn Fame^ valida and
great hounger in so much that the people where all most lost for the fault
of mete Thanne hit hapenyd there come ships of the Emperors frayghte in to an
hauyn with whete in that country. Thanne went seint Nicolas to hem and preyde
hem that he might have of every ship a.C. bushelles of her whete for to
releue the people with And he would vndyr take that they should lake none of her
met when they come home thanne he had all his askyng and when the ships
come to the emperor they had her full mesure and lackyd no thing of her
corn that seint nicolas had thorough his holy preyour Oquam probat sanctum
dei farris augmentacio. O how meruelously be grace of god and preyour of this
holy man this whete was multiplied and encresyd for of that whete was so great
plente that hit found all the people to ete and drink and sowgh y now three
year after.



Anothir miracle there where.ij. knights that where accused of treson to the
emperor of a false matter and where commanded to preson for to have been put
to death sone after Thanne they cryde to god and to seint nicolas for help and
socour so that the night before that they should be deed seint nicolas come to
the Emperor as he lay in his bed and said thus to him why haste so
wrongfully dampened these knights to death a rise up anon and dely uer hem
o^te of preson anon or else y woll prey to god to reyse batell up on the in
the which thou shall dye and wild bestys shall ete the. Than said the
Emperor to him what art thou that so boldly spekyth and so thretenyste me
Thanne said he y am nicolas the bishop of mirre than the Empero(...) sent
after the knyg^^^s and ^^yde to hem what wyche craft can ye that thus has
traueled me to night know ye any man that hyghte Nicolas bishope of mirre
Thanne as soon as they herd this name they fell down to the ground and held
up her handys thankyng god and seint Nicolas. when they had told the
Emperor of his lyffe and how holy he was the Emperor ba^ hem go to him and
than ke hem of her lyffe and so they deed and he prey de the knights to prey
Nicolas to thretyn the Emperor no more but prey to god for him and for his
reame and so they deed. Thus ye may see that he has great compassion of him
that where in dissese. Thanne after when seint Nicolas should dye he preyde to
god to send him an An gell to fette his soul. And when he saw this angel
come seint Nicolas lowted and said. In manua tu^^ domint commendo spi ritum
meum redemisti me domine dt no veritatis. And so he yield up the ghost. and
when he was bery^d at the he de of his tom be sprange a well of oil that deed
medicyns to all sores Thanne hit hap pyd many yeris after that turkys distroyed
the cite of mirre there as sein te nicolas lay and when the people of the cite
of Barus herd that the eite of mirre was distroyed. xlvij. knights where
ordeynd to go the dyr than they arayde shippis and went the thyr and be
tellyng of four monks that where left there they knew seint nicolas tomb and
vndede hit a none and there they found seint Nicolas bones swimming in oil
than they took hem up and brought hem to the cite of Barus with great
solempnite. Thanne for great miracles that where ^roughte there in the cite of
mirre encrefid ^yene And so after seint nicolas was deed they chose anothir
bishop in his stead and anon after by enmyte of the people he was put
down from his bishopriche and than anon the oil sesyd and ran no more.
Thanne was the bishop called ayene to hi(...) than the oil sprang^oute ayene
as hit deed to fore and deed many miracles.



There was a criston man borrowed a certain some of money of a jew and the Jew
said he would lene none but he had a borow. and this christian man said he had
none but seint nicolas and he granted to take seint nicolas to borow Than this
christian man s^ore up on the auter that he would well and trewly pay this money
ayeny and so departed and went her wey till day of payment come and when
this day was passyd than the i^we asked his money and this christian man seyde
that he had paid him and the jew seyde nay he had not. and that other
seyde he had and that he would do his law and swear up on a book And so
when the day come that they should go to the law the christian man made him an
holowe staff and put the gold there in and so come to the law. And when he
should swear while he went to the bo lie he took the Jew his staff there the
gold was ynne to hold. And by this mean swore he had paid the jew and when
he had sworn he took his staff of the jew a yene and went homewardes And
as he wen te by the wey he was pas sing slepy and he leyde him down to sleep
in the high weye Thanne hit happened there come a carte rennyng and went over
this man and slew him and brake his staff that the gold was ynne and the
gold fylle out. Thanne the people saw that this come of great vengeance for
the falshede that he had done And they fette the jew and bad him take up his
money. Thanne was the jew sorry and said he would not but if that they would
prey seinte nicolas to rere him ayene than he would be christian. ^eleuauit a
defuncti^ defunctum.

Thanne this deed man was reryd from death to lyffe by the preyour of seint
nicolas Baptisator auri viso indeus indicio Thanne this i^we that was out of
the believe by the fight of this miracle he was cristened.



Also there was anothyr jew that saw the great might of seint Nicolas in
miracles worthyng and he let make an image of seint Nicolas and set it in
his ship to keep his good and chargyd the image to keep well his good while
he was absent and when this man was gone there come theuys of the sea and
robbed this man and bare a wey his good And when this Jew come home ayene
and saw all his good gone he was full wroth with seint Nicolas and took a
staff and all to beat this image and seyde. Ecce omnia bo na mea posui in
veltra custodia Ioqd he I took all my good to your keeping for great trust and
hit is stole a wey ye have disseued me and there for thou shalt a bye every
day till y have my good ayene. Tha^ as these thieves departed the good seint
Nicolas come to hem and said Cur tam direct fe cistia me flagellari why have
ye made me be betyn thus sore Than they said Quia eatn what art thou that
spe^yste thus to us Than he said Ego sum Nicolaua seruua dei. I am Nicolas the
servant of god that ye have made thus sore be betyn and shewde hem how sore he
was betyn for the good that they had bor ne a wey that was taken him to keep
and he bad de hem goo and bear this good ayene a none or else goddys
vengeance shall fall one you and ye shall be hongyd in hell euerichone. Than
they were sore a ferde and bare ayene the good that same night And one the
morrow when the Jew come and saw his good brought ayene anon he was
cristenyd and after that he was an holy man And every year after on seinte
Nicolas day for the great love that he had to seint Niclas and alse of a sone
that he had de that was a clerk he made a great feste on seint Nicolas day
thanne hit happed on a time up one a seynte Nicolas day he badde many clerc^ys
to his feste Thanne come the find to the gate in ly kenesse of a pilgreme and
a shyd sum good for goddys sake. Thanne the good man that made the feste took
his sone elmesse to bear the pelgre me so the child went to the gate thanne
was the pelgreme gone And the child followed after the fend. And when he was
a good wey from his fadyris place the fend caughte the child and slew hit
And when the fadyr herd there of he was full sorry and took the child and
leyde hit in his chamber and tryde for sorrow and said a seint Nicolas is this
the reward and mede that I shall have for the great worship that I do to the
and anon the child rose from death to lyffe than this man was full glad and
thankyd god and seynte Nicolas.



Anothir miracle there was a man that preyde to god and to seint Nicolas that he
might have a child and if he had a child he would led hit to the church of
seynte Nicolas and there he would offer up a couppe of gold and than sone
after he had a child. And when this child was of reasonable age his fadyr
deed do make a couppe of gold And when hit was made hit likyd him so well
that he let make anothir and thanne he went toward seint Nicolas church
and he must pass over the sea. So when they were in the sea the fadyr badde
the sone take up some water with the couppe. And than the child would have
caught water and the couppe fill out of his hand in to the sea And than the
child would have caught the couppe ayene and fill after in to the sea and so
the child was drowned there in the sea. Thanne the fadyr made much sorrow but
yet he went forth with y^ other couppe to do his pilgremage And when he come
to seint Nicolas church and offerid up his couppe and set it on the Auter
anon hit was cast from the auter and he set hit ayene and hit was cast
ferther and yet the thride time he set te hit ayene and thanne hit was cast
much ferther Thanne come the child with y^ other couppe in his hand and said
to all the people that seint nicolas took him up by the hand when he fill in
to the sea and latte him save out. Thanne was the fadyr glad and of fered up
there both coupes and went home a yene with great joy and myrthe.



There was anothyr rich man that be preyores of seint Nicolas had a child
and he made a feyre chapel in worship of god and seint Nicolas. So hit
happed on a day this child was takyn wi^h enemies and ladde in to anothir
straynge country and there he was in service in the kings court And as it
happed on a seint Nicolas day he be thought him of the great myrthe and
solempnite that was made that day in his fadres chapel at home and he was heavy
and sikyd wounder sore. Thanne the hyng herd there of Thanne said the king
Nicolas what meneste thou to sight so sore be merry for thou must nedys a bide
here with us And anon there come a great wind and smote the house and braste
hit And the child was caughte up with the cup that he bare in his hand and
was set be fore the gate of the Chapel there as his fadyr made his feste.
Thanne was there made great joy and myrthe of this miracle. To thus ye may see
how great compassione that seint Nicolas had of hem that where in misheue and
dissese sum bokys say y^ this child was of Normandy and was takyn with a
sowdon be yonde the sea and often he was betyn. And ones when he was betyn up on
a seint Nicolas day and put in to preson than he wept sore And with that he
fell on sleep And when he woke he was in the church of his fadres.

De concepcione heat marie virginie.
Ood men and wymmen soche a day ye shall have the concepcion of our lady the
which day and feste holy church makythe mind and mention of the concepcion
of our lady for three special causes The first is for her fadres ho^lynesse
The secounde for her modres goodness And the thride for her meekness She
had a fadyr that was called Ioachym that was so holy a man that when he
was but.xv. winter of age he deparryth all his good in to three parties. And one
part he delyd to wedowes and to fadyrles children The secounde part he gave
to them that where pore and nedy. The thryde part he kepithe to him self and
his household And wha^ he was.xxxij. winter of age for the great goodness of
Anne he wedded her And when they where wedded they where to gedyr.xxij. year
in the which time Anne never displesed him with no manner thing nothir night
nothir day. For she was so gentle to him for they where both good and holy
yet god sent hem no fruit of her bodies but where bareyne. where fore they
made a vow to god that if he would send hem a child they would offered un to
him up to the temple for to serve god both night and day.

Thanne on a day as Ioachym went with his neyborus to the temple to do his
offerynges The bishop that highte Isachar whukyd him openly before all the
people and said Ioachym hit fallyth not for the that art bareyne and haste no
fruit to do offe rings with other people that god has sent fruit in
Jherusalem Than was Ioachym sore dysmayed and distonyed with this rebuke Than
he went home weeping and took his schepard preuely with his schepe and went
forth into a far country a mongt mounteynes and hyllis and purposid to have
be there all his lyffe and never more to come home to Anne his wyffe Thanne
when ioachym was gone Anne was sorry and preyde to god and said lord that me is
woo that I am bareyne and may have no fruit and now more my husbonde is gone
from me I wot not whethir he is be come lord have mercy on me. Thanne as she
preyde thus an angel come down and comforted her and seyde anne be of good
comfort for thou shall have a child in thine old age there was never none
like ne never shall be. Thanne was anne a ferde of this Angellys his word is
and of the ^ighte of him and lay all wey in her preyoures as she had be deed.
Thanne went the same Angel to Ioachym and seyde these same words and badde
Ioachym take a lamb and offyr hit in sacrifice to god and so he deed and
when he had done so from mydday till euensonge time he lay on the ground
in his preyoures thankyng god with all his heart. Thanne on the morrow as the
angel bad he went homewarde to Anne his wyffe with his sheep And when he
come nyghe home the Angel come to Anne and bad her goo to the gate that was
called the goldyn gate and a bide her husbonde there till he come. Thanne was
she glad and took her meydenes with her and went to the gate and there
schemette with ioachym and said lord I thank the for I was a wedowe and now
am a wyffe I was bareyne and now y shall have a child y was woo and weeping
and now y shall be in joy lykyng And sone after anne conseyued our lady And
when she was borne she was called mary as the angel badde be fore.

Than after that she was wenyd she was brought to the temple and left there
among other virgenys to serve god both night and day. Than was she so meke
among all other virgenys in all her leuyng that all virgenys cally^ her queen
of virgenys So she is the mekyste of all the seintes that be ^^ heaven and most
redye^^ to help all them that callith to her in any need.



we read in holy write a miracle of our lady.

There was a lordys man that had gaderyd much good of his lordys for he was
his rent gaderar and went to be re hit to his lord Than was there theses that
set for him to rob him by the weye in the wood there as he must nedys goo
thourghe So when he come in to the wode he be thought him that he had not
seyde our lady sauter as he was wont to do And he knelyd down and began to
sey. Thanne come our lady like a fair madyne and set a garlounde on his
head and at each aue she set a rose in the garlounde that was so bryghte that
all the wood shone there of and when he had done he kyssed the earth and
went his wey. Thanne come the theses and took him and led him to her maistre
the which had seyen all these doings than seyde he to him what woman was that
that set the garlaunde on thine head and he said ^irre for so the y sye no
woman ne garlaunde Than said these master these y wot well thou art a lordys
man and haste much good with the but y would feign wete what woman that hit
was that come to the and why thou knelyst down and he said when y sigh you y
was a ferde and also y be thought me that y had not said our lady sauter and
knelyd down to sey it preyng our lady to help me at my need than said he for
her love goo thy wey and prey to her for us and so he went his wey safe and
sound be help and socour of our dear lady.

But now ye shall here how this feste was first found. There was a king in
England that highte wyllyam conqueror he sent the abbot of ramsey to the king
of denemarke on his message and when he come in to the sea there come a
derkenes and a tempest that he and all that where with him went to have be
drowned. And every man preyde besyly to god and to our lady for socour and
help and other diverse seynt^s and this abbot preyde to god and to our lady
full deuotely Than come to hem a fair woman and said to them if ye woll have
the contepcione of our lady in worship that is.ij. days after seint nicolas
day she woll be ready to help and socour you at this time and than this abbot
said ye with good will and y woste what should be the service of the feste.
Thanne said she the same that is in the Natiuite safe turn the natiuite in to
the concepcion And the abbot seyde hit should be done with full good will. than
anon the tempest ^^ssed and all was well and they saylid forth and the Abbot
deed his message and come ayene safe and sound and spedde well in every degree.
And when he come home he told the king this vision the king made him preche it
in all the reame about

And thus hit was a lowed in all holy church.



Also we find that there was a seculer chanon that one a time went over a
water to have done a vowtrey with a woman And as he was a boute to be gynne to
sey our lady matenes and as he was at the inuitatory that is Aue maria there
with the fend cast him down and drowned him and would have had him to
hell. thanne come our lady and said why haste thou take this man the fend
said for we find him in our service going to do a vowtrey. tha^ said our
lady he was in my service and anon restorid him to lyffe again and bad him do
no more sin And bad him to halowe also her concepcion so he deed and was a
good man ever after all his lyffe.



Also there was a clerk that every day used to sey the service of our lady
thanne hit happid be council of his frendis he should have a wyffe and when
he should be wedded he be thought him that he had not said our lady
service. Than he made all the people to goo out of the church while he said
his service And thanne he knelyd a down and said his service till he come to
an antem of our lady Quam pulchra es amica mea. Thanne our lady aperyd un to
him and said why sayste thou that I am fair and honest why wit thou than
leave me and take anothir Thanne said he on to our lady what wolte thou that I
shall do thanne said our lady if thou wolte leave thy fleschely wyffe and serve
my sone and me I shall be thy spouse and thou shalt have with me a crown of
ever lastyng lyffe in the kingdom of ever ^astyng bliss the which god and
his blessed modyr saint mary and all holy seintys in heuene bring us all
thethir now and ever Amen.

Sequitur sermo breuis de sa^cto thoma apostolo.


GOod men and wymmen soche a day ye shall have saint thomas day that was
cristys apostell and ye shall fast the euyne and do him worship specially
for three causes The first for the preuyng of our believe And for great
wounderes in his wey And great miracles in his day. This holy apostell preued
so our feythe that he left no troble for when the disciples said that our
lord was resyn from death to live and they had seyne him and spoke with him
Thomas said he would not believe it till he had put his hand in to his side
in to the wound that the spear had made. Thanne.viij. days after when all
the disciples were to gedyr and Thomas wi^h hem Thanne our lord ihesu criste
come bodily to hem and seyde Par vobis Pees be with you and thanne our lord
said to Thomas of ynde. Mitte manum tuam in latus meum Put thy hand in to my
side in to the wound that was made with the spear that smote me to the heart.
Et noli esse incredulus. And be no longer out of the believe but be stead fast
in the feythe Thanne when thomas had do so a none he cried and seyde for
great woundre. Dominua meus et deus meus. my lord my god I believe that thou
art verry god and man.

Thanne our lord said to him Beatiqui crediderunt et non viderunt. blessed be
tho that believe and se not. for now thou haste seyn thou beleuiste but yet the
taryng of Thomas brought us to sadder believe and to the blessyng of our lord
ihesu criste Of this spekyth seynte Gregori and seyth thomas of ynde thou haste
help more to the feythe that woldeste not believe till thou haddiste felyd his
wound thanne did mary mawdeleyne that did believe at first sight M^nus est
enim in maria magdalene que cicius credidit quam Thomas qui diu dubitauit Thus
Thonas preued our feythe and our believe that we nedyd never to vary nor be in
dowte. Also thomas did many meruallys and great wounderys that were in his
days.



Hit happid that a king of ynde send his messenger Abbanus. In die requirens
artificium to seek sum crafty man in to the country of caesar to seek a
carpenter that could make him a palyse to his plesaunce Thanne our lord ihesu
criste mete with this abbanus and sent him to Thomas in to ynde also when
thomas and Abbanus were passed the sea they come in to a cite there as the
kings daughter was weddid the same day where fore all manner of people were
commaundid to mete so among other people thomas and abbanus come ynne and where
set to mete but thomas ete not for his thoghte was ever of god and had no
lust to ete Thanne come a botelere to thomas and smote thomas on the cheke and
bad him ete than said Thomas to him Non hunt surgam donec manus qui me
percussit a ^anibus affertur. I shall not rise from this place till that hand
that smote me be brought in with a dog Thanne anon after the Boteler went
after water and a lion met with him and flew him and drancke his blood and
ete of his body and than come a blake dog and caughde that hand that smote
thomas and brought hit in to the halle in the sight of all the people and
leyde hit down before thomas than was there a woman that understood thomas
wordis and anon knelyd down to thomas and cryde and said thou art god or
else on of his disciples for right as thou wolte so hit is thanne the king
preyde to thomas to bless his daughter and her husbonde. than thomas was
glad there of. Cepit ergo predicare beatus thomas. therefore the blessed thomas
be ganne to preche and told hem of our ihesu criste that he turned the man
that was weddyd the same day from his wyffe and made him bishop of the same
cite and his wyffe a nonne and they were marterys after for cristys sake Thanne
went thomas forth in to ynde to the king to make him a paleyse to his
plesaunce so when thomas was come to the king he was glad and delyueryd
Thomas a great sum of gold to make a paleyse with. than rode the king forth
in the mean time And so when thomas should have made this paleyse him thought
hit was better to make a paleyse in heaven than in er^h and delyd his gold a
mong pore people and co^uertyd hem to the feyth Thanne come the king home and
went that his paleyse had be ready made And when he herd how Thomas and
Abbanus had done he would have put hem to death but hit happid that his
own brothir was deed the same time and therefore he put hem both in prison
in to the time that he had beryed his brothir Thanne as god would when his
brothir had long lay deed he rose from death to life and told the king that he
had seyne his paleyse in paradyse that thomas had made for him and preyde the
king that he might have hit and he would give him as much gold as he took
thomas Thanne the king took his counsel and said nay I w^ll have it my self
let him make the anothir for his brothir had seyne this paleyce in paradyse
made with gold and ^rayed with precious stones and clothe of gold. Thanne the
king took cristendome and many a thousend with him and when the bishops saw
that the king and so much other people for soke her lawus and turned to
cristondome they where so wroth with thomas that one of them seyde he would
venge his god and with a spear smote thomes thourghe the body and slew him
Than christian people beryed him in a tomb of cristall and there god wot
wroughte many miracles for him For the hand that was in cristys side would
never come in to the tomb but ever lay with out Also in his techyng and
prechyng he taught Duodecim gdua virtutum assignare Primua est vt in deum
crederent ^ui est vnua in essencia et trinua in personi^. Dedit eis triplex
exemplum se^sibile quomodo sint indiuidencia vna* tre^ person* Primum est quia
vna e^ in homine sa^ie^cia et de vna procedit intellectus. memoria et ingenium
memoria est vt non obliuiscaria in tellecto. vt intelligas que ostendi possunt
vel doceri ingenium est vt quod didiceri^ inuenias Secundum est quia in vna
vinea tria sunt lignum folium et fructus. Et her omnia tria sunt vinea. Tercium
est quia caput nostrum ex quatuor sencibu^ constat In vno autem capite sunt
Disu^ a^ditua adoratu^ et gustus et hec plurasunt et tame^ vnum caput. Secundus
gradua est vt baptismum suscipiat. Terciu^ gradus e^ vt a fornicacione
abstineat. Quartu^ vt se ab auaricia teperet. Quintua vt gulam distringeret.
Sertu^ vt penit^ciam teneret Septimus vt in hiis perseuerarent Ocrauns vt
hospita litate^ amarent. Nonus vt volu^tate^ dei requira^t Decimu^ est vt
facienda quererent Vndecimu^ vt caritate^ amicia et innimici^ impendere^t
Duodecimu^ est vt custodia^thiia vigile^ curam exhiherent Item apostalus Omnea
qui oderant deum de tribus breuiter instruxit scilicet vt ecclesiam diligerent
Sacerdotes honora rent Et assidue adverhum dei conuenirent. Also there be many
marvelous and wondre full things done on this day for on that day all the
country comythe the dyr to take pardone of that hand that lythe out of the
tomb in the use of the bishop of the cite that gothe to mass. And when he
has said Confite or thanne he takyth a branche of a vine and put hit in to
thomas hand that is out of the tomb and than he gothe forth to mass and
the branche burgeneth out grapus and be that time the gospel be said the
grapis be ripe than the bishop takythe the grapis and wryngith the wine in the
chales and so singith with the same wine and hoselyth the people. and when any
man or woman comythe that is not worthy to receive this hosell anon the hand
closithe to gedyr and will not opyn till he be shreuen clean and than hit will
opyn Also if any people be in debate they shall be brought be fore thomas
tomb and there the cause shall be rehearsed than woll the hand turn to him
that is in the right and so they be made at one. Thus thomas preuith our
believe and did many wyntres in his days. Also johan crisostomus seythe that
thomas come in to the country there as the three kings of coleyn were and
thomas cristened hem for they had worshippyd god in his birth And there fore
thomas come to hem and taught hem the feythe and the believe of criste to that
believe that we may be sauyd god bring us all Amen.

De natiuitate domini nostri Ihesu cristi.
GOod men and wymmen as ye heryn and seyn as holy church makyth mind and
mention of the great myrthe and me lodye of the blessed birth of our lord
ihesu crist very god and man that was this day borne of his modyr mary in
socour of all man kind But in e special for three causis First to give pese
to man of good will and to light hem that were darcke in sin and for to
draw us with love to him. Thanne as to the first cause he was borne to give
men peese of good will I may well preue this for when he was borne angellys
songhe thus Gloria in excelsia deo etc. Joy be to god in heaven and pese in
earth to man kind of good will At midnighte our lord was borne for be kind all
thing was in pees and rest inshewyng that he was and is Princepa pacia Prince
of peese and come to make pees be twyxe god and man and be twyxe the angel and
man and be twyx man and man And for to be true mediator be twyx god and man he
took nature and kind of both and was both verray god and man and by his
mediacion he knette the love of god to man so saddely that the fadyr of heuyn
spared not him that is his own but sent him in to this world to bye man
kind with his precious blood thourghe his great meekness to joy of paradyse
that man had lost be couetyse of vnbuxsumnes.

Thus he made pees be twyx god and man and man and man. for when angeles say
her lord wroth with man for his vnbursumnes for it is a sin that angeles
hatyn greatly. There fore they kept the gatys of paradyse and would let no
soul come ynne till they say her lord borne of man kind Thanne a none for
love of our lord the angels did mankind worship and spoke goodly to mankind
as to the sheperdys that keptyn her sheep in the country by They bad hem go to
the cite of Bethlem and there they should find a child borne and leyde in a
crache and bad hem do him worship and so they dedyn And ever syn angelys have been frendely to man and lowly end have done reverence to mankind for the
incarnacion of our lord ihesu criste. Thus he made pees between angelys and
man Also he made pees between man and man for a yene the time that our lord
would be borne he made so great pees that in all the world there as kingdoms
and countries were in debate and werred each with othyr on to the time of our
lordis birthe. Than there was so great pees that a man that was called octauian
Emperor of rome and he had the governance of the world for all the world
was subiete to rome and hit dured. xxx. winter in so much that there was a
mau^ment sent out from rome in to all the world comaundyng to all manner of
people should go to the cite that he drew lynage of and ley a penny upon his head
and so offer hit up in knolechyng that he was sogette to the Emperor of rome.
Than must Joseph our ladies husbonde nedys go to the cite of Bethleem for to
offer with other people but for he had no money to offer he took an ox with him
to selle at the cite to make money to do his de^te with but for he durst not
leave our lady be hynde him for she was nyghe her time. And there fore he set
her upon an ass and took her with him. And so when they come to the cite of
Bethleem hit was so full of people so that Joseph and our lady might have no
logyng but turned in to a cabon that was made betwyxse two houses there as the
people of the country set her horses and their asses and other bestis when
they come in to the town to the markette and so there they found a crache
with hey And they set the ox and the ass there to and so there they tarried
all that night. And when hit was a little be fore mydnyght our lady badde
Joseph goo in the town and look her for a myddewyffe when the time was come
she should be delivered(...) asked her where there should after him any be borne
that should be gretter than he Thanne at myd day Sybill looked in the son and
there she say a cercle of gold a boute the son Et in medio circuli virgo
pulch errima And the myd dys of the cercle a fair maiden and a child in her
arm with a crown of gold And when sibyll had shewid this to the Emperor she
said to him this child shall be gretter than those art or ever were or ever
shall be and there fore do him worship and reverence Than a none the emperor
took ensence and deed worship to him and charged all the people to do the
same and to call the child her god and him but a man as other were. Thus all
christian people may learn to do worship and service to this child this day
And there fore the third mass this day is said at myd day in tokenyng that
christian people should come and offer in the worship of this child and his
modyr and shown him servant and suget to him and knoleche this child for his
lord and his god and each man should come to him for love and not for dread And
there fore the office of the mass this day begins thus Puer natus est nohis.
A child is borne to us he seyth and not a man for all christian people should be
bold and not a ferde to come to him to have grace for he is full of grace and
ready to give mercy to hem that askith hit mekely with dew reverence he is ever
ready to give mercy and grace.

In tokenyng that same day that crist was borne in Bethleem a well of water in
rome turned and ran oil all that day showing that the well of grace and
mercy was borne that day that should give mercy and grace to all them that
would come to him and ask mercy and grace and that ye shall here be ensample.



we read of a woman that was defowled in lechery and all most fill in dispayr
of dread. for when she be thought her of the streytenesse of cristes dome
and the gre^^ horrible peynes of hell that were ordained for soche sinners as
she was ^or^ a ferde and be thought her of cristes passion what love he show
de to all christian people she thought she was vnkyn de to him and he sufferid
so sore for h^^ And than she be thought her how children be they never so
wroth and show never so great vengeance how lightly they woll sese and for
give where fore this woman a none cryde to Criste preyng him for his child he
de to for give her and to have mercy on her and a none she herd a voice an
high in the air and said thy trespass is for yeuen the Amen.

Sequitur ^^^uis sermo de sa^rto stephano.


GOod men and wymmen soche a day ye shall have an high day and a holy feste
in the church of seint Stephen the martyr the which was the first martyr
that suffered death for goddis sake after cristes ascension. Than for to stere
your devotion the more to this holy martyr. I will tell you sum what that
he suffered for cristes sake as the book of apostlys tellyth Post ascensionem
domini. after the ascension of our lord that he was styed^vp in heaven the
apostlys labor was all to preche and to teache the word of god to christian
people And for they where to few to serve all the people that rome. there come
so many to turn to the feyth there for they chose.vi. holy men and good
lyuers for to help hem in goddis service of the which seint stephen was one
of hem and the first and the wyseste and was so full of grace and might of the
holy ghost that he did many miracles and marvelous among the people. But
though a man be never so holy ^it he shall have enemies wherefore of diverse
countries that had enmyte to stephene and come ayene him and disputed with
him for to have over come him with disputacion and for they might not they
brought false wyttenesse against him to put him to death But when seynte
Stephene saw and know her malice anon he thought to sese hem be on of these
three weyes other be shamyng in disputacion or be dread of reuolacion or be
preyours of holy orysones. But first he said be shamyngm disputacione For
when they be gonne to dispute with him he was so full of the holy ghost that
they had no pour nor no might for to a gayn sey him And so he over come hem
in all her matters and preued all her matters false that they seyde ayenste And
there for he said he was ready to take the death in very fiyng of all that he
said And so put hem that where great clerks and knew the law and the
prophecy to great shame and velonye. But yet they would not leave but alwey
ayene stood him.

But he was so full of the holy ghost that he preued that he said be great
reason and truth yet would not they be leave it for all that the holy ghost
spoke in heart and yet for all that would not they believe in their concience
that they deed a mysse and there as they seyne the co^mynte turn to the feyth
for wordys and miracles that god showed in her sight yet they again stood him
and set goddis miracles at naught be malice and enmyte of her cursed hertes
and by none other reason of scripture. And so they fretid her hertis withyn him
self and grugged with her tethe for anger and how that they might over come
him with disputacion Than they sought if they might have take him with some
word of Cristes death where by they might have made them a cause to have
put him to death Thanne seynte stephene knew her malice and lift up his
eyes into heaven Et vidit celos apertos And he saw heuyn opyn and our lord ihe
su criste sittyng on his fadyr right hand ready to help him. And there with
his face shone as bryghte as it had be an angel of heaven But when they herd
him speak tha^ where they feign and stoped her erys as though they had herd
him speak false sclaundre of god and so a none drow him out of the cite to
stone him to death as for adisclaunderer Thanne they took.ij. young men that
cowde best hurl stones and took of his clothis and leyde him at the fete of a
young man that hight Saul and after was saint paul Than when saint stephen
saw that he might not sese her malice be reuelacione showing he turned to
devout oryson preyng and yet hit would not be And than they hurled stones at
him and smote out his brain and thanne he cried to god and said Domine i^e su
suscipe spm^ meu^ O thou lord take my spirit for he would prey more de^outly
for his enemies than for him self he knelyd down to the ground and seyde
Pater ig nosce illis quia nesciunt quid faciunt. Fadyr for give hem for they
wot not what they do and anon he slepte in god. Now take he de what brennyng
love he had in his heart to god that preyde more devoutly for his enemies
thanne for him self In this he gave an ensample to all christian people to be in
charity echon with other and to prey for his enemies and hem that pursewe him
and do him dissese ^ni^ersa delicta cooperiit caritas Charity hidith every
trespass for he y^ preyth for his enemies that martyr him with any dissese and
sufferyth patiently he is a martyr be fore god For there is* iij. manner of
martyrdome^. The first is be passion and will there to be will with out
passione be passione with out will The first is shewid by saint stephene that
is set next the birthe of criste for he sufferyth passione and had will
there to saint Johan the euan geliste he had will but no passione The
innocents they suffered passion and no will there to but not against will Thus
may a man be a martyr though he shede not his blood that is when he suffered
great wrong of cursed people and thankyth god there of and takyth hit with good
will and preyth for his enemies devoutly in clean charity Now take heed and ye
shall se how these.iij. where in per^ite love and charity Seint stephen when he
should dye he knelyd down and preyde for his enemies Seint Johan when he
went to war dys his end he said often to hem that ladde him children love to
gedyr for charity is now to salvation The innocents for they were so young
that they cowde not speak yet they shewde love be signs for the deed laughe
and pleyde with her hondes when they saw the knights come with her brighte
s^erd^s to sle hem. than for seint stephyn was so glorious a martyr god shewde
many fair miracles for him.



There was an honest man that had vij. sons and iij. doughtres but in mysse
hap on a day all they wrathyd the modir at ones and in a great anger she
cursed hem all at ones and a none there ^ill great vengeance upon hem for
there come soche a sikenesse one her preuy members that they were so for gnawyn
that they might nethir a bide for woo but walkithe up and down in the
country like mased bestis that all the people that saw hem had great ^ite of
hem

Thanne happid hit so that one of the breshere^ that highte paul and a sustyr
highte palida come in to church of seint stephyn and there they herd people
tell how devoutly seint stephen preyde for his enemies y^ martred him a none
they kneled down and preyde to seint stephene to prey to god for hem and they
would be his true servants and kneled down in the church preyng seint
stephene hertely of his help and a none they fill a sleep in sight of all the
people and so were hole. And an on they went aftyr all her other brethren and
^usteren and they were hol pyn all in the same wise



Anothir miracle seint Austyn tellith how there was a senator of rom^ went to
iherusalem and there he made a fayrt chapel of seint stephen and there he dyed
and was ^eried in the same chapel. Than long aftyr his wyffe would home in to
her country and would feign have had her housbondes bones with her in to her
own country and preyde the bishop that she might have hem

Than the bishopp^ brought seint stephenes bones and her housbondes bones to
her and seyde y know not thy housbondes bones from seint stephenes bones and
she was glad and said I know my housbondes bones well y now and took seint
stephen bones in s^ede of her husbo^des Than when she come fer in the sea
angeles song with great melody in the air and there was a passing s^^ete
sauoure y^ come out from the bone that passid any spicety in the world. And a
none they herd fendes cry in the air and said woe woe is us for stephen
be*dithe us and burnyth us bitterly and there with reysid a great tempest^ that
the shippemen wend for to have be drowned for great fere cry*d to seint
stephen and a none the tempeste ses^d Than the people herd the fendes cry
thus thou cursed prince our mastir thou nor we may do n^ne harm to this
shipp^ for stephen our adversary is ^herynne Than the prince of fendes sent
v. fendes for to have burnyd the shipp* but thanne goddis angel was ready and
drowned the fendes in the ground of the s^e And so wha^ they come to the land
with the ship fendes cried and seyde goddis servant comythe that was stoned
to death with the iewis And than in worship of saint stephene the people made
a church and leyde his bones ^her ynne where god wrought many a fair miracle
for him.

De sancto io^a^ne euangeliste.


GOod friend is soche a day ye shall have an high feste in holy church the
^este of seynte Johan euangeliste the which was goddis own d^rlyng. where for
all holy church makithe mind and mention of the specialte that once lord
gaffe to him for any other of his disciples Our lord gaffe him grace to keep
his ^ ginite and of keeping of his modir and our lord shewde him his prynyte He
gaffe him grace to keep his virginite that is maydynhode. For this story
tellith and the people have opynned when johan should wedde mari maudeleyne
criste callidr him and he come and sero^d him and johan left the worlds vamte
and sewed our lord and so kept him self clean maiden till he passid out of
this world In preuyng of this when Domician the Emperor of Rome herd the
people tell that johan preched in a country that was callid asia and there
johan made to bilde many churches and when the Emperor herd that he sent
aftyr Johan and made him be put in a brayson tonne full of sethyng oil. and
when Johan had long sodyn there ynne that all the people wend that he had
be all to sodyn and deed Thanne the Emperor badde opyn the tonne and when the
tonne was opyn Johan come out of the tonne and as ^e was clean of all sin so
was he clean of all manner of b^ennyng or harm in all parties of his body. A
nothir hard tourme^t he had on a day Johan saw a temple of jews and was full
of mawmentry and than he preyde to god to distroye hit and a none there with
hit fill down to the ground ^all to powdyr. where fore Aristodimus the
bishop of the temple was so wroth that he put Johan in to prison Thanne
seyde johan yet wolte thou that y shall make the believe in ihesu criste Than
seyde aristo dimus y woll mak^ venym and make hit drink be fore the and when
thou seyste hem deed drink thou there of with out harm and than woll I
believe on thy god than seid ioha^ go and do as thou seyste tha^ ordained the
bishopp^ poison and fette ij. me^ out prison that were dampened to drink of
the poison and anon they were deed tha^ seyde johan if thou give venym to
drink y shall call to my god And than Johan took this poison and blessid hit
and drank there of and he was never the worse but rathir semyd the bettyr and
the fayrer for as he was clean from sin so he was clean from all grenaunce of
the poison yet seyde the bishop he would not believe un to the time he had
seyne these ij. men ar^rid from death to lyffe that where deed. Thanne johan
cast of his cote and seyde Dade et mitte ^a^c tunicam super corpora
defunctorum. Goo and ley this cote upon the deed bodies and sey thus Ihesu
cristus apostell sent me to you and bad that ye should a rise up in goddis
name and a none they resyn to lyffe ayene. Than the bishop with many other
turned and believed in criste and johan cristoned hem and aftyr the bishop
was a full holy man Thus johan had grace to kept him clean both body and
soul and thus he was a martyr to fore god in with stondyng of sin Also he
was keeper of cristus modir for our lord saw the great clennesse that was in
Johan be fore all other when our lord should dye he seyde to Johan. Ecce
matter tua. See thy modyr and be took Johan the keeping of his modir and our
lord seyde to his modir Ecce filins tuns Se thy sone and so be took eythir to
other and when our lord was deed and ley in his tomb Johan took our lady
home with him in to his house and kept her till our lord ^hesu criste was a
reyson from death to lyffe a yen And when our lord was stied up in to heaven he
kept our lady in the same chamber as long as she leuyd aftyr thus he had
grace of keeping of goddis modir Also he had grace of knowing of cristus
p^uite for this was furste wha^ our lord sat at his soper on sherthursday for
great love that johan had to our lord Ihesu criste he leyde his he de to
cristus breast and in the same wise as a man leythe his body down to a well
and drynkithe his body full of water right so johan drank his soull full of
gostly wisdom at cristus breast and at the same time our lord showed him all
his priuyte be fore all other. And for he was old and would not leave to p^che

of dome and as he saw hit he wrote hit in great fermacion of holy church But
aftyr wh^ he Emperor was deed Johan was callid again in to the Cite of Emphesie
for there he was Bishop and he come the dyr. And there was a wedowe that
highte drusiana was deed and leyde on a bear Thanne Johan saw much people
weep for her and thanne he seyde Drusiana arise up and make me sum mete and
anon she rose and went for ^he as she had rose from sleep



Hit happid on a time there were ij. young men be prechyng of joha^ they sold
all the good that they had and went forth with Johan for they were rich
men tha^ on a day as they come to the Cite of Pargame they that were her

were ynne to serve god but go ye to the wode and ethyr of you bring with him a
board on of small yerdys and so they deed. Than thourghe the preyour of Johan

I bid the tell these ij. men what thou haste seyne and what joy was ordained
for hem and how they have lost hit. And thanne the man told of the joy of
paradyse and of the peynes of purgatory and of hell how strong and how

her good angellis were for they had lost that glorious bliss of heaven and

sorry and cryde to johan and preyde him to prey to god for hem and wept sore
and johan saw hem we^e he preyde to god for hem and yaffe hem penannce and
when he had do so anon the gold turned in to yerdis a yene and aftyr they
were holy men.



A nothir holy reuelacion Johan had shewde by the preuyte of god hit happid
one a day he saw a child that was li ke to have be a man where for Johan

In fide essetia sta hiles et in mandatia dei feruentea Be ye stable and sad in

that no man might se him And when this light was gone the grane was full of
manna and wellid up a^ does sonde in the watyr And thus he departid out of
this world into the bliss of heuene that never shall have end to that bliss
bring us all to he that did on the rode t^^^ for all mankind Amen

Sanctorum inno ^^^tum


GOod frendys ^^ che a day is callid Innocents day sum people ca^le but
children mass day for children were slayue that day for Cristus sak they be
callid innocents that is to sey with out sin for they deed no syn for god
is ever gretely (...) with sin and in special with proud people ^ yense her
neybo^^es doing hem wrong These innocents deed never syn^s ^^ ^onsentyng to
sin where for I may well s^y that they leuyd here with out shame and d^^d
with out blame and were cristoned in her own blood at home and sum in her*
moderes arms. Holy church as this day singithe and redithe in the worship
of these innoce^tes for they were with ynne ij. year of age and there for they
were not a shamed of her own shappe for they were not defowled with no manner
spotte of sin. but the sin that they had of the drawte of kind of our
fadyr Adam and Eve. For Adam and Eve were in the same wise in paradyse the
state of innocentrie fore they where nakyd but they were not ashamed of her
shappe all the while the were with out syn but as soon as they had do sin
anon they saw her own shappe and were ashamed there of and covered her shapp^
with leuys of a fig tree Right so when synn begynnyth to take roode in a
child than innnocensie gothe a wey from him for he kno with good from ille
and ille from good and leuith the good and does ille than he synnethe and than
he is not innocent no longer for thanne greuithe he god. But these children
leuyd not so long to know that on from that other but were slain with ynne
age of innocentrie where fore they leuyd her lyffe with out shame and blame
For king herowde the king of iewis made to sle hem with out gylte. For when
the iij. kyngis come to king herowde and seyde to him Obi est ^ni natua e^ re^
indeorum where is he that is home king of ^e wis and badde him tell hem for
they were come to worshipp^ him fer out of the Este. Thanne wa^ king herowde
foul a stoyned of her word is and asked his clerkys where this child should
be borne and they seyde in Bethleem inde And thanne king herowde told hem so
and bad hem goo thethir and worship him and come again by me that I may go and
worship him. also and so the kings went thethir and worshippid criste and
when they had done here offerynges to criste Per aliam ni^ reuersi sunt in
regionem suam By an other wey they turned home again For the Angel bad hem do
so in her sleep Than was king herowde wondyr wroth and anon ordained to sle
ceiste and when he had made all ready there to hit happid so that the Emperor
of rome sent aftyr him for to come to him in all the haste y^ he might for.n.
of his own sons had accusid him to the Emperor of treson Than herowde
left all his purpose of criste as at that time and rode to rome and had the
better of his sons and come home again with more worship than he had to
fore But yet he thought all wey to sle criste left criste had come to
man's astate and would have put him out of his kingdom. Than sent he a
none and had sle all the children that were in Bethleem and in all the country
a houte that were with in ij. year of age and that were borne same day and so
they deed. For king herowde was going and coming and so taryyng ij. year and
there for he made sle all that ever were with ynne ij. year of age And for he
was so vengable in party hit fill on him self for a child of his own was
slain among other the same time But there come an Angel to Joseph and seyde
to him Accipe puerum et matrem eius et fuge in egiptum Take the child and his
modir and fle in to egipte and be there and so he deed Thus innoce^tes were
slain with out blame and they were not ashamed of their own shappe and they
were cristoned at home in her own blood and not in no font. There fore ye
shall vndyrstonde that there is three manner of cristonyng One is in water as we
be cristonyd in the font Anothir is as these children were cristoned in her
own blood and a thousand martirres mo that shed her blood for cristus sake
The iij. cristonyng is in the feith in the which all patriarchs and prophets
and othyr holy faderis that were before the incarnacione of our lord ihesu
criste y^ believed verily in the coming of crisce the were cristoned in the
feythe Thus ye may see what enmyte this tir^unt king herowde had to shede so
many childerens blood for cristus sake that trespaced not to him nor to none
other. There wept many a modir for there children at that time but god wroughte
full feyre for hem and that tyraunte shewde enmyte and hit fille on him self
for as he partyd an appell with the same knyffe he slew him self Thus he was
glad to shede blood giltelese. and there for at the last he shed his own,
blood.

For he that is with out mercy and ever vengeable often time vengeance fall
lithe on him self And he that loves to do mercy shall have mercy.

And this I may preue by ensample.



We find in the lyffe of seint Siluestre how Co^stantyne the Emperor was
mesell and by counsel of his lechis he made to gadyr iij. thousand children
for to be sleyne and all her blood should be gadered in to a^ ssell and the
Emperor should be ^athi^ all hot there ynne till hit were ^olde. Than these
children were gadered in to a place and the emperor come ridyng in his chair.
but when he come nyghe there as the moderes of the children were the moderis of
the children weptyn and cry ^ din and made great weyme^ tacion on the Emperor
and made a derefull noise. Than asked the emperor what women they were that
made that wey mentacion and the people seyde they were the moderis of the
children y^ should ^e deed for to hele him Than seyde the Emperor hit where a
delefull deed of us all to make thus many to be slain that be fair bodies to
hele on foul body and I am but one man as anothir is and many of these her
aftyr may be full good men and worthy and sto^de the Emperor in good stead.
^ay seyde the emperor I woll not do so but late every woman take her child a
yen home with her for they shall not be deed for me. And tha^ were the wymmen
glad and merry and took her children with great joy to hem and went home. Than
the night aftyr as this emperor lay in his ^edde Petyr and poule come to him
and seyde for the great compassion and pite y^ thou haddiste on the wyme^ and
her children there for send aftyr seint Siluestre and ^e criston and thou
shalt be hole and so he deed and as soon as he was cristoned the lepre fill in
to the water and he was clean fair and hole. Thus ye may see how he that woll
do mercy shall have mercy and they that does vengeance shall have vengeance
So did herowde vengeance and hit fill upon him self and Constantyne the
Emperor did mercy and he had mercy and grace I hope for ever more and so must
we all Amen

De sancto thoma epo^ Ca^tuarien^.


GOod men and wymmen soche a day ye shall have se^^t Thomas day that was slain
for the right of holy church and the law of this land. This holy man
seint thomas was borne in the Cite of london and his ^adir was callid Gilbert
that was shryue of london. Than aftyrward he ordained him self and yode in to
(...)e holy land and there (...) was take and put in p(...) Than come a
worshippefull woman to him and sryde yif he would ^lighte her his truth to
wedde her she would help him and bring him out of dissese and he deed so Tha^
come gilbert home in to England and when this woman saw her time she come
aftyr and met in london at the church of poules Tha^ Gilbert made the
bishop^ to criston her and aftir ward for to wedde hem to gedyr and gilbert
gate seint Thomas on this woman. So when scho was with child she dremyd in a
night that she come to seint poules church but when she would have gone ynne
she thought her womb was so great that she might not in to the church by no
wey Thanne on the mo row she went ^n to her confessor and told him all the
dreme than seyde he dame be glad and thank god highely for thou haste a child
in thy body that all holy church shall be to litill to resceyue him Thanne was
she glad and thankyd god highely and so sone aftyr this child was borne and
was callid thomas. tha^ he wexed a man and so he was a man in all degree for he
served the king manly and served god worthily and deyde fore the lewis of holy church mekely I may well sey he served the king manly for when he was made
chaunceler of En glond this land was so full of outeland men and so sore over
set with he^ that there might no man goo by the wey un robbed. But in short^
time aftyr Thomas with his wisdom and his manhood he drofe them out of this
land that all the people might goo un robbed. Thomas wa^ also manly in
repeyryng of the kings maneres that were let down and destroyed and in
special the kings paleyse in london at westmestre that was all let fall
down But between Estye and witsonty de thomas made to repair hit a yene for
he had there so many workmen of diverse craftys that a man should onethe
here his fellow speak for donnyng of strokys. He was also manly in dedis of
arms for there as the king had many Castellis and towns out of his hondis
and he spe^te much good to get them and shed much blood for get hem a
yene at the furste and they were hold out of his hondis Than thomas with his
wit and wisdom get hem a yene Also when he was in the kings werres of
france he quyte him so manly that when the king of england had exiled thomas
the king of france was his chief help and socoure Also thomas was as manfull
in his array for he was clothyd in the best and richeste clothe and furre that
might be found And also his repair to his hose sadeles brydele s^hon^ as
bryghte as any silver he was also manfull in his household for hi^ hall was
every day in some^ cheson strawed with gr^ne ruschis And in winter with clean
hey fore to save the knights clothis that sat in the flore for de ^awte of
place to sit o^ for there come so many every day to ete of his mete and
drink for he would have of all manner of deyntes that might he found in thi^
land

In so much that the king him self many time vnwarned come to Thomas to mete
both for love that he had to Thomas and also to see the array and also revel
that was in thomas household for there sp^ke so much people worship by
Thomas. And where fore more trewer and also better love that thanne was between
the king and thomas while hit last was never between to men. where for I put
this ensample Hit happid that hit fill in a cold winter as the king and Thomas
come rydyng to gedyr in to chepe side at london the king was ware of a poor man
that was well nere nakyd and had no clothis and was sore a cold Thanne said
the king to thomas hit were a great alms deed to give to this poor man betyr
clothes Sire seid thomas of soche ye should take heed Thanne had thomas on a
clothe of good scarlet and well furryd with rich furre than the king leyde
ho^de on this clothe and would have pullid hit from thomas for to have give it
to this poor man but thomas held hit fast and thus they wrastelid long in so
much that they were like to fulle to the ground. but at the last be favor
thomas suffered the king to take his clothe of and than the king cast hit to
the poor man and bad him run a wey fast and selle hit and bey him other and
if thou be set hit well thou may fare the better ever whiles thou leuyste
Than thomas feigned him self wroth but in his heart he was well a paid that
his roue was so well befette Thanne the people meruelyd gretely furste what was
between the king and thomas but when they saw what hit mened the people were
glad and had great sport there of. This I sey to show ensample how well they
louyd to gedyr thus thomas served the king manfully. also we must learn of
our holy patron seynte thomas to serve god deuoutely. when he served god
full devoutly for as soon as he was made arch bishop of Caunterbury a none he
turned his leuyng in to better leuyng and thought to serve the king of heaven
as well as he had the king of this world be fore. Thanne a none he leyde a
wey scarlet and rich furrys and wered clothe of myddell pryse and cast a wey
silk and send^ll and weryd here next his body that was right hard and a
bryche of the same hame side in the which was so much vermyn that hit was an
horrible sight to see but this know but litill people. Also every wedenysday
and freyday he made his confessoure to beat him with a rod on the bare body
like as a child is beat in scole Also he vsid every day to wesche ttre pore
men's fete knelyng one the ground and thanne he yaffe each of hem four
pennys And also much more penance he vsid in preyng and wakyng that were to
much to tell at this time. Thanne when thomas was in the abbey of pou^teney
upon a day whann he had seyde mass he knelid down be for the Auter in his
preyour^s than the Abbote of the same place had to speak with him and stood
vndyr a pilour and abode thomas And he saw how our lord The s^ criste
appeared to Thomas and told him how he should be slain in canterbury in his
own church for his sake and bad him be steadfast and hold forth as he had
be gonne Than come thomas out of his chapel and a none the Abbot fill down
to the ground and Sire ye may bliss the time and the hour that ever ye were y
borne and also blessid mute sho be that ever did bear you for to have soche a
visitacione as I have herd you have.

Thanne se^de thomas I charge the that thou tell hit never to no man while y am
a live no more he deed but when thomas was deed he told it opynly to all the

to over set holy church and soche law is as would have destroid the land.
Than thomas put him self forth and repreuyd the king of his miss dedis
