found hem all most vij year all that they be houyd Thanne great disseses and
greuaunces thomas had of the king of england and all he suffered mekely Than by

Ego pro deo mori parat^^ sin et pro defensione iusticie et ecclesie liberate
I am ready to dye for the love of god and for the fredomme and right of holy

and set his foot to thomas neck and thruste out the brain upon the pam ^t
Thus for right of holoy church and the law of the lord thomas took his

Thanne how this marterdome was known in iherusalem ye shall here. there was an
abbey of monks in the which that same day and the same time that thomas dyed
a monk lay at the death than for he was a good holy man of leuyng his abbote
bad him if hit were not to god displesaunce wha^ he were deed he should come a
yene and tell him how he ferde and so when he was deed he come again and told
his abbot when he dyed an angel brought him be fore god and as he stood there
he saw a bishop come with a great company of angeles and other seintes and
he stood be fore god at his iug^^ment and his head droppid down of blood of
wounds that he had* tha^ seid our lord to him thus hit be semythe a man to

grant the And the monk seid here by I know well that this is the grettiste

men



Also there was a bird that was taught to speak and cowde sey seinte thomas as
she had her de other pilgremes speak much of seint thomas and it happid on a
time this birdde sat with out his cage and there come a sparhawke and would

this sparhauke fill down deed than seint thomas of his great grace and
goodness herd the birdde and woste not what she men te much more he would have
herd and much sonner he would here a criste^ man or christian woman yt cried
hertely to him* for help and socour



Also there was a man that thomas loved passing well in his lyffe. and hit fill

De circumcisio^e domini.


GOod frendis so che a day is callid new yeris day and is the first day of the
beginning of the New year that is coming and is the last day of the year that
is gone. And there fore this day ye shall come to god and holy church to here
your deuyne service forth this year. For like as a good servant that has a
good mastir makithe his comenaunt but ones but holdithe forth from year to
year having full trust in his maistre that he woll for his good service yeffe
him a good toward in his great need at his last end. In the same wise goddis
seruauntis makythe comenaunte with him ones yt is at cristonyng at the founte
and there he makythe comenaunte to be goddis servant having full trust in god
that at his great need that is at the day of dome quyte him for his service
in ever lastyng bliss of heuene and so woll he do to all that be good true
servants Thus this day is called new yeris day.

Also hit is callid Circumcisi^ ^^mini the circumcision ^^ our lord

Also this day is callid new yeris day for this day is the first day of the ka
lendyr and the year gothe much he kalendyr there for his is callid new yeris
day Seinte Austein seith this day and this night he thyn people use many false
opynions and wyche craftys and false be leave the which be not to tell among
christian people les te they turned to that use where fore ye that be criste^
people be well were left ye be desceyued be any false so^ery as be taking
counsel of on man be fore a nothir or in being or sellyng or in borowyng or
senyng in the which sum have diverse opimons. And if they be well shreuyn
they be worthy for to have great penance for there miss believe for that
comythe of the fend and not of god This day is callid the circumcisione of
our lord for as holy chuche tellith this day he was circumsised and blede his
blood for our sake for when the flesche was cut he blede fast and was full
^ore for he was but young and tendyr and but viij days old and there fore he
blede the more. Thanne ye shall understand that he bledde v. times fore us.
^ni^^^ enim ^i ci^^a sa^guin^ s^^ pro nobi^ eff^dit The first time that he
shed his blood was as this day when he was circumcised. A nothir was for fer
of his passione for right as a child wepith for fere wha^ he seethe the rod
and has no harm so the flesche of our lord swede blood for dread of a
strenger passion that was coming. The thridde time was in his flagella cion*
when he was betyn with stourges so that all his body ran on read blood. The
fourth time was wha^ he was nay led hand and foot on the cross. The fifte
time was wha^ that longinus perisched his heart with a spear that watyr and
blood come out of his wou^des And than they took up the cross with the body
and lift hit up on high and with a sodeyne fall they let the cross fall
down in to the mortesse that all the senowis and v^ynes and joints braste a
two and blood and watyr come out of every wound this he suffered for us Tha^ne
seethe criste was cicumcised and shed his blood thus for us y^ was with outyn
sin and circumcision is for sin remedy and help why would he be
circumcised that did no sin Sanctus augu stiuua dicit ^ropterquat^or causa^
Seint Austeyn se^th hit was for four causes. the first was to make a seethe
with the jews for else they would and might have seyde that he hade be of her
law where for they would not resceyue him consent to his techyng. this was to
disceyue the fend For right as the fend disceyued a dam and Eve and so all
mankind was dampened So hit fill to criste to disceyue the fend where thourghe
all mankind might be saved. than whau the fend saw that he was circumcised
as a no^^ir child he wend y^ he had take that penance in remedy of
original sin. and so he know him not from a nothir child for if he had
know him verily that he had rome to have bought mankind he would never have
tysed the jews to have put criste to death. And this was all the cause that
our lady was weddid to Joseph for to disceyue the fend for the fend should
wend that Joseph had be his fadir and not consceyued of the holy ghost The
thrydde cause why he was circumcised that was in confermyng the old law in
great comfort to the old fadres y^ were of the old testament fore and if he
had be cristoned and not circumcised hit had be a great discomforte to all
that were be fore the incarnation of our lord ihesu criste The fourth cause
of his circumcision was for our lord woste well that there would come heretics
aftyr that would have seyde y^ criste had a body of the erthely fantesy and not
of flesche and blood as on of us have for a body of the eyere may not blede And
there for to put a wey all soche errors criste was circumcised and blede in
his cut tyng of his flesche the which flesche was cut from his membre an
angel aftyr brought hit to king charles for the most precious relike in the
world and for the gretteste worship that he ^owde do there to he brought hit
to rome to a church that is callid Saneta sanctorum For these iiij. causes
criste was circumcised This day also hit is callid the vtas of the natiuite
that is the viij. day of our lordis birthe in great tokenyng to all us that
bethe good servants to think on these viij. days that folowith the birthe
The first day is to think y^wardly on the sede that we were conceived of that
is foul and abomynable in hit self that as a man or a woman be they never so
feyre that and they saw the matter they would have be a shamed of him self to
think ^ he were ever conceived of that foul think.

The secounde day is to think how grievously he ^aynithe his modir in his
birthe in so much that hit is an great miracle of god that she may have her
lyffe The iij day is to think how feeble and how wreched he is borne for all
the bestis of kind somewhat ca^ help hem self sau man kind he nothir may nor
can help him self in no degree but dye a none but he had help and socoure
of other. The iiij. day is to think in how much parell and dread he leuithe
here fore in e^^ry place death folowith him and is ever ready to fall on him
what time newere no man knowithe but only god him self In certum est locua in
quo more te exspectat. It is in certain the place there as death a bidithe the
The v. day is for to think how horrible death is when he comythe for in
short space and time he makyth a man to stink that all the best frendis
that he has be a vysed to put him in to the earth and hyde him there. The vi.
day is to think how rewfull is the departing of the body and the soul that
may not be departed till the he rte in the body br^ke fore dread of the sightes
that the soul shall see that for great fere the he rte brekyd. O more quam
amara est memoria tua. O thou death how bitter it is to think upon when
th^w art coming to any man.

The vij. is to think how dredefull is the dome that he shall goo to a none
and how streyte his judgment shall be tha^ he that woll think one these vij.
days besely on the viij. day I hope he shall be circumcised that is he shall
be cut a wey from the lust of his flesche and of sin and so do part from
this worlds likkyng. and thus comyth the viij. day that is the ^tas of criste
that is the joy of bliss that shall never have end to the which god bring
us all to Amen.

Judie epiphanie
GOod frendis this day is callid the xij. day but hit is the xiij. day of
cristus birthe The which day holy church callid hit the Epiphania domini that
is to sey the showing of our lord ihesu criste verray god and man for this day
he was showed verray god and man be three offerynges be his cristonyng and also
be tournyng of water in to wine. The xiij. day of his birthe be offering of the
three kings and that same day xxx. winter and xiij. days aftyr his birthe he
was cristened in the water of flom Jordan and that same day twelfemonthe aftyr
he turned water in to wine at the weddyng of cane galilee. But the feste
makythe most mind and mention of the iij. kings offering and there late us
follow the form of holy church. and here ye shall here how hit fill of her
offering to our lord Jhesu criste verray god and man These three kings where
of the lynage that prophesied how a sterre should shine of Jacob but they were
no jews of kind but they had herd by prophecye of this where fore the
had great desire and ^usce to see hit and so oftyn time when might come to
gedyr upon certain high hills than they would dispute among hem of this
sterre So hit happid upon Cristemas night the same time as our lord was
borne they were to gerdyr and were disputyng of this sterre Super mo^tem
auctorele^. upon the hill

Dominna enim erat ^at^a Our lord was borne Et appar^ it illis And apperid to
hem in the sterre as fair a child and vndyr his head a bryghte cross of
gold and seyde thus to hem goo ye a none in all the haste that ye may in to
the land of jury and ta^e with you Gold mirre and ensence And offer these three
things to him that ye shall find there new born^ king of Jews verray god
and man and I shall be your gyde and led you the wey. Thanne they a none for
great haste they took bestys that be callid dromedaries that be of soche a
kind they be so swifte that they woll run further in on day than any other
best wolle run o^ go in three days And so they come to Iherusalem that was
the che^e Cite of all jury hopyng that they should here there sum tydinges
where that this child was borne. But as soon as they turned in to the Cite of

wey till that they come the dyr bryghter thanne the son Thanne wha^ they come
in to the Cite of iherusalem they rode to king he rowde for he was there the
same time and seyde to him ^bi est qui natua e^re^ indeorum where is he that is

sterre in the este ^eniemus adora^e eum we be come to worship him. Thanne

clerhys where this child should be bore and they said in Bethleem ^de. Tha^
king herowde askid the kings p^uely of the sterre and bad hem goo in to
Bethleem and worship the child and come ayene by him and tell him where he
might find the child that he might goo worship him. Thanne when the
kings where passed toward bethleem a no^ the sterre aperid to hem and when
they saw the sterre was come again they were glad in their hertys and as hit is
in many places peynted the king that is in the myddell for great loye of the
sterre he lokyd bacwarde to his fellow be hind him and with his finger shewid
him the sterre And that is the cause that the myddyll king lokyd bacwarde. And
thus the sterre brought hem to bethlee^ and when the sterre come over the
house there as our lord was ynne he stood stille Than the kings lyghted down
and yede in to the house and with all the reverence that they cowde knylyng a
down and offered each of he in these iij things Anrum tusse et mirram Gold
cense and mirre knowlechyng by the gold that he was king of all kings And by
the ^ncense that he was verrey god And by the myrre that he was verey man and
sholld be deed and leyde in grave with c^te roting.

For golld is chief of all metallis Ensens is burnt in holy church in
worship to god. Mirre is an oyntement that kepithe deed bodies from ^tyng.
Thus when the kings had do her offering be techyng of the angel Per altam
viam reuersi sunt in regionem suam By a nothir wey they went toward her own
lands and left king herowde. and the ster^^ vanisched a wey from hem. Thanne
as seynte Bernard seythe joseph kept of this gold as much as him nedith^ to
his tribute that he should pay to the Emperor and also more to keep our lady
with while she lay in child bed and the remenaunte be delid to pore people
soche as had great need there to. The sense he burnt to put ^ way the
stenche of the stable there as she lay ynne. And with the Mirre our lady a
noynted her child to keep him from worms and disseses

But what be fill of the kings aftyr I find nothing in certain but sum
people have an opynyone how that seynte Thomas of Inde Cristoned hem wha^ he
come in to that country of Inde. and than as the sterre lyghtenyd hem to
cristus birthe So the holy ghost lyghtenithe hem in her souls and taught
them the perfyte wey of the be leave and also of perfect and gracious leuyng in
so much that they left all her kingdom and went forth one pilgrr^mages
that is for to say to Iherusalem and in many other places and so they come
forth to myllayne and there they diede all three. And so aftyr that they were
translatid to coleyne and there they be yet. Now have ye herd by these three
kings how our lord ihesu criste was this day showed verray god and man where
for like as they offered with great deuocio^ so should ye do your offerynges
when ye come to holy church kneling down with all the reverence that ye can
or may not on your one kne as to a temperall lord but on both your knees and
do him worship with good preyoures Than offer ye preciouse gold for there is
no gold so p^cious as is the good preyoure devout And than hold up your
hondis to him with all the reverence that ye can and devout heart prey to him
and show him all your love of your hertes and than ye offer to him ensence.
For there is none ensence sauerithe so sweet byrnyng in the fire as does good
preyoure that is devoutly seyde with a byrnyng love in clean charity And if
thou do thus than thou offereste knelyng on thy knees make a cross on the
earth and kiss hit and think well thou art but earth. than must ye offer
mirre for right as mirre kepithe a body from rotyng so the mind of death
kepithe a man's soul from dedly sin in this wise do ye your offering and
than shall ye have as much mede as had the se iij kings. Also he was showed
both god and man at his cristonyng For he come to the water of flom Jordan he
went in to the water and hallowed hit for right as he was circumcised to
conferme the new law and for no need that he had there to for he was clean
with out sin but for to make the sacrament that should wasthe hem took
cristonyng in his name from all sins

Thanne was ioha^ baptiste ready there and much people with him that come
thethir to the cristo nyng. Than said Johan to our lord all qua king and
tremelyng. blessid lord thou art god dislambe with out syn thou haste no need
to be cristoned of me but that I ^ man gotyn and borne in sin have need to
come and be cristoned of in remission of sins

Thanne seyde our lord criste jhesu johan suffer at this time for thus we
must fulfille all right wisneste and johan cristoned our lord ihesu criste
and as hit is credible our lady was cristoned aftyr with other of cristus

michi been complacui. This is my well-beloved sone the which plesith me This was
to teache all criston people the feythe of the be leave of holy church for all
criston people be bound to be leave stead fastely in the fadyr and the sone and
the holy ghost.

In baptismo christi toto trinitas semauifesta^it scilicet. Pater in noce
filin^ in carne* spiritus sanctus in columba et totum celum apertum est

In cristus baptym all the holy Trinite was shew^d for the fadir spoke in

was there bodily when Johan baptiste seyde

Ecce agnus dei and the holy ghost was sent Sicut columba as a white dove
These ben three persons in on godhede for the fadir spoke above and the sone
was there bodily and the holy ghost in likeness of a dove ye shall be leave
that these iij. persons be but one god in trinite This be leave ye shall know
on the watyr brynke that is in your cristonyng at the founte where fore he
that beleuythe thus and does werkys of be leave shall be saved Qui crediderit
et baptisa^u^ fuerit sal^^^ erit He that beleuithe and is cristoned shall be
saved and folowithe the werkys of believe.

Qui ^ero non crediderit condem^na bitur And he that beleuithe not nor doth^
not the werkys of believe shall be dampened The werkis of believe be mekenes and
charity for with out these ij. shall no man be saved and he that has these
ij. he is wreton in the genelogie of our lord ihesu criste the which is radde
in cristemasse that begynnethe a boue with Abraham And so comythe downewardes
to joseph and to our lady ^n showing that he that is most mekyste in heart is
most next our lord ihesu criste and soche he a vaunsith in everlasting

^^ackyd wine at the mete.

Thanne badde our lord that they should take vi. steues or pottys that were
empty and bad fill he^ with watyr and they did Thanne our lord blessed hem and
bad they should ^ere them that be ganne the table and late him begin and
than he be ganne and said hit was the best wine that ever he drank. Thus our
lord showed him self both god and man god in that he turned watyr in to wine
and man in that he et^ and drank with hem This miracle he shewde at the
weddyng in tokenyng that he blessed all weddynges that he done aftyr the law
of holy church And there for keep your wedloke and be in full feythe and
believe of holy church as holy church techithe and so ye shall come to ever
lastyng bliss Amen

De con^ersi^^^ sancti pauli.


GOod frendis soche a day ye shall have (...) lis day that is callide ^^^
con^ersion of seint poule for that day he was co^uertid^ and ^^^^ned from a
cursed tyraunte in to goddis servant from ^^ high man and a prowd^ in to a
meke man and a good man and from the disciple of the de^yll in to goddis holy
apostell so for this man was tournede from all wickkednesse in to great
goodness in great strenghte help and socoure to all holy church There for
holy church holdithe his ^ouersion and so we do of no mo but of him only and
that i^ for iij. causes. The first for great miracles in his tourning and for
the great joy in his defendyng. and fore the ensample of his amendyng First
or he was turned he was called saul for right as saul the king of Jherusalem
pursewed holy david to have slain him right so the saul porsewed criste and
his disciples to bring hem to the death. There for while criste went one earth
here this saul would never come to him to here his techyng but as soon as
criste was steied up in to heaven than a non this saul for he was learned and
cowde the Jews law he be ganne to with stand and a yense seyde cristus
disciples disputyng a yense hem and poursewed hem in all he might in full
entente to have distroied hem and christian feythe. Thanne on a day he disputed
with seynte Stephyn and for he might not over come him he be thought him how
he might bring him to his death and so he left him never till he was deed
Thanne hit is the manner of the fendes children when they have done a cursed
deed to be glad and feign there of proud in her hertis and ^encrese her malice
^o was saul glad of the death of seynte Stephyn and fore he would have gotyn
him a name of wickedness passing all his fellows he went to hem that had the
jews law to keep and get him a letter of warraunt for to take all that be
leued in in criste where they might be found and to bring hem to Jherusalem
for to be put to the death there. Thanne when ^e had these lettres he took
soch a pride there with and envy in his heart a yenste cursten people that when
he herd any man speak of hem a none fore great anger he would snefet the nose
and frothe at the mouth for anger and grugge with his tethe thretenyng and
masesseynge towardis hem that all Christian people was sore a ferde of him.
Thanne on a day he herd that in the Cite of damask was much criste^ people
hid for dread and rode the dyr wards but a none our lord ihesu cristeshewed
the sweetness of his grate when this saul was in his high^pride and in
will to have do most harm Than a boute midday our lord cast a light of
grace a boute that was much lyghter thanne the son and the light spoke to
saul thus. Saul saul quid tu me perseq^ri^. Saul saul what folowest thou
me and a none he was a ferde and fill down of his horse and cryde and seyde
for great fere Quis es tu domine Lord what art thou than seyde our lord. Ego
sum ihesus ua sarenua. I am ihesu of nazareth for that was the name of his
manhood Thanne saul a none be leued on him and seyde lord what wolte thou that
I shall do Thanne saw the people^ a boute him the light and herd the wyre
but they saw no thing but a none went, to saul and took him up by the hand
fore he was blind and might not see and so ladde him in to the Cite to a good
man's house and there he was three days and three nyghtis fasting and nothir
ete mete nor drink ^e might not fee but ever preyde to god fore dread of that
vision The which time the holy ghost taught him cristus law Than the thridde
day on of cristus disciples that highte Ananyas as god bad him come to him full
sore a ferde and said Saul frater dominua ihesua misit me ad te qui apparuit
tibi in via Saul the lord has sent me to the ihesus that apperid to the in
the wey and that thou shuldeste see and be cristoned. and when Ananias leyde
his hand upon his head a none he saw and there fill from his eyes like
scales of fisches. And wha^ he had cristoned him he callid him Poule. and
than ete and was comforted and had his strenghte and was there a few days
with the disciples. Than went ^e in to the temple and prechid openly of our
lord thesu criste p^uyng clerckly that he was both god and man and none other.
Stu^ebant autem omn^a qui eum andiebant et dicebant. For fothe all that herd
him were a stoyned and seyde that hit was a great miracle and grace of god and
his ^o deyne conversion for he ^ was of so cursed leuyng so litell be fore was
^o sone turned to god and man Thus may ye here how great miracle god shewde in
his conversion and how great joy holy church makyth of his defendyng hit was
great joy to all christian people that was a litill be fore to distroye christian
people and a non aftyr as besy to encrese christian people* And he that was so
besy and so glad to shede christian men's blood. than was he so ready to shede
his blood for hem. And as besely as he went to put hem to death than with as
good a will h^ was ready to take the death for hem and there as no man durst
p^^he the word of god for him aftyr the comfort that they had of him they
spared not for lord nor fore king but openly preched the word of god and
taught the feythe aftyr in every place And he that was to fore so proud and
so feres and sone aftir was so meke and so lowly y^ he fill to the ground to
every christian man's foot that ever he ^respased to and mekely be sought hem
of mercy with a full pacient heart where fore seynte* Austeyn likenyth him to
an Onicorne of kind that berith an horn in his nose and with that home he
^leithe all the bestys that he fightithe with Also he is so ferse in him self
that thee may no hunter take him but thus they wolle be gile him they wolle
aspey where the unicorn hauntith and use to walk and there they wolle set a
meyde and as soon as the unicorn seethe the maid a non be kind he wol fall
down and ley his head in her lap and than all the might and streghte is
gone And than they come and take him. Thus he seythe seynte Poule was first fo
ferse in him self that they durst not preche there as he was nor speak to him
for dread. But when our lord ihesu criste showed him sweetness of his grace
and this fair maid that is the law of holy church a none poule fill down
to the ground and was soget to all criste^ people here fore holy church was
glad of his defendyng He is set also in high ensample of high a mendyng
for our lord is so gracious y^ all christian people may be saved that woll for
fake her mys^e leuyng and be conuertid Multomagis gaudiu^ erit in celo de vno
peccatore penitenciam age^ re quam de nonagin ta n^uem qui uo^ indigent
penitentia. There is more Joye in heaven upon on sinner doing pen^unee thanne
upon xcix. that deed never sin And there for our lord would that all were
conuertid and saved where fore in high ensample and coumforte to all sinful
people he set seynte Poule to look upon for though a man had do never so
much sin and he would fore sake his sin and sin no more Thanne all the
company of heaven makythe myrthe and melodye of his conversion as we do here in
earth of the conversion of seynte Poule but there is much people that love
more sin with lust and likelyng in this world than they do god. Fore there
be many that wolle never leave sin nothir for the love of god nor for the
desire of the bliss of heuene nor for fer^ of the fend nor dread of the great
pains of hell But sum people seyne god wolle never lose that he has
boughte dear with his passion. but they that sey so be notte wise god would
that none were lost but be ware thou lose not thy self for all the while
thou loueste, more sin than god and had lever to serve the fend than god
thou art cause of thine own dampnacion fore while thou haste more will to
serve the fend and be his child than goddis child thou lesiste thy self and
god has ordained fendes to tourmente hem in ever lastyng pain But seinte
Gregor seyth they that shall be dampened begin her penance here in this
world in party and aftyr her death contin^ueth of ever more. where fore I tell
you this ensample



There was a man and that was an officer with a lord and stood a cursed and on
a time ^^ he rode toward a manner of his lord is he fille out of his mind
and ^n b^^ de^id his horse and he bare him in to a manner of his lordis And than
a none the bailey conseyued how hit was with this man that he was discranght
out of his mind and a none made the people to bind him to a post in a barn
so wha^ the bailey and his servants had souped he bad one of his servants go
look how that this man deed and he went to this man And when he come there he
saw iij. gre black dogs plucking a wey this man's flesh from the bone
Thanne was this servant a ferde that ^nethe he had his mind but went to
his bed and lay there sike long aftyr And on the morrow when the people come
the their as this man was bound the^ found no more of this man but his bare
bones and all the flesche was clean a wey Thus ye may see he that contynualy
leued in sin may be full sykyr of a foul end and though^ his end semythe
fair in the sight of a man yet hit is right foul in the sight of almighty
god and all his angellis where for hit is needful for every christian man and
woman to a me^de him while he is here in this world and has time and space of
a mendement And he that does so shall come to seynte Poule and be there with
him in everlasting bliss to the which bring us he that died for us and all
mankind Amen.

Sequitur ^e parificacio^e beat marie virginia*
GOod frendis soche a day ye shall have candelmas day that day makith m^de and
mention of our lady and of her sone and speciyally iij thingis our ladies
purificacion in sime onis metyng and in ca^d^les offering. This day is callid
the purificacion of our lady in englische hit is the clensing of our lady but
fore no need that she had there to fore sche was clensid with the worchyng of
the holy ghost in conceyuyng of her sone that there was in her no manner of
spotte of filthe.

But for that day was the xl. day from the birthe of her sone and was callid in
the jews law the day of the purificacione not only for our lady but for all
other wymmen where fore we call hit the purificacion of our lady The law of
the jews was soche that a woman that was delyueryd of a man child was hold
unclean vij. days aftyr tha^ the law gave her leave to go to her husbonde. but
yet she was unclean xxxiij day^^ but till xliiij. days were fullfilled she
should hold her with out the church with her offering And the offering* in
those days was of a rich man a lamb and for a pore man ^^s a peyre of
turtyll doves or else other doves and so offered our lady with her sone And
if a woman be delyueryd of a maiden child she should duble all those same
days a fore said that is for to say the coming to her husbonde. and also the
coming to the temple and so this is there son there of For hit is so that all
great clerkys sey that hit to vij. days aftyr when a woman has conceived a
man's child or that the same sede turn in to blood.

And hit is also.xxxiij. days aftyr o^ it turn to any shappe of man. and
than god sent lyffe in to hit and if hit be a maid child hit doublithe all
the days both in tournyng in to the blood and also in shappe of body and this
is the cause. eve that was the furste ^ormyd woman that e^^r wrathid our lord
more tha^ did the man Adam therefore she is longer in formyng Thus fore fleschly
complexion of man and woman she is un clean in her self there for this
purificacion is ordained But vnderstondith well that our lady had no need to
this clensing fore she conceived not with complexion of man but only of the
holy gosce so that she was clean of all manner of filthe touching consent of man
But yet she went to the temple no other wymmen deed specially for iiij.
causes. The first was to fullfillethe scripture that seyth thus Quanto mai^e^
ta^to te humilie^ The higher that thou art in degree the mekyr thou shulde^^e
make the Thus did our lady for she wyste well sche was modir to goddis sone of
heaven and had so great worship passing all other wymmen yet sche made her as
the poreste woman that was in the company. The secou^de cause was as she
fullfillithe the law of circumcision of her sone in the same wise she
fullfillid the purificacion and in offering of her sone in the temple doing for
him as other pore wymmen did for her children.

The thridde cause for to stop the jews mouths left they had seyde that she
had not do the law and so caughte a great sclaundre a yense h^e^ in time
coming.

The fourth cause was for to give ensample to all other wymen that they should
come to church aftyr the birthe of her child and thank god that he has
sauyd hem from death in her trauelyng for in that time a woman is in great
parell of death for there is no sikenes in the world that gothe so nyghe death
fore these causes holy church makythe mind of our ladies purificacion Hit
makythe mind also of the coming of symeon and Anne Symeon ille senex din
vixerat ^ine etas cooperatur Anne

This symeon was a passing old man but he had preyde to god besely all his
lysse that he should never dye till he had seyne criste bodily in this world
and so he deed And this Anne has preyde the same Also ye shall understand
that this was not ^ine our ladies mo dir but an other a^na*that had a husbonde
vij. year and when her husbonde was deed she would not be weddid no more but
leuyd till she was lxxx. year old and served god in the temple night and day
and preyde to se god or she dyede and our lord grauntid her. Thanne when our
lady come into the temple with her sone the holy ghost warned symeon and Anne
and a none they with much joy went a yenste him and brought him in to the
temple

Et Symeon accepiteum in uluaa sna^. And symeon took him in his arms with all
the reverence that he cowde and might and seyde. (...) dimittis sernum tuum
domine secundum nerhum ^num in pace and cetera. O thou lord now for give thy
servant aftyr thy word in pese. and so with all the worshipp^ and reverence
that he could he louyd and tha^kid him that he would let him leave so long to
see him bodily with his eye^ where in mind of this when a woman comythe to
church of a child she a bydithe at the church door till the priest come and
cast holy water on her and takythe her in by the hand in to the church
yeuen her leave aftyr to come to church and to goo to her husbonde for and they
have comened to gedyr be fore they must both shreyue he^ there of and take her
penance Also holy church makythe mind of candels offering and as ye see hit
is a common use for all christian people that be of convenient age to come that
day to church and bear a candell brennyng in procession as though they went
bodily with our lady. But now ye shall here how this worshippefull feste
was first found Sum time when the Romans by great might and vial
power conquered all the world fore they had great dominacion they were so
proud that they for get her god and made hem diverse goddis aftyr her own
lust And so among all they had a god that they called Mars that had be to
fore a notable knight in battle And so they preyde to him fore help and fore
they wol^^ speed the better of this knight the people preyde and did great
worship to his modir that was called februa aftyr the which woman much
people have opinion that this moan that is callid februarij where fore the
secounde day of this moan is Candelmas day The Romans this night would goo a
boute the Cite of rome with torchis and candels bre^nyng in worship of this
woman Februa for hope to have the more help and socoure of her sone mars. Than
was there a (...) that was callid Sergius and when he saw Christian people draw
to this false maumentry and vn^^^ we believe he thought to undo this foul use
and custume and turn hit in to goddis worship and our ladies and yaffe
commandment that all christian people should come to church and offer up a
candell brennyng in the worship that they did to this woman februa and did
worship to our lady and to her sone our lord Ihesu Criste so that now this
feste is solemply hallowed through all cristendome and each christian man and woman
of couenable age to come to church and offer up her ca^dels as though they
were bodily with our lady hopyng for this reverence and worshipp^ that they do
to our lady to have a great reward in heaven and of her sone our lord ihesu*
criste and so they may be sekyr and hit be do in clean lyffe and with good
deuocione. A candell is made of weke and wexe So was cristis soul hid with
ynne the manhood. Also the fire be tokemith the god head Also hit be tokenithe
our lady modirhode and maydenhede light with the fire of love Also hit be
tokenith every christian man and woman that does good dedis with good entente and
perfect love and charity to god and to all christian people. where for if there
be any of you that his candell of charity be queynte goo a none and be a cordid
with his neybores and light his ca^dell and tha^ offer hit up fore that is
goddis will And if ye do not thus ye shall lose all your me rite and your
mede in heaven (...)

god kept them so that they had no harm.

Than for this* Judas was one of the xij. apostels and the nombre of he^ must
be fullfilled. than was criste steyed up in to heaven and the xi. apostles were
to gedyr with many other people in a place Thanne seyde Petyr to hem thus now
all good men and brethren hit is well know to you that Judas was one of the
xij. and be cause the no^bre may not be in perfeyte hit is needful to chese on
of these ij. men that has be with our lord chesu criste from the time that
he was baptisid in to the time of his asce^sione to bear wittenesse with us of
his vprysing and of his doing. Than they setten these ij. men Joseph barsabas
and mathie and leyde lotte upon hem and seyde thus preyng our lord O lord
thou knowist the hertis of all men show to us which thou che^i^te of these
ijj men and the lotte fill on mathie and so he was in nombre with the other xi.

Than mathie went in to mirre to preche word of god and fore he had the grace
of the holy ghost with him he did miracles and turned much people to the
feythe of criste Than was the fend sorry and aperyd to the Bishop of the
jews law in likeness of a young child with long heris and hoar and bad him
take mathie and do him to the death or else he would turn all the people to
cristus feythe Than the Bishop wexyd nyghe wode forwrathe and sent out
people to seek mathie and wha^ they had him they bound him his hondis be hynde
him and cast a rope about his neck and ladde him to prison and there bond
him fast with cheynes of iron Thanne the night aftir our lord ^hesu, C^riste
come to him with a great light and lousid his bondis and wha^ he had well
comfortid him he opened the prison door and bad him go preche the feythe and
spare for no man Than there as he p^chid there were sum that a yenestode him
and letid other y^ would have turned to the feythe Tha^ said mathie to hem I
tell you be for he shall fall down to hell pit. and so a none in sight of
all me^ the earth opened and they sanke down in to hell body and soul and
never was seyne more of hem. than was the people sore a gaste of that sight
and turned to the feythe a great nombre of hem Tha^ when the bishopp^ herd
there of they took him and bound him and set men to throw stones at him and
when he was nyghe de de he bad christian pleople to bear the stone that he was
stonedwith in to the grau with him in wittenesse of his martirdom^ and he
knelid down and held up his hondis to god and seyde O lord I be sech the take
my spirit and gafe up the ghost Reynold of chestre in his cronicles tellith a
nothir miracle like this and seythe. when seynte wolston visitid his
bishopp^riche the people brought a man be for him that did his neyboures much
disese and would never be in pese preyng the bishop to chastise him and when
the bishop had prechid this man he was ever longer the worse tho^ the bishop
and all the people preyde to seint mathie to show some miracle be this man what
he was worthy to have than ano^ in sight of all the people there come out of
the earth ij. fendes with brennyng hokes and pullid this quick man dou^e to
hell and when he was gone the people were well releued and had rest and pese
ever aftyr Amen*

De annunciacione beat marie uir ginis.


GOod friend is so che a day ye shall have an high and a sole mpne feste in
holy church the annu^ciacion of our lady and he that had a vowed or joined in
penance must fast the even ye shall understand that hit is callid the
annu^ciacion for this cause for the fadyr of heaven sent his angel Gabriell
Missus est an gelus gabriel a deo in cinitatem cui no men nazareth In to the
cite that was callid nazaret to our lady that was new wedded be the bidding
of god and reuelacion of the holy ghost to a man that callid Joseph and as she
was in her chamber in her prey ours the Angel gabriell come to her and seid
our lord i^ with the

Thanne was she greatly a stoyned of this greting for there was in that country
a man that cowde much which craft and so with help of fendes he made him
self like an Angel and come to diverse maydenes and said he was sent from
god to hem on his message and so often time lay by hem and did hem great vylony
Thanne when our lady herd tell of that man she was a drade left hit had be
he for she had spoke with none Angel be fore nor there were no soche wor^is ne
soche gretynges made never none to her be fore Tha^ Gabriell the Angel
comforted there and said. Ne time as maria in^e uisti graciam apud dominum.
Dread the not mary for sothe thou haste found grace of our lord for a mong
all wymmen our lord has chosyn the forto be the modir of his sone and him
thou shalt conceive be feythe and be love of the holy ghost with out any deed
of man that shall shadow the and quench all fleschly lust and tend the
light of gostely love that thou shalt conceive the sone of the high god. And
thus thou shalt be both modir and maid and so was never no^ before. Thanne a
none our lady herd this wordis a none there with come a spiritual
swettenesse and joy in her heart that a none or any erthly mo^ ^owde tell hit
and so with all the reverence of meke nesse that she cowde sche answered thus a
yene and seyde. Ecce aucilla domini fiat michi secundum uerbum tuum. Lo here
goddis own maid ready to do goddis will preyng hit may be to me right as thou
seyste. Thus that blessed body conceived our lord ihesu criste in ever lastyng
joy to all the world. Thus I may likyn our lady to a p^cious stone callid
enix and he is as clear as any criscall and shall of kind wha^ the son
shynythe hot on him hit openithe and received a drop of the dew of heaven in
to him and closithe a yene till.ix. months aftyr and thanne hit openithe and
fallithe out a sto^e of the same kind and so closithe a yene as ever hit was
and never openithe aftyr. Thus our lady was as clean as any cristall for the
hot love of the holy ghost at the ix. month is end she was delyueryd of her
sone our lord ihesu criste and she aftyr as clean meyden as she was to fore
Than when the Angel had done his message he went his wey to heaven and our
lady went to her cosyn elisabeth that was great with child with seinte Johan
Baptiste and who^ she come to Elisabethe she grette her mekely and as soon as
our lady spoke to Elisabeth the child in Elisabethes womb pleyde and made
great joy for^^ ^^we that our lord had take mankind and was come to save he
in that were lorne. Thann^ our lady dwellid therewith Elisabeth her cosyn till
the time yt seinte Johan was borne and was myddewyffe to eli sabeth and took
seint Johan from the earth and there she learned all that her ned id for to
know aye^ the time yt her sone should be borne and was persite y noughe there
of Tha^ mekely she took her leave and went home a give to Nasareth Than
thought Joseph he would go ^oke how his wyffe deed and went toward her and
when our lady herd of his coming sche went agayn^ him and great him full
mek^ly. But when joseph saw her great with child he meru^yled gretely how that
might be for well he wyste hit was not his fore he had never part of her
body in that degree fore he know well that she had made a vow before she would
never have part of man's body and thought how he was made to wedde her by the
byddyng of the holy ghost and great miracle showing and thought right in his
heart he was not worthy to dwell in her company and tho^ght in his heart to
have gone home aene and to leave her there Thene come an angel to him and said
be not aferd to take mari thy wife to thy keeping fore it is of the holy ghost
that is quick in her body for thou shall be her keeper and norse to her child
and when* hit is borne call it ihesus for he shall be savior to all the
world. Than ye shall understand that for iiij. causes as seynte Ambrose seyth
our lady was weddid to this old man Joseph The first was if she had
conceived with out wedloke the jews would have seid that she had be an evil
woman of her body and so have stoned her to death. The secou^de cause was fore
she was so shamefast that and she had herd any have put any defame to her
she would have dyede fore sorrow. The thrydde cause was for joseph should bear
wittenesse of her maydenhode The fourth cause fore joseph should help her at
her birth and bring her to bethleem and aftyr in to Egipte and so ayene in to
her own country fore these iiij. causes she was weddid to this old man Joseph
And also to be gyle the fend that he should not know him from a nothir*
child. Now have ye herd of the Annunciacion. There be sum people that ask
a question why there stondithe a wine pot with lyllyus between our lady and
Gabriell the Angel at her salutacion. This is the cause fore our lady at
her salutacion conceived be feythe



Hit be fill thus upon a cristemasse day that a christian man and ^ jew sat to
gedyr and spoke of the concepcion of o^re lady and as they were there stood a
wine pot to fore he in with a lyly there ynne Thanne said the christian man we
be leave that our lady conceived like as this lyly conceyuythe color of grene
and aftyr bryngi^h forth a white flower with out craft of man or any pay ryng
to the stalk right so our lady conceived of the holy ghost and aftyr
brought her sone our lord ihesu criste without any wemme of her body that is
flower and chief of all wymmen.

Thanne seyde the jew when I see a lyly spring out of the death stalk that
stondith in this pot thanne wolle I believe that thou seyste hit is true and a
none there with sprange a white lyly out of the deed stock that stood in that
same wine pot And when this Jew saw that a none he fill down un to the
ground upon his knees and seyde thus. lady now I see well that thowe
conceived with the holy ghost our lord Ihesu criste goddys sone of heaven And
thou were clean maiden both be fore the birthe and also aftyr the birthe And
so a none he was cristoned and so aftir he was a full holy man. And this is
the cause where so: that the pot with the lylyus is set between our lady
and the Angel for right as the jew disputid with the christian man of the
manner of the concepcion So our lady disputid with the Angel of the manner how
she should conceive and be both modir and maid or she consentid there to
Thanne ye that woll fast the v. eu^^ys of our lady in worship of her v.
joys that she had of her sone The first was when she conceived of the holy
ghost and know that sche was modir to goddis sone of heaven.

The secounde was on cristemasse day when she was delivered of her so ne with
out any pain of her body for as she conceived with out lust of her body
also she was delivered without pain of her body. The iij. joy was one Estyr
day when her sone rose from death to live and come to her and kyssed her and
made her more ioyefull of his ^prysing than she, was sorry of his death The
fourth joy was whann he^s^yed up to heaven on holy thurday in the same flesche
and blood that he took in her body The v joy was in her assumpcion when she
saw her sone come with great multitude of angelis and semtis to fette her to
heaven and crowned her queen of heaven and Emperes of hell and lady of the world
and so all that be in heaven shall do her reverence and worship and all bethe
in earth shall do her service

These be the v. joys that our lady had of her sone and ye shall
understood that he that woll great our lady with v. aueys shall never come in
to the pain of hell



we find wreton of an holy maiden that was devout in our lady service and
every day great her with v. joys Than hit happened so on a day that she fill
sike and felt her self well that sche should be deed and for fere she ^ighed
wonder sore and made great moan for be cause she wysce not whet^r she should go
afher death Thanne come our lady to her and seid why art thou so sorry y^ have
made me so often glad gretyng me with joys that I had of my sone there fore
be not sorry but know thou well that y^ shalt go with me in to ever lastyng
bliss and joy ever with out end



we find of seint Gilbert that one a time he was nigh deed of the quincy and
wha^ his throat was so great and w^ll nigh deed ^ he might uneath take brethe
our lady come to him and seyde to him gilbert my servant hit were evil do
that thy throat should suffer penance that has so oftyn times gladid me with
my joys and a none she took her feyre pappe and myl^yd on his throat and went
her wey and a none there with he was hole and thankyd our lady ever aftyr.

De sa^cto georgio martire.
GOod frendis soche a day ye shall have saint Gorges day the holy martyr hit is
wreton in his lyffe that there was an horrible dragon be side a Cite that was
callid Cirme of the which dragon me^ of the Cite were sore a ferde in so much
that be counsel of the king every day they gaffe him a child and a sheep to
ete fore fere left he would have come in to the Cite Than when all the
children and shep were nigh eton for because that the king him self gaffe hem
that same counsel they constreyned him that had but a daughter to give her to
the dragon Than the king for fere of the people with weeping and great sorrow
making delivered hem his child and sent her forth in to the place there as
they were wont to set te her own children and a sheep with her to a bide till
the dragon come.

But than by the ordinance of god seint iorge come rydyng that wey and when he
saw this damysell in her array him thought she was a woman of great birthe and
asked her why she stood there with that sheep in soche ^ray fo morning Thanne
answered sche and seyde gentill knight well may I morn and make sorrow for I
am a kings daughter of this Cite And now am I set here to be devoured of a
dragon that had eto^ all the children of this cite and be now distroied and
now he must have me for my fadre gaffe he^ counsel there to and therefore
getyll knight ride hense fast and save thy self left the dragon slay both
the and me Tha^ seide gorge damysell that were great shame and vy lony to me
that I am a knight well arayde and should fle and thou a woman and should a
bide Than with that the dragon put out his head at an hole and spitte fire
and proffered battle to gorge A none Gorge made a sign of the cross be fore
him and set his spear in gate and with great might bare down the dragon to
the ground and than he bad the damysell bind this dragon with her gir dell a
boute the neck and led him with her in to the cite and so the dragon followed
aftyr her as it had be an hounde made for to bow patiently

But when the people of the cite saw this dragon come they flede for fere a
wey Thanne gorge callid the people a yene and seyde to hem be not a ferde for
and ye woll be leave in criste and take cristendome I wolle save ^ew and ^^e
this dragon and delyuere you of your enmy Thanne where they so glad that a
none.xx. thousand men without wymmen and children were cristonyd and the ^^^g
and the queen were surs^e of all with all his ^usholde and than Gorge slew the
dragon and bad the people tey oxon unto him and draw him out of the that the
sauer of him did the people no harm Than gorge bad the king edify and bilde
churches in each cornere of his land and be lusty to goddis service and to
honor and worship to all people of holy church and ever have and
compassion and be sorry for hem that be pore and nedy and be in any dissese
Thane when gorge had done thus and had turned all the lord to christian feythe
he he^de of an Emperor that highte Dioclesian how he did many christian me^ to
death than he went to him and rebu^rd him of his cursid de dis. Than the
Emperor a none commaundid to put Gorge into prison and to ley him vprighte
and to ley a my stone on the breast to press him to death. Then Gorge preyde
t^ god for help and our lord kept him that he hadd no harm in no part of
his body And when the emperor herd there of he ded make to whelis and set
hem full of hokys and Gorge was set in the myddys between the^ ij. and than
the whelie were turned and so to race his flesche from the bones and when
Gorge was in this tourment a none he preyde to god of so coure and help and
anon he was holpyn And than they put him in to an hot lyme kylle and closid
him there in for he should have be burnt But a none our lord turned hit in
to cold and there in he was iij. days and tha^ they wend to have found him
all to burnt and he was save from all manner harms and was merry. Than he was
brought forth and set before the Emperor and Gorge repreuyd him of his
false goddis and seyde they were but fe^des with out might and power Than the
Emperor to beat his mouth with stones till he was to powned and made to beat
his bare body with dry besomes till the flesche fille from the bones and the
people might have seyne his guttis yet aftyr y^ they made him to drunk venym
that was made strong for the nonys for to have peyned him to death. And when
Gorge had made a syne of the cross he dra^ke the poison with out grieve in
so much that the man that made the poison turned to Christian feythe and a non
he was do to death Thanne the night aftyr as Gorge was in prison preyng* god
come to him and seyde Gorge be of good comfort to morrow thou shalt make an
end and come to ever lastyng joy and bliss and set a crown on his head
and gafe him his blessyng.

Than on the morew for he would not do worshipp^ to the false goddis the
Emperor made to smite of his head and than as the Emperor would have go to
his paleyse there come a fire lyghtening and burned him and all his people.

we find a scory of antioche wreton that be side iherusalem a fayrt young
knight apperid to a priest and seyde I am seint Gorge and a leder of christian
people and commanded the priest he should bear with him his relikes and come
with him to the siege of the rusalem But when they come to the walls of the
rusalem the he thyn people there ynn were so strong that the christian not
durst come to the walls. Than come seint Gorge clothid in white and made a
cross on his breast and went upon the ladder and badde the christian people
come aftyr him And so with the help of seint Gorge they got the Cite of ihe
rusalem and slew all the he thyn people that were found there. and there fore
late v^ prey to seint Gorge to help us a yense our go stely enmy new and ever
Amen.

De sancto mar^o euangelista.
GOod frendis soche a day ye shall have seint marks day that was one of the
four* Evangelists that wreton cristus gospel and p^^ched hem to she people
This mark was first an he thyn man and aftyr he was crisconed of seint Petyr
and he made him to go^ and preche to the people goddis word And tha^ fore he
was so holy a man the people would have had him to be a priest. But he was so
meke in him self that he made on of thombes to cut of for him thought he
was not worthy to be a priest but for god would have hit so seynte Petyr with
great instau^ce made him take the order of priest hode upon him. Tha^ was he
besy both day and night to p^che the word of god and all that he said with
word he confermed with good ensample and with doing of great miracles Thus by
the e^spiracl on of the holy ghost he went in to the Cite of ^^^^aundir fore
to turn the people to the feith Thanne when he come to the cite uneath he was
enterid in to the cite his scho braste and there by he wyste well that he
should be deed. Than he saw a man sit and cloute schon to pore people and
mark preyde him to me^de his scho Than for this man was pore him thought hit
was alms to help him at that time and took his scho and began to sewe and a
none with his na^^ he hurt his hand and what fore ache and fore great
penance he seyde god help and when mark herd that he callid to god a none
Mark preyde to god fore him And tha^ mark spatte on the earth and blessid hit
and a noyn tid his hand there with and seide In nomine patris Ihesu xpristi
filii dei vi^i san^tur mann^tua. In the name of the fadir ^he su criste the
sone of quick god thy hand be hole ^ocahitur autem homo ille anania^* For
sothe that man was callid anama and when anania saw soche virtue in mark he
preyde him to twelle stille with him Comoratusq^ i^. de^ du^^us annis And there
dwelled he ij. year and cristoned him and all his household and aftirwarde for
great holiness that mark saw with this man he made him a bischopp^ Thanne the
people saw how mark (...) in the Cite they took him and tide a rope a ho^^te
his neck and drew him among stones till the flesche fill to the earth and
seid draw we the bugull to the bugull place So when he was draw nyghe to
death tha^ they put him in to prison till on the morrow Than the same night
criste come to him in to prison and said Pese be to the mark our eua^
geliste be not a gaste fore I am with the Thanne on the morrow they co^^^ and
fe^te him out of p^ son and drew him till he was deed and when he should dye
he seyde In ma nn^ tuas And so gaffe up the ghost and aftirward they would
brenne his body and than there come sothe an earth quake with a lightenyng and
thoundyr that there durst no man a bide Than in the night christian people come
and took marks body and beried hit Than fill hit so that every christian land
hallowed seint marks day save one country that is callid appolonia the which
country was so greuyd with he^e and drowthe that all the country failed hem of
fruit so that they were well nere famelyd And tha^ there come a voice from
heaven and bad hem halowe seint marks day and than they schulde be comfortid
and they deed so and a no^ god sent hem ple^te of all manner of frutesy now.

Now hit is to wete why we schulde fast this day and go in precession.

we read in the cite of rome one this day fill soche a qualme and a sodeyn death
that when a man yaned or gapid or fuesid a no^ he dyede and there dyede many
suddenly. Thanne was there a pope was callid Pellagius that commaundid all
christian people that when he yaned every man schulde make a cross over his
mouth And when any man her de a nothir fuese he schulde sey criste help the.
and so many were saved. and there he made the people go a procession and so
preyng to all the semty^ of heaven to prey to god for hem and so they deed Tho^
come aftyr seint Grego ry and made hem do the same on seinte marks day to
halowe and fast and go in procession and canoni^ed hit to be done for ever
more than come there a pope yt was callid Liberius in his time all manner frutis
in this time of the year of great tendirnesse of hit self took great harm so
what by thoundyr lightenyng and unkind hete^ by stormys mildewes by worms and
by long tayled fleyes for vengeance that a none aftyr Estyr day the people
turned a yene to her old sin having no reward of the sacrament which they
have receyned and there fore god sent more vengeance this time than in any
other time of the year. where fore this holy (...) to put a wey all these
things and in special goddis wrethe fro the people he co^mau^did to all
christian people to halowe and to fast and go in procession and he that seyde
that hit is made be a co^stitucion is a cursed till he come to amendment And
there for I charge you and counsel you all that thynkith to be saved keep
this day aftyr the rewle of holy church

In die philippi ^ iacobi.
GOod frendis soche a day ye shall have the feste of philippe and jacob the
which were holy apostles. But for this feste comith with ynne feste of Estyr
ye shall not fast the even but ye shall come to church to worship god and
the holy apostles Tha^ ye shall know well that philippe was ordained by all
other apostles to goo in to country that was callid Sithia to preche to the
vnbeleued people. But when he come the dir and prechid and yene the maumentes
preuing that they were fendes and no goddis and so they took him and ladde him
to her temple and would have constreyned him to have do sacrifice. Than as they
were besy to do him dissese suddenly a great dragon come out of the ^^ the and
slew iij. of this miss believed people and venemed so the people with his
brethyng that there f^ll on hem soche a sikenesse that the woe and the sorrow
that they had they cride aftyr help. Than seyde philipp^ to hem if ye woll
be helped and helid of your sikenes and also these men reaid from death to live
Furste cast down the maumentes and set in her stead crossis like to the
cross there as our lord dyed upon and do hit worshipp^ Thann they deed so for
they were glad to be holpyn of her sikenesse and as soon as they had do so they
were holpyn And than philipp^ preyde to god for the iij. men to rise from death
to live Tunc precepit phillippus draconi vt in locum suu^ redescenderet Thanne
philippe commaundid the dragon to go down to his place a yene and never
dissese man more. Than the cursed people of the Cite saw that philippe would
have turned all the people and took him and did him upon a cross and so on a
cross he dyed and went to ever lasting bliss Amen.

and he answered him and seyde from iherusalem and woll toward Rome. Thanne
seyde Daspas^an I am glad there of sore I have herd sey that there be many
go^d leches in that country. where fore I would well thou cowdis^e hele me.
And but if thowe do not he le me thou shalt be deed Tha^ answered he and

Emperor dyed and than was he chosyn Emperor and turned a yene to rome and
left Titus his sone there to distroye the Cite

Than Titus lay so fore to the cite that he enfamylde hem in so much that the
eton her schon and her botis and the fadir took mete from the sone and the sone
from the fadir and eythir took hit from otheris mouth the husbo^de from the
wyffe the wyff from the husbonde Tha^ among all other there was a woman of
great birthe and was come of gentill blood and had a young child and fore
hungir she seyde my dear child I have suffered much more pain for the than
ever thou dediste for me where for her is more reason that I ese my hunger on
the Tha^ though I dye and thowe both and so took her child and slew hit and
rostyd half of hit and kept half till on the morrow And than as the flesche
rosty^ the sauoure went in to the Cite and when the people felt the sauoure
they wend there had be plente of mete and come in to have had part and than
this woman would have hid hit. but they seyde they would se what mete she
had And tha^ she brought hit forth and shewde hit and seyde lo here I have
rostyd my own child and here is that other half a yense to morrow. Tha^ the
people were sore a gresid there of and all a mased of that sight and went
forth leuyng the woman etyng of her child Than hunger encresid so gretely
that there dyed with ynne the cite so thike that they cast the bodies over the
walls out of the cite in to the dikes and so filled the dikes full of deed
bodies and the stynke smote forth in to the country and enfectid the people
greatly Than so at the last great need made hem to yield up the cite Than titus
went in with his oste and right as the jews sold crist: for xxx. penyes so
they sold xxx. jews fore a penny and turned the cite up so down in so much
the y left not estone stondyng upon a nothir but distroied hit to the
vtermeste part Jo thus may ye se though that god almighty a bide and suffer
long he smyth sore at the last and takith great vengeance on hem that be
lusty to shede christian men's blood where for every christian man and woman a
mende hem self preyng to this holy apostles to be mediatoures between god and
hem that they may have verray repentance here in her hertis with shrift of
mouth and sassaction in deed doing that we may come to the bliss that never
shall have endyng Amen.

De inuencione sa^rte cruris.
^Ood frendis so (...)ht a day ye shall (...) have the inuenci(...) the holy
cross but ye shall not fast the even but come to god and to holy church as
criste^ people should do in worship of him that dyed on the cross Than ye shall
understand why it is callid Inue^cio erucis. the fyndyng of the cross the
which was found in this wise as I shall tell you when Adam our furste fadir
was sike for old and would feign have be out of this world Adam sent seth
his sone to the angel keeper of paradyse p^yng the angel to send him the oil
of mercy to anoynte his body with when he were deed Tha^ went seth to paradyse
and seyde his message to the angel Than answered the angel and seyde that he
might not have hit tille the yeris be fullfillid but have this branche of the
tree that thy fadir sinned ynne and serce hit one his grave and when hit berithe
fruit thann shall he have mercy and not erste Tha^ took seth this branche and
come home and found his fadir deed Than he set this branche on his fade r^s
grave as the a^gell bad him do the which branche goowed there till solomon was
king and he made fell hit down for hit was fair to the work of his temple But
hit would not cord with the work of his temple Salamon made to cast hit
down in to the earth and was hit hid there in time that the bishop of the
temple let make a wayre in the same place there the tree lay to wess^ in sheep
that were offered in the temple Than when this wayr was made they callid hit in
their langage Probatica piscina in the which watyr every day come an angel
from heaven and did worship to the ^tre that lay in the ground of the weyre and
meuyd the watyr and what man or woman that come in to the watyr next aftyr the
angel was made hole what sikenes that ever he had be virtue of the tree and so
endured many wyntres in to the time that criste was takyn and should be done
one the cross Than this tree by the ordenau^ce of god swa^ upon the watyr and
when the jews had none other tree ready to make the cross of fore great haste
that they had they took the same tree and made there of a cross and so did
our lord there on and than that tree bare that blessid fruit cristus own
body of the which wellith the Oil of mercy to Adam and to Eve and all other
of her of spryng But when crist was deed and was take down of the cross for
envy that the jews had to him they took the cross and to ij. other crosses
that the thefes were hong^d^ on eythyr side of criste and beried he m^depe in
the earth for criston people should not wete where y^ they were done for to do
hit worship And there it lay a year and more in to the time that Elene the
Emperes modir of constantyne gaderid great people to fight with maxencius at a
great watyuouer the which watye lay a great brigge for disceyte of conscantyne
maxencius let make a trappe hoppyng up and down so for to have disceyued
Constantyne that he should have fallyn in to the watyr and as Constantyne lay
in his b^d sore a ferde of maxencius for he was much bigger of people than he
was. than come to him an angel with a sign^ of the cross sheytrnyn^^s gold
and seyde to him* to morrow whannethon ghost to the battle take this sign in
thy hand and by the virtue there of thou shall have victon Thanne was
constantyne woundir glad and anon let make a Cross of the tree and to bear hit
to fore he^ to the battle But wha^ maxencius saw him nyghe the brigge he was
so feres of him self that he had for get the trappe the which he had made
him self and so come one the brigge and fill down in to the watyr by the
trappe and was drowned Tha^ was all his often woundir feign to yield hem to
co^stantyne with good will Than for Constantyne was not yet cristoned of him
and also he was helid of a leper that he had Than a none be counsel of the
pope he sent his modir queen Elene that was queen of iherusalem ^ preyde her
to go and seek the cross there crist dyed on. This Elene was a kings daughter
of England and the Emperor of rome weddid her for her beute and so she was
made emperes of rome But aftyr lxr husbondes death she had the kygdome of
iherusale^ to dowry where she made gadir all Jews that might be found and
seyde but if they would show her the cross they should all be burnt Tha^ was
there on of hem that highte judas and all seyde yt he knew best where the
cross was. Than seyde Elene to him. Si vis ninere ostende michi lignum crucia.
if thou would leu^ show me the cross that god dyed upon or else thou shalt
be burnt and so putt^ him to great distress.

Than he saw he mustened is tell or dye and seid to hem I be seche you let me
to the mount of Caluary there as I shall bide you and I shall show you the
cross of Criste for he was blind and might not se And so wha^ he was
brought to the mou^te of caluary he knelid down and preyde long and when he
had preyde the place there the ^rosse was menyd and the earth quoke and there

any spicery in the world. And than they diggid there long and at the last
they found there iij. crosses but tha^ wuste they notte which was cristus

the body rose to live and thankyd god Tha^ seyde this judas Thowe art criste
trewly and savior of all the world And aftyr that judas was cristoned a none
and was an holy man aftyr. Than took Elene a part of y^ cross and send hit

Than as we read we find in a cite that was callid Birectus a christian man hired

cowde that hit was not so ne never saw hit be fore that time yet not with

was a preuy christian man and had a rode preuely in his house Than anon come all
his mybo^^^^ wode forwrothe and all to bet this man and drew him and togged

is the image that thou beleuest upon And they took the image and beat hit and

ny^ted the sike people with this blood and a none they were hole than went

De festo sancti is hannis ante portalatinam
GOod frendis soche a day ye shall have seint iohan^ day at port latyne why is
this day callid so ye shall here. Hit happi^ as this day this holy seinte
prechid the word of god in a Cite that was callid ephesie the iusti^ of the
cite saw that he turned much people to the believe of Criste and would have
had him to do sacrifice to his false goddis and for he would not but rathir
lyse h^is lyffe. thanne this justice let take him and co^mau^ did him to be
set in p^son while he sent to the Emperor of Rome to wete what he should
do to him and when his letteres were come to the Emperor in the which
letteres he callid Johan all the worste that he could and said h^e was a false
disceyuer of th^e people thanne wrote the Emperor a yene to th^e justice and
bad he should send Johan a yen to him to Rome and so he did

And the Emperor apposed him o^ his dedis and johan stood stedfast^ in the
feythe and fore great skorne the emperor made clippe of sum of iohans here
of his head fore he had a fair head of here And when he was so clippid all the
people laughed him to skorne and so did him great dissese

And they ladde him to a yate of the town of rome the which is callid port
latyne and there they put him in to a tonne of fervent hot oil and closid
him there ynne and put under fire to have burnt him there in But for he was
goddis own derlyng he kept him so that he had no harm in no part of his
body tha^ when the people went y^ he had be deed they unclosed the tonne and
found him as hole and as found in all the partis of his body and clothis as
no thing had touchid him there for christian people let make a church there in
the worship of god and martyrdom that suffered there Than fore the Emperor
might not over come him by no wey of martyrdom nor penaun he exiled him in to
an isle that is callid pathmos Than herd seint johannes modir that her sone was
sent to rome fore to be deed for great sorrow and compassion of him sch^ went
aftyr to rome but whann she herd that he was exiled she turned a yene and
went home ward ^^d ^^ w^an s^^ come to a cite that was callid ^etu^am and
there she fill sike and dyed and there she was heryed be sides the cite in a
roge and when she had l^yne there many yery^ semte James her other sone come
thedir and took up his moderis body and hit smellid as sweet as any spiceey and
brought hit in to the cite and beried hit there with great worship and
honor. Amen

De festo sa^cti iobannis baptiste
GOod frendis soche a day ye shall have an high feste and an holy that is
callid seint iohans day the baptiste and is callid so for he baptized criste in
the watyr of flom Jordan where fore ye shall fast the even. And ye shall
understood and know how the euenys were first found in old time in the
beginning of holy church hit was so that the people come to church with cande
les brennyng and would wake and come with light to wards night to the church
in her deuocions and aftyr they fill to lecheery and songs dau^ces harpyng and
also fill to glotony and sin and so turned the holiness in to cursednesse
where fore holy faderis ordained the people to leave yt wakyng and to fast the
even and thus turned the wakyng in to fasting. But hit is callid vigilia that
is wakyng in English and yet hit is callid the even for at the euyne they were
wont to come to church But in worshipp^ of seinte johan the people woke at
home and made iij. manner of fyres on was clean bones and no wode and that is
callid a bone fire A nothir is clean wode and no bones and that is callid a
wode fire fore people to fit and to wake there by The thridde is made of wode
and bones and that is callid seint johan fire The first fire as a great
clercke Johan bellet tellith was in a certain country for in the country was
so great hete the which causithe the dragons go to gedyr in tokenyng that
Johan dyed in brennyng lone ^ charity to god and man. And they that dyen in
charity schalle have part of all good preyoures and they that do not schall
never be saved Than as this drago^s fleith in the air they shed down to the
wateres frothe of her kind and so enuenymed the wateres and causithe much
people to take her death there by and many diverse sikenesse Than on a time there
were many great clerkys and radde of king alisa ^der how on a time as he should
have a battle with the king of Inde and this king of inde brought with him
many olyfauntes beryng casteles of tree one her backs as the kynne of hem is to
have knights armed in the castle fore the battle Thanne knew alisau^dre the
kind of the olyfauntes that they drad no thing so much as the ^arryng of
swynne where for he made gadre to gedir all the swyne yt might be goton and
caused hem to be dreuyn as nigh the oly^au^tes as they might well here the
iarryng of the swyne and thann they made a pigge to cry and when the swynes
herd the pigge cry a none they made a great iarryng and as soon as the
olyfauntes herd that they began to fle each on and cast down the castellis
and slew the knights that were in he^ and by this mean Alisaundre had the
victory in this wise. Also these wise clerkys knew well that dragons hatith no
thing more than the s^enche of brennyng bones. there for they gaderid so many
as they might find and bre^de hem and so with the ^tenche there of they drove
awey the dragons and so they were brought out of great dissese. The secounde
fire was made of wode for that woll brenne light and woll be seyne far fore
hit is the chief of fire to be seyn fe^re in tokenyng that seint johan was a
lantern of light to the people. Also the people made blasis of fire fore they
should be seyne fer and specially in the night. Semt jeremy the prophet many a
yeris or johan was born he prophesied and spoke thus with godd is mouth and

Defesto sanctoru^ ^etri et panli.
(...)od frendis so (...)he a day ye shall (...) have the feste of (...) and
^oule and ye shall fast the even and on the morrow come to church and worship
god and prey to these ij. seyntes ^ were holy apostles to prey fore us. Our
lord has Petyr one his one side and Poule on that other side and he has his
woundis opyn and fresche bledyng schewyng to all manner of christian people that
he suffe^^d the woundis for us that bethe the v. wells of mercy that he
suffered for us ye shall understood that these ij. apostles were furste great
sinners.

But for they left her sin and were sorry and contrite and sinned no more our
lord took he^ in ensample to all other that woll leave sin they shall be sauyd
For he that is shreuyn and for sakith his sin mercy folowith that. and do his
penance and he shall have mercy and grace For as glad as the ^adir is to se
the sone rise from death to lyffe also glad is our lord. and much gladder to
se a man rise out of dedly sin and never to do hit more and therefore showing
by ensample Poule berithe a sword to all christian people to cut a weythe
cheynes of synn with his sharp sword of confession for this dedly sin
byndithe a man sore to the fend and there for cut awey that cheyne Petyr is
also ready to opyn the gatis of heaven to all crisien people and to take hem ynne
that woll fore sake her sin ye shall understood that pou^e was furste so
high and so ferse a yense all goddis servants that there durst no p^chour
dele with him but aftyr he left that great malice and there as he was ferse
aftyr he was gracious. And there he was be fore high and proud of heart aftyr
he was meke and lowly to all goddis servants. Petyr also held him self
most perf^te and steadfast of all cristus disciples where for he made boste by
a vain glory that he was ready to go to death with criste and seyde thus Hit be
houit me to dye with the and whann Criste seyde that all his disciples should
fore sake him Petyr for the great boste seyde though all men for soke him he
would not. And yet more over when criste was take Petyr drowe out his sword
and smote of a servants ere that hight mal cus But sone aftyr wha^ he saw
that criste was take and should be put to^e the tha^ he swear and starid that

and sorry for his tr^space. and there as he was a boster and unstable of his

leuyng in so much that crist callid him Petyr that i^ a stone in english For
there as thou leyeste a stone there thou shalt find hit so was petyr so sted
fast aftyr that nethir for well nor for woo he never fle tered but ever stood
stead fast in cristus law and had ever his synn in mind and to a mende that
he had do a mysse and was aftyr of great abstinaunce that he ete but bread and
oil wortes and full seldom flesche and wered but a singull kyrtell with a
ma^tell. And ever as oftyn when he herd any manner a man mind Ihesus a none
he be gonne to weep full sore. And when he herd any cokke crow a none he rose
up and would goo and prey and suffer penance and he wept many times so
bitterly that the teris of his eyes burnt his face in so much that were he
was he had a clothe in his bosom all wey to wype a wey the teris.

Thanne so following he was so holy that where that ever he went and he might

GOod (...) ^^ ch^ a day ye shall have the ^este of mary M^w deleyn that was so
