she was the furste in time of grace that did penance for she had lost grace
be fleschly lust where for she is made a mirror to all other syuers that woll
for sake sin and do penance they shall have grace the which was lost by
sin. She had a fadir that was a great lord and nigh of the kings blood and
had a great lordshippe in iherusalem the which he gaffe to lazarus his sone
and he gaffe mary the castle of maudeleyn with all the lordshippe longyng
there to. of the which castle she had her name and was callid Mary mawdeleyn
for sche was lady there of. Than as many bokys seyne saint ichan evangelist
weddid her and our lord bad him go with him and hepe his virginite and so he
did and was clean virgin. And than mawdeleyne went forth and gaffe her all
to sin in so much sche lost the name of mawdeleyne and was callid the
sinful woman But hit was oftyn seyn that our lord made of the grettyste
sinners the hoolyeste aftyrwardes and so when our lord saw time he gaffe
this woman grace to know her self and to have repentannce for her sins Than
when mary herd that criste was at a man's house that was callid Simon the
pharise sche took a box with oyneme^t soche as the people vsid that time for
hete of the son and went thethir but she durst not for schame go to fore
him but at his fete be hynde him and hard him speak and thann sche took a
great soww in her heart and wept tenderly and so with the teris of her eyes
sche wosche cristus fete. and with the here of her head sche wyped hem and with
all the love of her heart she kyssid he^ and a noynted hem but no word she
spoke that any man might here but softely in her heart she cride mercy and made
a vow to him that she would never trespace more. Tha^ our lord ihesu had pire
on her and cast out of her vij. fendes and for gaffe her all her sins in
heryng of all that there were. tha^ she took soche a love to criste that she
left all he lordshippis the castle of maudeleyn with all other goodis and
sewid him for the with great love that in his passion there as his disciples
fley a wey from him she left him never till she with help of other had leyde
him in his tomb And when no man durst goo thedir for the knights that kept
him she spared not Cumtenebre esse^t when hit was myrke in the dawnyng sche
took with her sweet bawmes to a noynte cristus body with thus she shewid soue
both in will and deed where for criste in his live for her love he lid martha
her sustre of the read flixe that she had vij. year to fore and pyned her full
sore Et resuscitauit lazarum a mortuia and resid lazar her brothir from death
to lyffe that had ley iiij. days stynkyng in his grave And when our lord rose
from death to lyffe he apperyd to her and suffered her to touch him and kiss
his fete. Than when hit was knowyn to the jews that criste shewde her so many
tokenes of lone for all other Than when criste was styed up to heaven the jews

De sancto lauren cio martire.
GOod frendis soche a day ye shall have seint Laure^ day goddis own holy
martyr his martird ome as maxiuis seyth shynith to all holy church and
lyghtenith all the world. where fore ye shall come to god and holy church and
schall fas;^e the even* this senite was holy in leuyng and great in compassion
of stryng Sei^t^ Austeyn seythe that ensample i^ doing is comendable^ than is
preching and techyng There for seint La^rence gaffe all christian people to
schewe a yense malice meekness and a y^^ e^uetyse largeness a yense

enquerid fast aftyr pore people and went to hem and gaffe hem mete and dryn^e
and clothis so he come to a wedowes ^ouse there as was much pore people loggid
the which wedowe had belo^ge sike on the head ache Than Laurence had
co^^assion of her and made her hole and mekely wosche all the pore people fete

there be side in a place that was blind he went the^ir and helid him So ever

beried hit with great lame^tacion. thus la^rence sheude mekenes a yens malice

great love y^ he had to god made him set naught by all his tourmen^s y^ were
do* to his body Seint gregory tellith how there was a p^ste that hight staculus
and was ^ely to me^de a church of seint laurence that was disiroyed with

and he preyde to god and seint laurence besily of help and tha^ he lokid in to
an ouyn and fo^de hit full of new wh^re bread but he went h^^ would have
seruid he^ but fore a weke and hit fo^de ^^^^y now all the time his work was a
making

we find y^ there was an emperor that a cursed man of leuing and when he was
deed there come a leg^o^ of fendes to fech him and as they come by a holy
ermytes selle they made a great noise the ermyte had great marvel there of and
opened a wyndow and spoke to on that come be hind and askid in the name of god

wha^ his sins were leyde in the balau^ce and was ny over come than come that
brennyng deko^ laurence and leyd a great pot on the balau^ce and hit drew up all
to gedir thie post was a great chelyse y^ the Emperor made in the worshipp^
of seint laurence by that he was saved. Thus ye may see and learn to make in
sufferaunce a yense enuyous people also what merit and mede is in largeness
to give hem that has need and what joy and merit hit is to suffer
tribulacion and persecucione and dissese patiently learn of the holy marti^
seint laurence and late us take him for a mirror and prey to him that he woll
be mediator to god for us that we may come to ever lasting bliss Amen

De assumptione beat marie nirginis.
GOod frendis soche a day ye shall have the assumpcion of our lady and hit is
callid so for that day her sone took her up in to heaven body and soul and
crow^^ed her queen of heaven for the angel of heaven come to fette her up
Angelis yoyng and singyng come with procession a yense her with roses and
lilies of paradyse in tokening that she is rose and lely and flower of all
wymmen. and they did homage to her for all angelis and seintes in heaven made
joy and melody in worshipp^ and hnoure of her and so holy church makith mind
of her assumpcion. And yet the gospel of that day makithe no mention but of
ij. sustres that was martha and mary mawdeleyne and said thus. Iutrauit ^hesus
in ^uada castellu^ et mulier ^da^ ^c^. Ihesus entered in to a castle and a
woman y^ was callid martha that took him in her house and she had a sustre that
was callid mary that sat at cristus fete and herd him speak Tha^ was martha
besy to serve criste and sche seyde to him sire bid my sustre a rise and help
me. tha^ answered criste. maria m^liore^ parte^ e legit aue no^ anfere tur abea
Mary has chose the better part y^ shall notte be take a wey from her these be
the words of the gospel of that day and here be no words of our lady as be
seming But he that redith what seint ancesme seyth there he may se that the
gospel pertenith all to our lady and to the l^uing of her. for she was the
castle yt ihu^s entered in to for right as a castle has diverse propertees
that longith to a castle that hit should be mighty and strong right so was
our lady be for all other women. For there as women be fre ell and feeble ^ esy
to over come our lady was strong as a castle and a yen stood the can tells of
the fendes engynnes and put hem be side at all times for right as a castle
has first a deep dike right so had our lady a deep meekness in strenght of
the castle in so much she passid all other in virtue of meekness wherefore god
chose her to b^niodir to his sone be fore all other wymen. and there to criste
berith wittenes thus. Quia respexit bu^ilitate^ a^cille su^ for god be held
the makenesse of his hand mayde^ all generation shall bless me This dike if
it be full of water hit is the more strong to the castle this water is
compassion that a man should have for his sins and to other people dissessed
This water had our lady On this dike lithe a draw brygge that shall be draw
up a yen^ en^myes and let down ^ yense friends be this brigge ye shall
understand discrete obedience for right as a man shall notte late down the
brygge to his enmy though he bid him so man shall not let ^he fend come to
his soul though he tempte him But a none as he is bid any thing that is
help and socoure to his soul tha^ shall he let down the brygge of
obedience and the sonner the better thus did our lady wha^ the angel Gabriell
come to her of co^cepcion of her sone she let not down the brygge a none till
she knew were he was a friend or a enmy and said she should co^ceyue and be a
maid and by the v^w of chastity that she made to fore and as she herd y^ she
let down the brigge of obedience and seyde Ecce ancilla dm^ etc^ Lo here
goddis own hand maiden be it do to me aftyr thy word. This castle is treble
walled. The furste wall be took nithe wedloke fore furste she was wyffe to
joseph for else the jews would have stoned her as for a l^chour if she had
conceived with out wedloke and so the furthir wall be tokenith patience and
the ynner virginite that is may denhode but that is litill worth but hit be
strengith with the wall of patience and litill help is fore mandenhode hit is
lityll worth that can no thing suffer of persecucion nor disseses but ever
playng ^^grochyng and to be a claterer a iangeler a curser and a waryer and a
scolde of her tongue t^ese defend not ma^denhode but rathir cast hit down for
may denhode should be of few words and that she spekith should be honest and
worship both to her own person and to all that be in her p^sence. For hit
is an old englische a maiden should be said and not herd this vera^ had our
lady. For senit Bernard seythe read all the gospel over and thou shall not
find that our lady in all her lyf^e spoke but iiij. times by her own but as
schewas causith The first to gabriell the ij. to elisabeth the iij. to her own
sone in the temple and the iiij. at the weddyng of cane galilee. Thus must the
wall of patience defend the wall of maydenhode This wall of maydenhode and
hit be well kept hit is passing all other. As Bede seythe wedloke is high
there as hit is well kept but yet wedowehode is higher. but virginite passith
all and has most worship in heaven passing all other This wall kept our
lady fore schewas clean both be free will and by a vow and she had a degree
passing all other maydenes that ever were nor never shall be for sch^was both
maiden and modir. And in this castle is a yate that be tokenith feythe for
right as hit is in possible fore a man to go thourgh a wall of stele right so
hit is as in possible fore a man to plese god with out feythe

This feythe had our laby passing all other fore as hit semyth in possible for
a woman to conceive with out carnal concupiscencion of man for hit was never
sey be fore but be techyng of an angel she believed and so come criste and
entered be yates of be leave in to the castle yt is in to the body of our lady
This yate had a toure a boue be tokenith charity For that is a boue all things
and that virtue had our lady well may she be callid a castle For right as all
manner people fle in to a castle both old and young for dread of enemies in so
much that the least child that can cry or speak that is a ferde of any thing
a none cries lady lady for socoure and help for she is socoure and help both
to young and to old less and more in sike and in health The holy ghost is
capteyn of this castle. and his knights be holy angel^e that go with our lady
night and day In this castle be ij. sustres martha and mary mawdeleyne Martha
recepit il lum in domu^ ^^ am. Martha received him in to her house and was besy
to serve him and that other satte stille and had great lust to here him speak.
Be these ij. sustres I understand ij. manner of leuyng of the people that one
is actyfe and that other contemplatyf martha be tokenith actyfe that is be
synes in this world But that should be for cristus sake that is to receive pore
people in to his house and to give hem mete and drink clothe herborowe visit
hem that be in prison comfort the sike crooked blind and lame and to bery the
deed. be that other I understand the contem platyf lyffe that is to people of
holy church that should void in all yt they may this worlds besines and give
hem to all spiritu all occupacion and though they do thus yet there be coueytus
people of this world that said that it is all lost that me^ of holy church
h^n for hit semyth to hem they do no good but ever compain on hem and sey
they do no good Seynte Austeyn seythe that all the world is holy church and
these worldly people hatith me^ of holy church But yet god answerith for hem
and is her voket and so woll at all times while they leave in rest and pese
with ynne hem self But now see how our lady full fillythe both these lives.
She was first martha forther as martha was besy to receive criste in to her
house our lady received him in to her body and there in he was ix. monthus and
she feed him and aftyr come pore and nakyd in to this world and sche gaffe him
mete and drink of her pappes and so fed him and wha^ he was nakid she
clothid him and norisched him. and when he was sike be hynde of youth she heli^
him and when he was boundyn hand and foot in his cradell as in prison she come
to him and vnbou^de him^ and took him and ^elid his soris with the milk of her
pappes. and when he was deed she help to bery him in his tomb and thus she
full fillithe the office of martha perfourmyng the vij werkys of mercy. and yet
she was many time too beled in her heart ^ohan she must bear him from country
to country that was full of mawmentes and there as she knew no man. and when
that she saw him takyn and bound strepe nakyd beton with stour ges that all
his body ran with stremes of blood and naylid on the cross and so do to
death that was to her ^ great troble. thus was our lady actyffe for as the
gospel tellithe she gaffe so great delight to her sons words that she bare in
her heart all the lyffe and techyng of criste in so much that she taught the
iiij. eua^gelistes mark ma ^h^w ^uce and Johan much of yt they wreton and
namely seint Luke for he wrote much of the ma^hode of criste. and thus she
fulfillid the office of mary for hit was for the best wha^ her sone was styed
up in to heaven sche le^te all her besynes and gaffe her all to contemplacion
till her sone fette her out of this world. Thus every man yt can understood may
se that this gospel is co^uement to be radde for hit touchithe the lyffe of
our lady Tha^ for this day was the end of her lift in this world. there fore
holy church redithe this gospel in ensample to all criste^ people to
perform the same leuyng in as much as they may and as god woll gene hem
grace to serve our lady y schall give you ensample



we find of a clerk yt loved our lady well for he radde of her b^wte he had
great lust to see her and preyde besely that he might onys se her or that he
dyed. Tha^ at the last come there an angel and seyde to him fore thou seruyst
our lady so well thou schalt have thy pre your but on think y tell the if
thou se her here in this world thou schalte lose thy sight for the great
clernesse of her Than seyde he I wot well safe so that I may se her.

Than seyde the Angel come to soche a place and thou schalte se her thann was
he glad and thought that he would hyde his on eye and lokyd with that other So
wha^ he come to the place he leyde his hand over that one eye and saw her with
that other eye and so come our lady and he saw her and she went her wey a none
and he was blind with that one eye and saw with that other. tha^ the sight
likid him so well that he would feign se her a yene and preyde night and day
that he might se her a yene. Than seyde the a^ gell if thou se her a yene thou
shall lose the sight of that other eye and he seyde y wot well saffe thou ghe
I had a thousand eyon Than come to soche a place and thou shall se her so when
he come he saw her Than seyde our lady to him my good servant when thou saw me
first thou lost thy one eye how wolte thou do now when thou haste lost thy
other eye Thann seyde he dear lady I wot well saffe though I had a thousand
eyon. Tha^ seyde our lady for thou haste so great liking to me thou shall have
thy fight with both eyon a yene as well as thou had diste and better and so he
had Than served he our lady ever aftyr to his lives end and went to ever
lasting joy and bliss to which god bring us all to Amen.

De sancto bartholomeo.
GOod frendis soche a day ye shall have the feste of seint Bartholomew goddis
own apostle and ye shall fast the even and come to church and here your
seruyse in the worship of god and seint bartholome ye shall understand that
bartholome is as much to sey as Fill in ^s uspe^ dentiame That is to sey the
sone hanging upon me or upon wate^^s than ye schall understand that god is he
that hongith upon the watres in ij. weyes. The first is when he hongith upon
the clouds in the ^irmament till he se time to late hem down Anothir wey he
hongith upon w^ teres when a man or a woman is sorry for his sins and weping
sore for his trespace and bitterly Thanne god takith his teris and ha^ gith hem
upon the high hill of heaven where all the seintes in heaven may have hem in
fight in great joy to all seintes and all angels y^ ben in heaven wha^ they
may se man or woman that has do a mysse many trespass to for sake her sin and
turn to no more there to fore of the teris of a man or woman that is sorry for
his sin in this manner quenchithe the fuyre of hell of this te ris spekith
Johan criso stome and seythe. O thou tere that art mekely let in oryson and
preyour with good devotion the might is so great that thou ghost to heaven and
takyste the word of the jews mouth making him to turn the to saluacione ^
be fore were in the wey of dampnacion also thou makist thy^accusars dom the
fendes and so thou^ q^^chist the fy^e of hell that fendes ma(...)die a yense thy
coming (...) god hongith upon (...)tres. Than fore seint bartholome was goddis
sone as all ben that seruith him he was honging up in iij weyes in devotion of
holy orisones preyng and in feythe full monicion and in sufferyyg of passione
he was honging to godwar de in devout* orison fore that he seyde wit his
mouth he did with his heart so that his heart was all wey hongyng up toward
god both in word and in dedeas the p^ste seyth in the mass. Sur^um ^orda
holds up your hertis to god ^hus this holy man seint bartholo me had ever
his heart to god for great devotion. we find wreton of him thus that he knelid
an C times on the day and a C. times on the night fore great (...)cio^ that he
had to god But for he should not be weary of the travel god sent an angel
ever more to sew him and kept him thus hanged he up be holy orisens preyng. He
was also hanged up be the feythfull monicion in this wise fore god gafe him so
great power ouyr all findis that be his holy monicion he suspendyd hem whedir
they were in man or woman And al so in other mawmentes. we find wreton of
semte bartholome how he come in to ynde in the temple in the which temple was
an image and there in was a fend a mawment that was callid astroth and this
image was made of gold than the fend that was there ynne spoke to him and did
him worshipp^ and by soche words as he spoke he made the people be leave that he
was god and yet the more be leave to the people that he helid many sike men and
wym^n both blind crokid and lame and of many diverse sikenesse that he had
cast^ upon hem to fore him self and so semyng to hem that they were ^eli^ by
him but soche sikenes as god sent upon hem he cowde not hele Thanne was the
temple full of sike people that was brought to this mawment to be made hole
but as soon as bartholome come to the temple he suspended the fendes power that
he might hele no man not there was a nothir mawment callid barth askid hem why
her god gaffe hem none answer he sey de bartholome the apostell of god has
bound him so sore that he dare not onys speak nor crake than told him the
fetru^ of barth and seyde he know every word that he speak now for he has an
angel of god with and tellith him all things that ever was said or down be
him And more over though ye seek him ye shall not find him but if he woll him
self. Than went they home a yene and sought bartholome and might not find
him. Than as bartholome walkid a mo^ ge the people ^ mad man that had ^ fend
with in him a none cride to bartholome goddis own apostell thy preyoures bind
me so sore and brenne me also Than seyde bartholomew hold thy pese thou* fend
and goo out of that man and with that word the fend went his wey and left
the man and a none he was hole Thanne hit happid so that the king of that cite
had a daughter that was mad and sore bounden with cheynes for harm that she
deed among the people And when the king herd how this man was helid a^ none
he sent to bartholomew preyng him that he would hele his daughter and so he
did. Thanne bartholomew prech^d so the king that he turned the king to be
christian and than a none he co^m^undid to draw down the mawmentis that were in
the temple Tha^^ the pepull tied ropis a bout the images neckis and wol de have
draw hem down the mawmentes but they might not for the fend was so strong in
hem

Than Bartholome co^maundid the fendis to come out of the images and to pull
hem to poudir and so they did for they had no power to withstond his
commandment and so they all to brake hem for the temples was so full of sike
people bartholomew preyde to god that they might be hole and a none they were
hole euerycho ne Than come there an Angel that god sent fr^ heaven and a none
in the sight of all the people the temple shone so brighte that no tongue co^de
tell and fly all a boute the tempull And in four partis of the tempull he
made a syne of the cr^^with his fingeres on the walls and seyde right as all
the people be hole of her sikenes so shall this temple be closid from all the
filthe of sin and of the fendes craft that has be there in and I woll show
you that same fend y^ ye have worshippid fore your god Tha^ the fend apperid
like a man of ynde all black and made a cursed noise Than the people began to
fle for fere he was so lo thely* Than seyde the angel make soche a sign of
the cross in your forhedis and be not a ferde of him Than a none in fight of
hem all the angel vnbou^ de this fend and bad him go there as was nostering
nothir of man nor of best and to be there till at the day of dome and never
dissese the people more. tha^ the fend went his wey and the angel stied up
in to heaven. Than the king his wyffe his daughter and all his meyne and much
other people turned to the feythe and bartholome cristoned hem all. thus
bartholome hongith be feythfull monicion for he suspended the fendes pouer that
he might do nothing He was also ho^gid up be suffering of passion for wha^ the
bishop of the temple saw that the people were all most turned to christian
feyth and left the fendes mawmetry he we^ te un to the cite there as a king was
callid astrages and brothir to the king Polmyes and playned to him sore and
said there was a man come to hem that was callid bartholome that had turned his
brothir and all the people to the feythe that they set not by her goddis.
But had draw hem down and all to broke hem and hallowed the temple only to
criste. for this cause he prey de him of help Thanne sent the king ^ M. me^
aftyr bartholome. Tha^ when bartholome was come he astud him why he had turned
his brothir and made him be leave one a deed man that was hongid on the cro^^^
tha^ seyde ^^rtholome I have bou^dyn that god that thy brothir believed on and
shewde that send And if thou or he maiste do so to my god than wolle y believe

And othere ^oo of diverse scy^t^s

And as a good holy man come by the cite and he saw a great company of men

we find of our lady how there was a jew that was borne in france and come
in to England for diverse matters that he had to do with other people and come
in glo^ater and to Bristow and so would go in ^o wilke show but he was take by
the wey with the fes and ladde in to an old house and boundyn to a post and
his hondis be hynde him and so left him there all night and at the last he
^^ll in a sleep he saw a fair woman clothid in white he had seyn never non
soche and enyn there with he woke and felt him self lose Than he saw our lady
bright that him thought she passid the son and seyde what lady art y^ and
she seyde I am mary that tho^ and thy nation dispison and seyn that I bare
never goddis sone. But yet am I come now to bring thy out of thyn error and
out of prison that thou art ynne and there for come thou with me and stand
yonder at the stone and look downewarde and so he did and there he saw the
horrible peynes of hell that he was nygh out of his mind Thann said our lady
to him these be the peynes that been ordained to all the that woll not be leave
in my sons passion and in the feith of holy church yet comforthe and se more
and she set him on an high hill and shewde him a place of great joy and
myrthe in so much that he was rebaschid with that sight Thanne s^yde our lady
Lo these be ordeynede to all y^ beleuyn in the incarnacio^ of criste and that
he was born of me* and I clean maiden before and aftir. and that my sone shede
his blod for all mankind. Now haste thou seyne both joy and pain chese
which thou haddiste leaves Than he went much of the night he woste not what
wey but walked forth. But on the morrow he come to bathe and there he was
cristoned and named johan and aftyr was an holy man Than^ to come a gain to
our purpose of our lady what time that Ioachim had offered our lady in to
the temple to the bishopp^ to keep her saffe in ward till shewere xij. year of
age and more. Than must the bishop ordeyne her an husbonde and than they let
cry all about in the country that kings lordis and other ge^tils that were
with out wyses should come at a ^^^tayn day for to wete who were best worthy
to wedde that fair maiden that was flower of all maidens. for right as the
lely is white and fair a mouge breris and other flowers right so was our
lady among other maidens so when they come to ^he^a salem to se the maiden
that was of the best blood of the world the bishop ordained an old staff
of asche that he had kept in the temple many yeris and was all worm ^ton and
he seyde he that ha^delid that staff and hit bor genyd and bare flowers he
schulde have the maiden and sche was brought forth in to the temple that all
the people might see her Than bad the bischopp^ bring forth the staff. and
when any man handild hit he bad him hold upon high that the people might se
if hit burgemd Than went to kings princes lords and knights squiers and
other gentill men but hit would not be the furste day ne the second day so the
iij. day they schulde make an end. the come there an old man in to the temple
and had herd of this but he saw hit not and thought to go to se how the
people did and come thedir and stood all far in a corner and lokid on this
maiden. Thenn he thought in him self I will not handell the staff for this
maiden is not for me that is so passing fair and I so passing old. thann come
there a white dove and satte upon his head with a gyldin bille and her fete
sihone as hit had be bright burnischid gold that all the people saw her and
sum would have caught her but they might not. Than was the bischoppe ware and
bad joseph come up to him a none and joseph seyde nay she is not for me. sche
is to young and I am to old to govern her a state Thann seyde the bishop
handell this staff and so he did and a non hit was grene and be ganne to
burgyn and bare leuys and blossomed and bare fruit Than was the bishop glad
and joseph sorry for to have her for he was full purposed never to have wife.

Thanne the Bishop. weddid hem worshipfully and bad joseph take her home with
him and so he did Tha^ sone aftir the holy ghost lightid in her with greting of
the angel gabriell and so be gane to wexe great with child Than joseph lokid
one her and thought to have go a wey preuely from her and leave her alone Than
come an angel to joseph and bad he should take mary to his keeping and stodynd
more there upon and leave all soche thought is fore y^ was goddis will and god
him self woll that hit be so Than he left all soch fantasies and kept her
well as a man should his wife

De exaltaco^e sancte crucia
GOod frendis soche a day ye shall have holy rode day in the which ye shall
come to church in worship of him that was done one the cross this day is
callid Exaltacio crucia the exaltacion of the cross that is ^^ say the lyftyng
up of the holy cross when seint Elene had fette the cross in iherusalem
christian people did hit great worship But than come the king of perse that was
callid cosdre and he took the cross with him and made the cite bare and bare a
wey all y^ he might and went in to the temple and took all the tresoure and
jewel is and precious stonis and bare hem a wey. Thus this cursed man did
distroye many kingdoms and so bare the holy cross in to his own country Than
the emperor Eraclius herd here of and was full wroth and sorry and sent to
this king Cosdre to trete with him fore Eraclius was a christian man Than Cosdre
answered cursedly and seyde he would not trete till he had all his people to
for sake cristendome and to do sacrifice to his mawmentes Than this Emperor
Eraclius be took all to god and gadered him an oste of people to fight with
this cursed king cosdre hoping to god to get the holy cross a yen But when
this cursed king cosdre come he fill in soche a fansasy and madness that he
took his sone all the governance of his reme and let make an house for him
self in manner of an auter like un to heaven and made hit all shyning gold and
p^cious stones and set him self in the myddis in a cheyer of gold and
co^mau^did that all people should call him god and so satte and the holy
cross in his right hand instead of his son and one the left hand a tame
cock instead of the holy ghost and him self in the middi^ instead of the
trinite. and thus he satte like a mad man Than his sone her de that Eraclius
was coming he went a give him and met him at a great water over the which
water was a brygg^ than be^ assent of both her h^ stis they set bother chief
cayns a mids the brigge to fight fore hem all and both ends of the brigge
should be draw up and which of hem that had the victory should have both
kingdoms Tha^ was Eraclins so in full feyth in the cross and trust in the
preyoures of the people that he over com his enemies Than all Cosdres people be
stering of the holy ghost that they turned to the feythe be fre will of hem
self and when they were all cristo ned than went Eracli us with both ostis to
the old king Cosdre as he satte in his trone and said to him thus. For because
thou haste do worship to the holy cross you shalt chese if thou wolte be cri
stoned and have thy kingdom a yen for a litill tri bute in rest and pese or
else to be deed and he for soke to be cristoned than a non Eraclius smote of
his he de right there and made a cry that his tree four should be dalte a monge
his men and ^cious stones and other iewles should be kept to restore the
chirchis that were distroyed and took the cross and went to iherusalem And
when he come to the mount of oliuete toward the cite of iherusalem ryding
one a trapped horse he would have rydyn in to the cite of iherusalem ^ut
suddenly the yati^^^^ to ge dir and was plain wall tha^ was he greatly a stoyned
and meruelyd gretely of y^ vengeance and made a great moan Than come an angel
and stood on the ya it is and seyde Qua^do^rex noster. when the king of heaven
come this wey and thourghe these yati^ to wards his passion he rode on no
trapped horse nor in no clothe of gold but mekely one a simple ass y^uy^g
ensample of meekness to all people. than the angel went his wey Tha^ the
king with all devotion that could and might a none did of his clothis un to his
shirte and bare foot Than the yate ope^^d and he went ynne to the yate of
iherusalem and so in to the temple and offered the cross a yene as hit was to
fore Tha^ for the great joy that the people had of this cross. and ^o^^ the
great miracles y^ good showed hit was more (...) ^ft^r tha^ hit (...) to ^^re
and the ^^^ ship of the cross that was cast down aftyr was lift up where
this this day is callid the ^^altacion of the cross ^^re as seint Austeyn
seythe. the cross that was furste of so great spite and velony now is of great
worship that Emperors kings worship hit we ^^de in legenda aurea that aie
we come to a church and for de^aute that no man was in the church he we^ te
to the rode and for g^^t en uye that he had to cri^^^ he cut the rodis throat
and a none the blood sterte out one his clothis and so his clothis were all
read blood And than he hid the rode in a preuy place and as he went home a
christian man mete him and sey de to him thou haste slay ne sum man where haste
thou done him and the jew said nay hit was not so and the christian man said thy
clothis be all blody of him. Than this jew knelid down and seyde for sothe
the god yt this christian people be leave upon is of great virtue and might and
told him how he had dove and cryde mercy with all his heart and so he was
cristoned and an holy man ^uer aftyr and so went to ^uer lasting joy and
bliss to the which god bring us all to Amen.

De quatuor temporum
GOod fre^dis this weke ye shall have ymbre deyes. yt is wedenysday friday and
satirday the which days calixte the pope ordey ned iiij. times in the year to
all y^ bethe of couenable age for certain cau ses as ye shall here. Our old
faderis fastid four times in the year a yense four high and solemn fe stis
and if we woll show us good children we must fast and follow the same rewle
that they vsid and there fore we fast iiij. ty mes. Furste in march. The
secounde at witson tide The iij. bytwix her ueste and sede time And the iiij.
be fore cristemas March is a time that dryethe up the moystenes that is in the
earth where for we fast that time to dry the earth of our body of humerus
that be full needful to the body and to the soul. For that time the humurus
of le chery temptith a man mo ste of any time of the ye re Also we falte at
witfontyde fore to get grace of the holy ghost that we may be in per^ite love
and charity to god and to all the world Caritaa cooperit multitudiue^
peccatoru^ Charity co uerith the multitude of sins Also we fast to have
mekenes in our her it is and to put a wey all pry de that reynith in us. Al so
we fast between herueste and sedtyme for to have grace to gedir fruits of good
werkis in to the house of our conscience and so be ensample of good leuyng a
monge the people that we common with both rich and pore. Also we fast in
winter fore y^ sleith all stinkyng wedis of sin and foul earth of fleschly
lusts that makid good angelis and good people to with draw hem from us For
right as net tell b^^nnith rosis and other flowers that be nigh hit in the same
wise a vicious man or woman sterith and settith on fire hem that bi^h in her
company. And for these causes we ^aste iiij. times in the year and every time
iij. days that be tokenith iij. special y^ tues that he lpith a man to grace
that is fasting devout preyng and alms deed doing And be opinion of much
people these days be callid ymbre days because that ou re elder faderis would
one these days ete no bread but cakis made under as kis so be the etyng of yt
they reducid in to their mind that they were but asks and should turn aye^
and wyste not how sone. and by that they turned a wey from all delicius me it is
and drynkys and took no head so that they had esy ^ustinaunce this causithe
hem to think on death and that will cause a man to desire no more tha^ he ne
dith and absteyne him self from all manner of bodily lusts and to encrese in
ver tue^be the which we may come to ever lasting blys

De festo sacti ma they.
GOod friend is so ^he a day ye shall have seint mathe u^ ^ay the which was
^^^^tus apostle and ye shall f^^ste the even and come to holy church in
worshipp^ of god and seint matthew he is greatly co^mendid in holy church for
certeyn^ holy virtues that he had Hewas obedient to criste at the first
calling he prechid the gospel with out faynyng and he suffered passion mekely
with out any deuyyng Furste he was obedient to criste at the first calling
for he satte in a certain place besy to get good and cris^ come that wey and
lokyd on him and bad him come and go with him Thann he cast so great love to
cris^ that he left all his goodi^ that he had and sewed criste forth full
simple and full pore. Also he fed criste gladly for on a day he preyde Criste
to ete with him and made criste a great feste not in delicat^ metis and drynkys
But i^* fedyng criste and all his co^pauy for he fed all that would come for
cristns sake for much people sewed crist where that ever he went Secuti sunt
eum turhe multe For diverse causes many followed him sommto be helid of her
sore^ and of diverse sikenes And sum to se miracles y^ criste did sum to
the and to drink with him. and sum that were his enemies that were learned in
the law if they might have takyn him with any word where by they my g^te
have accusid him. and sum to be reformed in virtues and to here his doctrine
and teching as the apostles and many other ^nde nersua Moribus signa cibua
blasphemia doctrina fuere Causa ^um dominum turba secuta fuit And when matthew
had fed ^^ist thus and all that come him criste made him on of his disciples
and gaffe him knowing to preche the be leave and gods word so boldly ever
aftyr y^ he spared nothir fore love nothir for dread. So this matthew apostell
como on a time in to a cite and prechid that was callid Nadabar and there he
found much people taught be the fendes craft in nigransy and taught so
many things and so marvelous that hit was great woundre to here to many man's
wit and all for the people should be leave in hem and do hem worship Thanne
mathewe a none delivered her nigramansy so that all the people knew openly that
hit was the fendes craft where for this people that be leued on this
nigramansy made dragones by the fendes craft to spitte fire and breune so that
the stenche of hem slew much people and they brought this dragones to have
devoured seinte matthew and when mathewe herd there of he made a cross be
fore him and went a yense hem and a none the dragones fill down deed be fore
him. Than seyde matthew to the people if ye have any might reyse hem a yene to
live but they had no power. Than seyde matthew if I were not god dis servant I
would make hem to do you that as ye purposed to do to me. But hit is the
techyng of my maystre ihesu criste to do good a yense evil where fore I bid
you dragons a rise and go to soche a place as ye shall never grieve man nor
best and a none they rose and went her wey. thus matthew turned much people
that come to se that sight. and thanne^ he prechid the people and told hem of
the joy of paradyse There he seyde is day and never night the ^^ is ever
youth and never age there is ever health and never sikenesse there is roses
lylyes and flowree with o^^tewel owyng there b^ popyngaeys and nyghtyngales and
diverse briddes ever singyng love rest and pese with ever lasting charity So
they that leuyth in criste and do aftyr his commandment shall come the their
and be there without endyng. Thus he prechid in a cite where cursed people
were they took him and put out his eyon and cast him in to prison till they
took a visement what death he should dye. But there come an angel thanne to
seint Andrew as he prechid in a far country and brought him over the se
there as seint matthew was and when Andrew saw matthew so foul done a non Andrew
wept and preyde to god for him And a none god restorid matthew his sight a yene
and Andrew went a yen in to his own country to ^reche there as he c^ome fro
and when matthew was out of prison he went and prechid in the cite of Nadabar
in the which the kings sone dyed Than sent the king aftir matthew ^preyde him
to restore his sone to life a yene and so he did where for the king and his
wyffe and his daughter that was callid eufagema took cristendome and the most
part of the people and for god had chosyn this eu fagema to be an holy woman
matthew blessid her and gaffe her the veil of chastity and charit^ and so was
aftyr an holy womo^ and was keeper of many other virgins than dyed her fadir
Thanne come there a king that was callid hertagus that loved this maiden
Eufageme and preyde matheco to help him that he might have her Tha^ seyde
matthew that might not be fore she was weddid to the king of heuene and m^yght
flot break that spouse hode the was her tacus wroth and bad sle matthew and so
as he stood and seyde mass at the Auter there come on be hynde him and slew
him and christian people beried the body in the same church. Than bad the king
set fuyre on eufagema house and that on every side to have brende her there
in. Than matthew apperid to her and bad her be a good there and a none turned
the fuyre from her house in to the kyngis palyse and left there no thing save
the king and a young child with him and the king was smetyn with meselry so
foul that fore great pain and woe he slew him self and so the vengeance fill
on him self that he would have do to other Now ye may well se by this great
miracles that he was an holy man and therefore late us serve him and he wolle
prey for us all Amen.

De festo sa^cti michaelia
GOod frendis such a day ye shall have seint michae^^ day the archa^gell that
day all holy church makithe mind and mention of all angelis for the great
socoure comfort and help that mankind had of angelis and specialy of seint
michaell And for iij. p^rogatiuis that he had for he is wou^drefull in apperyng
marvelous in miracles worchyng and victorious in fightyng he is woundrefull in
appering for as seint Gregory seith when almighty god woll wor^he any
woundrefull deed than he sent for michaell his servant as for his banerer
fore he berith a shield a sign of his arms. where fore he was sent with
moses and Aaron to egipte to wo^che meruelis for though the sign were in
moses the worchyng was done by michaell. For he de* partid the read see and
kept the water in ij. parties while the people of israel went thourghe and
so passid and ladde hem forth to flom jordan and kept the water like an hill
of each side hem while they passid save and sound to the land of be he^t^
Also michael is keeper of paradyse and takith in souls that bithe sent the dir
Also he shall sle antecrist in the mount of olyuete and he shall bid all the
deed a rise and come to the dome and other angelis with him shall bring all
the instruments of his passion the cross the crown spear nails hamer sponge
eysell g^all scorges and all other thyngis yt was at cristus passion to show
hem that shall be dampened that set naught ne believe not in his passion thus
it apperith wou^drely. Also he worchid miracles meruelously for appolia is an
high hill that is callid gargus and is nyghe a great cite and there dwellid a
rich man of diverse catell and as his bestis went one the hill^ there happid
a balle left be hynde other bestis tha^ went this man and his servant to
seek this bolle and found him stondyng be fore an hole in a great dene and
than on of hem shette an arrow at him and the arrew turned a yene and smote
him that shote the arrow and hurt him sore Thanne were they sore a ferde and
thought what that might mean and went to the bishop and told him all the
cause tha^ the bishop preyde to god to have knowleche what hit was Tha^ in the
mount of gargan michaell apperid to him and seyde hit was goddis will that the
man should be hurt for ye shall know well yt y am kepir of ye place where for
go thou and make a church of yt dene and so the bish^p made a fair church
there. Also michaell a^pered to a nothir bishop and bad him go to an hill top
to the mount of gardell and there as he found a bolle teyde he should make a
church in the worshipp^ of god and semte michaell Thanne were there ij.
ro^chis of stone on eythir side that the work might not up Than semt michaell
appeared to a man that hight baymo and bad him go and put a wey the roche and
dread no thing so this man went thethir and set to his shuldres and bad the
roche go utter in the name of god and seint michaell and so the hills went
utter as much as nedich to the work



we read also in the life of seint gregory how there was a great multitude of
people in rome and they saw arrows of fire come out of the air and slew
much people. Thanne seint Gregory preyde to god to sese that pestilence Than
he saw an a^gell stondyng one a castle wall wypyng his blody sword but that
angel he seyde was seint michaell was sent thethir to punische the people for
syn thus michaell was meruelons in miracles worchyng. Also he was victorious in
fightyng for when the citezenis of septutyne were oppressid with paynemes and
should give he^ battle they preyde often to seint michaell of help Tha^ the
night be for as the battle should be michaell apperid to the bishop and
seyde to him have no dread but go to the battle boldly and he would help him
and so on the morrow when the battle should be the hill of garganus was over
c^uered with a great myste and arrows come out of the myste fleyng of fire
and b^ltis of thoundir and hurt much people of the paynemes in so much that
they slew all that ever might fle And so many were sleyne and tho that were a
life were saved be great miracle of god and were cristoned. Seint johan
euengeliste seythe in his Apocalips how michaell and his angels foughten with
lucifer in heaven that is callid the dragon and his angels and with help of
god* michaell had the better and drove out the dragon and all his fellowship
in to the air between heaven and earth and so they be there yet as thick as
motis in the fonne And for criste come to heaven in a blaste of thoundyr. and
there for yet when they here thoundir they fall down to the er the for fere
and tha^ they go not up a yene till they have do sum harm. for than they
make batis and stryues and man slawter and make great wyndes both in land and
in water and do much harm and yet they would do much more than they do
nere seynt^ michaell for all her sorrows is to se souls engeles in heaven in
the place there they were ynne to fore Also other spirits there were that
s^ode not stead fast toward god but flatering the which seint michaell
drove out heaven all in to an isle of the sea as ye shall here As seinte Brandan
seyled in the se he come to an isle and saw a tree was so great be the high
and broad that it was wou^dir to tell on the which tree satte briddis thicker
than the bows and were as white as snow. tha^ he preyde to god to wete what
they we Tha^ come on of hem and satte on the shippis board and batered with
his wings and made a sown like an organ Than said brandan if thou be come a
messenger speak and tell me what ye ben Thanne he said we were angels that
stood not stead fast in the be leave a^ michaell wa^ and there for we were
dreuyn out when michaell drove out lucifer and his angels But yet we have
every day a remedy to woshippe god Thus was michaell woundrefull in apperyng
marvelous in miracles doing and victorious in fightyng where late us worshipp^
this holy angel that he may be our shield in fightyng a yense our gostely
enemy the fend so that we may have the victory of him now and ever Amen

De festo sa^cti luce.
GOod frendis soche a day ye shall have seint lukys day the evangelist ye shall
understood that criste had iiij. evangelists that is mark matthew luce and
johan these wrote the gospel the gospel is no more to sey but goddis word
these holy euangelistis wrote not only that god spoke but also what y^ he did
and what he suffered for mankind for hit should be know to all mankind fore
ever more to think on goddis word and to do there aftyr These iiij. be likened
to iiij. diverse bestes and so they be portrayed in iiij. parties of the cross
on every side of criste. for mark a lion for matthew a man for luce a calfe and
for johan an egyll But late no man suppose that they were soch bestis but
likened to soch bestis for diverse causes* for be cause that matthew wrote most
of cristus manhood there fore he is likened to a man And luke wrote most of
cristus sacrafice and his death there for he is likened to a calfe or to an ox
fore a calfe that was offered in sacrifice of the old law in tokening that
criste should be offered for sin of the people in sacrifice in the auter of
the cross And mark wrote most of the resurrection vprysing and there for he is
likened to a lion For as bokis sey and tell when a ly on has young welpes
they shall lie as deed three days aftyr they be welpid Than comyth the lion and
sethe his welpes deed a none he makith so the a roryng and a cry y^ the deed
welpes wake there with and quekon and take life So when criste had leyne iij.
days in his tomb Than the fadir spoke to him and bad him rise and so rerid
from death to live Also johan is likened to an egyll for be kind she fleith
highest in to the air and next to the son so johan wrote most of the
godhede and but litill of the manhood these be the causes that they be likened
to iiij. diverse bestio But now ye shall understand that Luke was likened to
a calfe. iij manner of weyes that is in the thought word and deed he offered
his thou ghte to god for there as he was furste besy to get goodis of the
world with his craft for as bo^is tell he was a leche and for couetyse of
good he slew many a man bodily than had he offendid god so grievously that a
none he offered his thought in sacrifice for as bo kys teache god is highely
plesid with thought that is when a man is sorry for his sins in his heart and
thynkith verily to for sake sin and a mende him Also he offered his word to
god in sacrifice for as he was wont to fore to spe^de his speech in many ydyll
words or he come to the apostle aftyr he turned his spech in to profit to
all criste^ people where for he went to our lady and she taught him the
gospel tho that he wrote and fore he was a clean maiden our lady cherischid
him the more And so taught him full goodly how the a^gell come to her in
message and what he seyde and what answer she gafe a yene. and so all things
that she did with her sone and of all her doing till our lord was styed up in
to heaven. and whann luke had learned this persitely than he lokyd what Mark had
wreton and matthew and so to ke athem and there as they wretyn darckly he wrote
openly all things. thus in prechyng and techyng he offered his word to god
Also he offered his deed to god in sacrifice. fore he peyned his body with
diverse penance of fasting and of hard leuing in keeping preyng Also he wrote
all the persecucion that the apostelis suffered of the jews in iherusalem wha^
they had great pursewte and tourme^t for goddis sake and he wrote all the
persecucione of seint steuyn how he was stoned to death Thann went seint luke
to saint poule and sewed him in many mystheuys and dissese ^ he had and in full
great dre de and never departid from him till poule was deed. Thanne went luke
to a country that was callid betanie and there he p^chid the word of god and
was there till he was xl. winter of age. than he dyed full fair full of the
holy ghost for he leuyd in holy virtuous. and aftyr his death god showed for
him many fair miracles and so endid in criste and went in to ever lasting
bliss to the which god bring us all to Amen.

De simone and inda
GOod frendis so che a day ye shall have the feste of Simon and jude and ye
shall fast the euyne and one the morrow come to church and worship god and
these holy apostles. we shall on derstonde that eythir of these has to names
that one was callid Simon elotes and that other judas iacola and judas tha deus
showing be these how the name that a man has in this world dies and passithe
out of mind when he is deed where fore every criste^ man shul de be besy to
take him a name that should be wreton in the book of lyffe y^ should last
ever. And there for these ij. apostles suffered great penance travel
tribulacion and dissese and at the last pain of death fore cristus sake with
hertes meke and clean conscience Simon is as much to sey as obedience that
makith a man meke in heart Judas is as much to sey as confessi on that
clensith a man's conscience of all manner of fynne And thus be fore or they
dyed they gaffe every man ensample how they took her death meke ly for cristus
sake and dye with clean conscience and than they shall be wreton in the book of
lyffe with great worshipp^ in the fra ternite of heaven but they that grochyn in
her hertes of dissese and persecucion and ever playnyng they have need to prey
to god to be helid of that sykenes that they have in her spiritis



We read in the lyffe of the apostell how a king that was callid Abagarus and
was leper and herd how that our lord ihesu criste did many miracles and helid
all that were sike Than he wrote a letter in this wise king A bagarus gretith
ihesus ^a uioure well that prechid in the country of iherusalem and I have
herd of thy miracles that thou doste and so thou heliste all manner of
sikenesse with out any herbis or salues and cureste blind and ^rokid and lame
and that is more merueyle thou reyse deed bodies to live where for I think in
my heart and in my believe that thou art very godd is sone and come down from
heuyn to earth and leuyste here among the people as one of hem where for I
write to the that thou wolte come to me and hele me of my leper that greuith me
full fore. and so I understand that the jews have orderned to do the to death
and y have a litill cite that is good and honest and plenteuous and hit is
sufficiant I now for us both to leave by and there shall we both be in rest
and pese. Than criste wrote a yene and seyde y^ art blessed that be leave ste
on me and haste not seyne me and for thou would that I should come to the I
sey to the I must do that I come fore and than y wolle send sum of my
disciples to the that shall hele the of thy leper Tha^ for this king that
criste might not come to him for great desire that he had to se him he sent to
him a payntour that was a maistre of that craft to peynte cristus visag as he
cowde But when this peyntour come to criste and lokyd on his visage hit shone
so brighte that he might not look there one. Than he made great sorrow and
morning that he was come so far and might not speed of his purpose Than
criste took a clothe of the peyntour and wypid his face there with and than was
the forine of his visage there on and than the peyntour bare hit to the king
Than was the king wou^dre glad and did hit great reverence with all his heart
Than aftir cristus ascension thomas of ynde be the sent of the apostles was
sent to this king Ab^garus and wha^ he saw thomas he saw soche a shynyng in
his face that he went hit had be criste Than said thomas to the kyn^ (...) in
criste and thou shalt ^e hole and he feyde I be leave holy in him and feign I
would be wroke one ^^^ that have done him ^o ^^ the and a none he was hole Than
judas went ^^^^ mon and went both (...) dir in to perse to preche and there

feyth. and so the christian people encresed strongely. So the king with all his
meyne were cristoned and with drew her offeringes from the mawmentes that was
the bishops leuyng where fore they were so wroth that they gaderid hem to
gedir and took these apostles and lad hem in to her temples to do sacrifice to
h^er mawmentes or else they should be deed Tha^ come an angel and askid if
they would have her enemies deed or no and they seyde they desired to have her
enemies turned to the feyth and the angel askid if they would suffer
martyrdom fore cristus sake and they said they would suffer death Than they
co^maundid and turned to the mawmentes in the temple and commanded the fendes
that were in hem to come out and to pluck the images all to pecis and so they

come a thou^ dir and a lyghtenyng and cleue the temple in iij. parties down to
the ground. and than these bishoppis suddenly slew these apostlis. tha^ the

worshipp^ of god and these holy apostles. Amen.

De festo omnium sanctorum.
GOod frendis soche a day ye shall h^aue all halowyn day and ye shall fast the
even and on the morrow come to ch^irch and worship god and our lady and all
halowyn. Friends ye shall understand that this feste was ordained fore iij
special causes and that be these Furste fore the temple h^alowyng for omission
fullfillyng and also fore negligent leuyng Furste for the temple halowyng for
when the romans were lords of all the world they made a temple in rome as a
doffe house and named hit panteon and set in the myddis of the temple an image
that was the chief mawment of rome and of every land in the world an other
image all a boute the walls and the name of the lord that the jmage was of
wreton under the fete of the jmage and all was made so by nigromancie if that
any lord turned from the emperor a no^ the jmage of the land would tourn
his back to the jmage of rome and his face to the wall So wha^ the bishopp^
come to the temple and found any image turned a none they would to the
Emperor and tell him. Than would they ordeyn an oste of people and send in to
the land and set hem at rest and pese And so this temple endured thus un
to the time that (...) Bonif^ce the iiij. come Thanne he went to the emperor
that was callid foca and preyde him that he would give him that temple that he
might put out the multitude of mawme^tis and to halow hit in the worship
of god and our lady and all balowyn And so he gaffe the (...) the temple Than
come there an other (...) that was callid Gregory and co^maundid all holy
ch^urche to halowe the feste like as it was be gone Also this feste was ordained
by the same (...) to fullfille our omissionis For many seyntes days in the
year we leuyn un served fo^^ there be so many that we may not serve each by he^
self For as jerome seyth that there be for each day in the year x. M. marteres
out take the first day of Ianiuere. where fore holy church ordained that this
day we should fullfille thatswe have left be hind all the year And thus ^ery
seintis euyne has his worship of us if we keep well yt day in worshipp^ to
god and our lady and all halowyn Also this feste is ordained ^o be hallowed to
cleanse us of our negligence and vnco^nyng and also by worldely occupacions
doing we be full recheles in keeping our holidays. and there for the holy
feste is ordained fore we should make a mendis as moch^ as we may of that we
have trespasid in other festis and there for understand ye that they be in
great parell that brekithe this feste or any other in worldely occupaciones
worchyng or in any synn doing in byyng or in sellyng or in any other fall hode
contryuyng. Also ye shall understand that this day our preyoures shall be
sonner herd tha^ any other day. fore this day all the seintes in heaven come to
gedir to prey to god fore us. and there fore ye may know well that all coming
to gedir shall be sonner herd than one or to be hem self. The seintes that be
in heuene were sum time as we be now both in flesche and in blood body and
bone and were our elder faderis and they be full glad and make much joy
whann they may get any preyoures or al^es dedis of us with the which they may
p^sente god and our lady preyng fore us. and to show you be ensample h^ow all
seintes come to gedir as this day ye shall here



we find wreton in legenda aurta that in the same year this fe^te was ordained
to be hallowed there was a keeper of seinte peter's ch^irche in rome that this day
aftir matenes at midnyght wha^ all people were go from matenes fore great
devotion that he had he went to every auter in the chirch and seyde h^is
deuocions and when he had gone all a boute than went he to the hye anter and
there fill a sleep and his spirit was raueschid and saw the fadir of heaven
sittyng in his mageste and a great multitude of angeles a boute him And than
come a fair queen with a crown one her head richely a rayde and a great
company of virgins and maidens sewyng her Thann the king a rose a yene her and
to set a cheyre of gold and set her there yun. tha^ come one clothid in
camel skyunes and h^im sewed a great company of aged men Than come a nothir
like a bishop and aftir him many other bishops And than come a great
multitude as it had be knights and aftir hem much other people and all they
come be for the king and knelid down before the king and did him worship Than
the bishopp began to sey matenes Than spoke this in to the angel that lad him
and askid him what all this people was in that a ray than seyde the angel the
king is god him self. and the queen is our lady and he that was clothid in
camel skynnes was ioha^ baptiste and other patriarchs and prophets with him
The bishop was seint petir and other apostles and confessoures with him. The
knygh^tis was seint gorge with other marterers comyners that were good true
leuers and servants to god here upon earth and they come all to thank god
for the great worship that they had here in earth and preyde be sely to god
that bithe^ in earth that he should have mercy on hem This is the cause that
this feste was furste found and there fore late us come to church and
worship god and all halowyn y^ they may prey for us that we may at once last
end ^^ of ^ nombre that shall worship god that book spe^^th of and seyth thus
Diditurbam magnam quam nemo dinume rare poterit for they be so many that no mau
can nombre hem and all they prey for us euyr more that we may come to that
bliss that they be in Amen.

In die auimaru^.
GOod frendis soche a day ye shall have all soule^ day the day of the souls in
purgatory there a byding the mercy of god and have much need of help and right
as holy chirch worshippid all semtes to be holpyn be the preyoures of hem right
so holy church ordeymth this day to singe and to read and to do alms deeds
having full be leave to relese hem that been in purgatory of her peynes where for
god will that all christian people to her power this d^y releue hem for the ^^^^^
preyour or alms deed that is done gretely releuythe hem. ye shall understand
that there be iiij. thynhis that gretely he lpithe souls that been in purgatory
and be these. Fideliu^ amicoru^ oracio elco^ sinaru^ largicio salutari^ boltia
nimia racio. ieiuniorum obseruacio that is preyoures of fre^des de uoutly seyde
and alms deed doing and masses singing and abstmaunce in fasting preyoures
helpith much a soul For like as a lord has a man in prison or in any
distress and at the preyoure of him that he louith he relesith in party or
all And that is showed be ensample



we find in legenda aurea that there was a man that had his house by a church
yerde side and his door openid to the church and be vsid be custume as often as
he come or went to sey every time De^rofundis fore all christian souls. Tha^
hit happid so on a time that he was pursewed with enemies as he went
homewardes But when he come in to the church yerde he knelid down and thought
to sey Deprofundis and these enemies come aftyr. A noue the deed bodies resyn
every chone with soche instruments as they wroughten with in her lyfes and a
none they dreue a wey his enemies but when they saw that they cryde god mercy
and this man. And ever aftir preyde and deed alms deed for hem that were in
pain Thus I may well prove that devout preyoures helpithe many a soul that been in purgatory. Also alms deed helpithe many souls Sicnt a^na extingnit
ig^e^ ita elemosina extingn^t paccatu^ Right as watyr quenchith fire so alms
deed que^chith the fuyre that brenuyth hem that bethe in purgatory if they be
in good lyffe and persite charity y^ down hit And if alms deed be done for
hem that be in joy and have no need there to hit is put in to the tresoure of
holy church and as goddis will is hit is delte and releuith hem that has
most uede there to and so god assynith hit to hem that have most need and
than the souls that bethe holpyn there with thank the soul that hit is done
for Thus ye may know well that alms deed helpith gretely souls that hit is
done fore and be in purgatory fore often holy men have herd fendes cry and
make great sorrow for with alms dedis souls were take from he^



we read in old time good people would on all halowyn day b^^^ beede and dele

^ado in regnum dei And I am p^rged and shall go to the kingdom of hepe^ And a

For right as mete and dryn^^e comfortid a man when he is febull so the

ie wreton in legend a aurea how a bishop suspendid a priest, for he could sey

Also we find that fiseheris set her news in he rueste to fische and they

De festo sa^cti martini.
GOod frendis soche a day ye shall have seynte martens day whann marten was but
iij. year of age he cut his mantell in to pieces as he rode among other
knyghtis and was not yet cristoned and gafe half his mantell to a poor man for
god dis sake^ that askid alms than the night aftyr god had the sameclothe and
said to his angel, Marten that is not cristoned has clothid me in this
clothe and marten herd this word out of heaven and a non he was cristoued and
thann a none he left this worlds occupacion and yafe him all to holiness So
as he rode on a time be the ^ey the fend come in likeness of a man and met
with him and askid him whethir he would and he seyde thethir as god woll thanne
seyde the feude y woll be thyn enemy in all that y can Then seyde marten god is
my help and there fore y dread me not thann merten wexed holy that he resyd
deed bodies to lyffe and so for his great holiness he was chosyn bishopp^ of
turon So ou a time as me^ were in great parell and like to be spilte one of hem
knew the holiness of marten and seyde marten help and a no^ they were holpyn.
Also he rode on a time in his visitacion a hounde at an hare under his horse
fete than had he pite on this besc* and bad the hounds stand still and late
the best go and a none the hounds stood as stille as they had be put in to
the earth. An other he saw an addir swimming in a water and he seyde to the
addir In usmine do mini iubeo te reddi re In the name of god I command the to
go a yene there thou come fro and a none she turned a yen Thann marten sighed
woundre sore and seyde I am sorry that serpents herith me and men woll not here
me An other time he come by the yate of a cite that highte padyse and there he
kyssed an horrible mesell a none he was hole with the same kiss Also he was so
paciente that many times his own clerkissmote him and yet he suff^red it
patiently and was not wroth So on a time as he rode by the wey in his
visitacion him self for that was his manner he had a row mautell of black and
come a carte by the wey with carriage and the bestes in the carte saw the black
ma^cell wau^ring with the wind and flewe a wey and all to barsce her gere
Thann the carters with her whippes all to beat marten and gafe him many sore
strokes and all he suffered mekely and said nothing Than would they have gone
her wey but they might not stere from the place till they knew that hit was
merten and thanne they cryde him mercy-and than a non he for gafe he and the
bestis passid fair forth and all the harneyse was save y now. Also on a time
as marten satte in his selle the fend come to him like a king with shynyng
crown and seyde y am common from heuyne to speak with the believe on me cristua
ego sum for y am criste and martyne lokis on him and seyde my lord ihesu criste
wolle not come in soche a ray and thou be criste show me thy wou^d is and a
none the fend went his wey and left an horrible stenche be hind him

yet an other time he come to mertyu and repreuede him that he took p^ple to
him that had sinned and were shreuyn and turned a yen to her syn that they had
done to fore and seyde though thou take he^ to thy grace god woll not Tha^
said mertyn wreche and thou wolte leave thy pursuit of criste^ people and ask
mercy with a meke heart I ^^nste to god he is so merciful y^ he wolle gefe
mercy. and when mertyn should pass out of this world and lay in his death bed
the fend come and satte by him disputyng with him if he might have caught him
in any word of mysse believe in his end. marten seyde to him. Goo hense thou
cruel best for thou shalt no thing find ^ mysse with me but god shall
resceyue me and thann he made to ley him in asks and here and he seyde the
vij. psalms and latinie and gaffe up the ghost and was heried in his own
church with much honor and worship in turon Than liiij* winter aftir there
come a bishop and translatid him. and when he had made all thing ready he leyde
hand one marte^s body to have borne hit forth but he might not Than thought
the bishop it is not martens will to be remenyd and left of Than come a fair
old man and bad him go to a yene and he would help him and thann they bare
the body in to the tomb with out lettyng and so whann the service was done
this old man vanisched a wey and there by they know well that hit was seint
marte^ And than god shewde many fair miracles fore him



Hit happid on a time that there was ij. beggeris that one was halte and might
not go and that other was ^^nde and might not se And so to make the people to
have the more compassione of hem the blind bare the lame and the lame taught
the blind where he should go and thus they gate much good and had esy live But
they were ever a ferde to mete with the shrine of seint marten left he would
have helid hem of her sikenesse And so on a time at a stretis end at a
tourning suddenly at a corner they met with the shrine of seint marte^ and a
none they were both hole And the blind might se and the lame might go And
than they cride to seint marten and seid marten we thank the fore the good
that we have fore thy sake here to fore. we thank the not for our hele. For
now we must goo labure and travel and so get our leuyng for the people well
give us no more alms and here to fore we leuyd full esyly with litill
travel and ferde well Alas alas that we come here this day fore now our
myrthe and well rare is gone Thus this holy man did many miracles where for I
may see that he may do with god there for let us prey to him that he may prey
to god for us Amen.

^e sancta katherina uirgine
GOod frendis soche a day ye shall have seint katherines day the holy martyr
she was a kings daughter and come of g^^t ^^e the But she set all her, mind
to god and set, naught be the pride and richesse of the world for hit is but
a vanite but she set her heart all only on ihesu So when she h^d be at stole
and learned a while a none she would dispute with any clerk y^ would come for
she was enspired with the holy ghost But when she herd on a time that
marencius was come to the cite of Alisaundre with so much people and so rially
that the cite dommed of hem For he come to make a solemn sacrifice to his
goddis that were of gold and silver in sikenesse of bollis and calves and
other bestis. Than seint katheryne saw that and blessid^ her and went in to
the temple and rebukyd the Emperor bodily and seyde that he did foul a mysse
fore to do that worship to fendes and leave the worship of god in heaven that
made all thing of naught and sent man lyffe wit and hele and preued by great
reason how criste was both god and man and how he bought all ma^kinde with his
passion one the cross with his death. and taught how every man should honor
god and lene false mawmentes. Tha^ was the emperor wroth and ^ad take her
toward till he might be at leysoure. So in the mean time he sent aftyr the
grettiste maistres and the wyseste clerkys that were in any country far a
bonte him And when they were come he bad hem go dispute with katherine and over
come her and they should have right well for her labor. Than were they wroth
to c^ome so far to dispute with a woe man and seyde the least scoler in the
scole had be y now to over come her. But when katherine had disputid with hem
with help of the holy ghost she conuertid hem every chone to the feyth of
our lord ihesu criste in so much that they were ready to suffer death fore
cristus sake* Than a none maxencius co^maundid to make a great fuyre and ^renne
hem in the fuyre. But by the help of the holy ghost the fuyre bre^ de uo
parties of he bodye^s ne the least cloth of hem and yet lay fair deed as they
had be a sleep

Than the Emperor made do ka herine nakid and beat her with scorgi^ ^ she was
all blood and full of wounds and than he put her in to prison vij. days
with out mete and drink Thanne had the queen a great lust to speak with
katherine and took a knyghre with her that highte porphirius and went to
katherine and than they saw an a^gell set a crown of shynyng gold on the
queen's he de and an other on porphirius he de and bad hem be stedefast for with
in three days they should come to heaven be suffering of martyrdom Thanne sent
the Emperor aftir katherine and went to have found her nyghe deed but all
that time god sent her mete from heaven and whann the emperor saw her a lyffe
he was wode for word and made her to be set between ij* whelis and turned
on vpwardes and anothir downewardes full of ^oll^s and sword points for all
to raze katherine. Than come an a^gell as ^it had be a wind and all to brake
hem and slew iiij M. of the tyrants Tha^ saw the queen that miracle and come
be fore the king her housbond and re^ukyd him yt he saw the might of god so
openly and would not be leave there o^n Than bad the king led forth the queen
and cut of her pappes from the body with hokys and tha^ to smite of her head
tha^ for porphirius beried her lxxx. of her knyghtis were martered with her
they smote of porphirius head Than spoke the emperor to katherine and seyde
that he would wedde her and she would fro criste and believe in his goddis and
she seyde she set naught by him nor by his goddis and when he saw that he
made to smite of her head Than a none in scede of blood come much fair milk.
And than come an angel and bare the soul in to heaven And angelis come and
bare the body in to the air and so in to the mount of synay and there beried
it with worshipp^ and there god wronghte many fair miracles into this day At
the foot of the mount there is an abbey of monks that leuyn in great
abstinaunce and this abbey is strong and high wallid and barred about with
yrou for wild bestis and in that abbey lies seint katherine in a fair tomb
of alabaster for her bones were shedi^ for the more worship and a bouyn in
the church is the bnshe there god stood in when he spoke to moses and wrote
the law in to ij. tables of stone and that busche is also grene and fair as
hit was the same day Also in that abbey is a great merueyle and is this every
monk has a lamp^e with oil brennyng and wha^ he shall dye they shall know be
hisla^ he for as he drawithe to ^^e death so drawith his ^^mpe And when this
^^bot dies his brethere^ shall singe a mass of the holy ghost and bery him so
lemply and when mass is done they shall find a bille writo^ on the auter how
shall be abbote and so they these her abbot Also on seint katherins night all
the briddi^ in the country come the dir and each of he^ bryngith a branche of
olive in her bill into the place and as pilgremes sey the monkis make oil of
the branches to her lamps for all the year and sum to selle



we find and read of a man that served seint katherine and fastid her even
bread and watir and on a time he come in felleship of recheles people and by
comfort of hem he left his fast and ete with hem and so in the night aftyr
he saw a great company of maydene^ coming by him and among hem there was on
passing all other and each of hem had a crown but on had passing a fair
crown and that was sein katherine. So when she come by this man she hid her
face from him and would not look on him. tha^ he askid on of hem what they were
and she seyde we be virginis and the principal that thou s^iste is seint
kather^^ y^ hid her fate for the be cause thou haste left thy devotion from
her even of fasting Than this man repentid him sore that he had done this deed
so and turned a yen to his devotion and fastid and aftyr was an holy man. and
there for sete us worship this holy virgin that she may prey for us Amen.

Narracio.

(...) in the gestis of rome that an a^gell told an holy bishop that hight.
Encres how that charles the king of france was dampened he took a wey holy
chirchis right that good people had yeuen to fore and bad him go and opyn his
tomb and se the sothe. Than the bishop took with him other people and opened
the tomb and there come out a great dragon and fley forth and left tomb
brenne with in as hit had be anouyn mouth and thus bery in holy place is but
litill a veil to hem that be dampened Also there be many that walkyn on nyghtes
when they aren beried in holy place but that is not long of the feude but of
grace of god to get hem help. and some be gilty and hane no rest
